Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Voluntary Prayer on a Mount: Basic Ruling and Conditions
Explains the permissibility, conditions, and intra-Hanafi dispute of nafl on a riding animal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing voluntary prayer on a mount outside the city, list its conditions, and explain the evidence from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
Voluntary prayer on a mount outside the city is permitted with gestures, based on prophetic practice and the concession of travel.

Imagine you are traveling by camel or horse and wish to pray an extra prayer, but stopping and dismounting would delay your journey. Islamic law provides a concession: you may pray while riding, using gestures instead of full bowing and prostration. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling, its conditions, and the prophetic evidence that establishes this facility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being discussed (voluntary prayer on a mount) and the hukm level: it is permissible, indeed recommended (mandub), as a concession for travelers and those outside the built-up area.
The ruling is not obligatory but a recommended facility.
2
Understand the conditions for validity
List the conditions: being outside the city (outside the built-up area), riding an animal, and performing the prayer with gestures (īmāʾ) towards whatever direction the animal faces. The rider need not be able to stop the animal.
The condition of being outside the city is key; inside the city the ruling differs.
3
Examine the method of prayer
The prayer is performed by making gestures: a slight bow for rukuʿ and a deeper bow for sujūd. Recitation is done normally. The rider may begin the prayer facing any direction.
The gestures replace the physical movements of bowing and prostrating.
4
Locate the evidence (dalīl)
Two main hadiths are cited: Ibn ʿUmar’s report of the Prophet praying on his mount heading to Khaybar, and Jābir’s report of the Prophet gesturing during voluntary prayers on his mount. These are narrated by Muslim and Ibn Ḥibbān respectively.
The hadiths are of ahad (singular) transmission, thus zannī al-thubūt.
5
Note the scope and exceptions
This concession applies to all voluntary prayers, even the emphasized sunan (rawātib), though for the Fajr sunnah, it is preferable to dismount. It does not apply to obligatory prayers except in dire necessity.
The ruling is a rukhṣah (concession) linked to the absence of hardship in dismounting for fard prayers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويتنفل راكباً خارج المصر، مومياً إلى أي جهة توجهت دابته. شيئاً، ثم يركع ليكون موافقاً للسنة، ولو لم يقرأ ولكنه استوى قائماً وركع أجزأه، وإن لم يستو قائماً وركع لا يجزؤه، لأنه لا يكون ركوعاً قائماً، ولا ركوعاً قاعداً. انتهى. وموافقته للسنة ذكرناها فيما تقدم، وفي «مجمع الروايات» أنَّه عليه الصلاة والسلام كان يفتتح التطوع قائماً ثم يقعد، فإذا بقي من قراءته مقدار عشرين آية أو ثلاثين آية، قام فقرأ ثم ركع ثم سجد. ويتنفل أي: جاز له التنفل، بل ندب له راكباً خارج المصر أي: خارج العمران ليشمل خارج القرية، وخارج محل إقامته الذي إذا جاوزه يصير مسافراً، كالأخبية. وسواء كان مسافراً أو مقيماً، خرج لحاجة في بعض النواحي على الأصح، فالمراد بخارج المصر: الموضع الذي يجوز للمسافر أن يقصر فيه الصلاة، وهو على الأصح، وقيل: إذا خرج قدر فرسخين أو أكثر جاز له، وإلا فلا، وقيل: إذا خرج قدر الميل يجوز، وعن أبي يوسف أنها تجوز في المصر أيضاً. حكي عن أبي يوسف: أنه لما سمع من أبي حنيفة عدم الجواز في المصر قال: حدثني فلان - وسماه - عن سالم عن ابن عمر أنَّه عليه الصلاة والسلام ركب الحمار في المدينة يعود سعد بن عبادة، وكان يصلي وهو راكب، فلم يرفع أبو حنيفة رحمه الله رأسه، قيل: إنما لم يرفع رجوعاً منه إلى الحديث، وقيل: إنما لم يرفع لأن هذا حديث شاذ فيما تعم به البلوى والشاذ في مثله لا يكون حجة، فأبو يوسف أخذ بالحديث، ومحمد كذلك، ولكنه كرهه في رواية مخافة الغلط بكثرة اللغط في المصر، ونفاه في أخرى للحديث الذي رواه أبو يوسف، وروي أيضاً عن أبي يوسف وأبي حنيفة أنها لا تجوز على الدابة إلا للمسافر خاصة للضرورة، ولا ضرورة في الحضر، فيصلي عليها مومياً إلى أي جهة توجهت به دابته لقول ابن عمر: رأيت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يصلي على راحلته وهو متوجه إلى خيبر رواه مسلم وغيره. ولقول جابر: رأيت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يصلي النوافل على راحلته في كل وجه يومي إيماء ولكنَّه يخفض السجدتين من الركعتين رواه ابن حبان في صحيحه، ولأن في إلزامه النزول والتوجه انقطاعاً عن النافلة أو القافلة، بخلاف الفرائض لاختصاصها بأوقاتها، فلا يشق عليه النزول للأداء والرفقاء متظافرون معه على ذلك، فلا يجوز إلا من عذر، كما إذا لم يقفواله وخاف اللصوص أو السبع، جاز له أن يصليها راكباً، ويجوز أن يفتتح الصلاة حيثما توجهت به الدابة، كما جازت له الصلاة حيثما توجهت به الدابة لمكان الحاجة، ولا يشترط عجزه عن إيقافها، وهو ظاهر الرواية، وإذا حرك رجله أو ضرب دابته فلا بأس به إذا لم يصنع شيئاً كثيراً، من «الفتح»، و«البرهان»، و«المعراج»، و«التبيين»، و«الحاشية» والإتقاني. وبنى بنزوله على ما صلى من التطوع إذا لم يحصل منه عمل كثير، كما إذا ثنى رجله فانحدر من الجانب الآخر فيتمها على الأرض؛ لأن إحرام الراكب انعقد مجوزاً الركوع والسجود بواسطة النزول، فكان له أن يأتي بالإيماء راكباً رخصة، أو ينزل بعد الإحرام راكباً، فيأتي بالركوع والسجود عزيمة، وبهذا يفرق بين بنائه وعدم بناء المريض إذا قدر على الركوع والسجود، وكان مومياً؛ لأن إحرام المريض لم يتناولهما؛ لعدم قدرته عليهما، فصار كإحرام النازل الذي افتتح الصلاة على الأرض، فلا يجوز بناء ما لم يتناوله إحرامه على ما تناوله، فلذا لا يجوز له البناء بعد ركوبه على ما صلاه نازلاً، في ظاهر الرواية عنهم، لأن افتتاحه على الأرض استلزم جميع الشروط وفي الركوب يفوت شرط الاستقبال واتحاد المكان وطهارته، وما جاز ذلك على الدابة على خلاف القياس ابتداء إلا لضرورة السير. وجاز الإيماء على الدابة لو كان بالنوافل الراتبة المؤكدة وغيرها؛ لأنها نوافل، فهي في حكمها حتى سنة الفجر، وروي عن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى أنه ينزل الراكب لسنة الفجر، لأنها أكد من غيرها. قال ابن شجاع: يجوز أن يكون هذا لبيان الأولى يعني: أن الأولى أن ينزل لركعتي الفجر، كذا في «العناية»، وقدمنا أن هذا على رواية وجوبها. وجاز للمتطوع الاتكاء على شيء كعصا وحائط وخادم إن تعب؛ لأنه عذر، وإن شاء قعد، وذلك بلا كراهة.
He may perform voluntary prayer on a mount outside the city, gesturing towards whatever direction his animal faces. Something, then he bows to be in accordance with the Sunnah. If he did not recite but stood upright and bowed, it suffices him. If he did not stand upright and bowed, it does not suffice him because it is neither bowing while standing nor bowing while sitting. End. And its accordance with the Sunnah we mentioned previously. In 'Majmaʿ al-Riwāyāt' that he (peace be upon him) used to begin supererogatory prayer standing, then sit, and when there remained from his recitation about twenty or thirty verses, he would stand and recite, then bow, then prostrate. He may perform voluntary prayer—i.e., it is permissible for him to perform supererogatory prayer, nay recommended—riding outside the city, i.e., outside built-up areas to include outside the village and outside his place of residence which when he passes it he becomes a traveler, like tents. Whether he is a traveler or a resident, he went out for a need in some areas according to the most correct view. The meaning of 'outside the city' is the place where it is permissible for a traveler to shorten the prayer, and that is the most correct view. It is said: if he goes out about two farsakhs or more, it is permissible, otherwise not. It is said: if he goes out about a mile, it is permissible. And from Abu Yusuf that it is permissible also in the city. It is narrated about Abu Yusuf that when he heard from Abu Hanifa the non-permissibility in the city, he said: So-and-so narrated to me—and he named him—from Salim from Ibn ʿUmar that he (peace be upon him) rode a donkey in Medina to visit Saʿd ibn ʿUbāda, and he was praying while riding. Abu Hanifa did not raise his head. It is said that he did not raise it out of deference to the hadith, and it is said that he did not raise it because this hadith is anomalous (shādh) regarding a matter of general necessity, and the anomalous in such a case is not a proof. So Abu Yusuf took the hadith, and Muhammad likewise, but he disliked it in one narration fearing error due to much clamor in the city, and he negated it in another due to the hadith that Abu Yusuf narrated. It is also narrated from Abu Yusuf and Abu Hanifa that it is not permissible on an animal except for a traveler specifically due to necessity, and there is no necessity in settled areas, so he prays on it gesturing towards whatever direction his animal faces, due to the saying of Ibn ʿUmar: I saw the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) praying on his mount while heading to Khaybar—narrated by Muslim and others. And due to the saying of Jabir: I saw the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) praying voluntary prayers on his mount in every direction, gesturing, but he lowers the two prostrations more than the two rakʿahs—narrated by Ibn Ḥibbān in his Ṣaḥīḥ. And because obliging him to dismount and face the qibla would cause interruption of the voluntary prayer or the caravan, unlike obligatory prayers because they are specific to their times, so dismounting to perform them is not difficult for him, and his companions support him in that. So it is not permissible except due to an excuse, such as if they did not stop for him and he feared thieves or a wild beast; then it is permissible for him to pray riding. And it is permissible for him to begin the prayer wherever his animal faces, just as it is permissible for him to pray wherever his animal faces due to necessity. And his inability to stop it is not a condition, and that is Ẓāhir al-Riwāya. And if he moves his foot or strikes his animal, there is no harm if he does not do much action—from 'al-Fatḥ', 'al-Burhān', 'al-Miʿrāj', 'al-Tabyīn', 'al-Ḥāshiya' and 'al-Itqānī'. And he builds upon his descent on what he prayed of supererogatory prayer if he did not do much action, like when he bends his leg and descends from the other side and completes it on the ground. Because the iḥrām of the rider is contracted permitting bowing and prostration by means of descending, so he may either perform gesturing while riding as a concession, or descend after iḥrām while riding and perform bowing and prostration as a determined duty. And by this is distinguished between his building and the lack of building for the sick person if he is able to bow and prostrate but was gesturing. Because the iḥrām of the sick person did not encompass them due to his inability, so it becomes like the iḥrām of one who descended and began the prayer on the ground, so it is not permissible for him to build what his iḥrām did not encompass upon what it encompassed. Therefore, it is not permissible for him to build after mounting on what he prayed while descending, according to Ẓāhir al-Riwāya from them. Because his beginning on the ground required all conditions, and in riding the condition of facing the qibla, unity of place and purity are lost, and that was permissible on the animal contrary to analogy initially except due to the necessity of travel. And gesturing on the animal is permissible even if it is for the emphasized supererogatory prayers and others, because they are voluntary prayers, so they are in their ruling, even the Sunnah of Fajr. And it is narrated from Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) that the rider should dismount for the Sunnah of Fajr because it is more emphasized than others. Ibn Shujāʿ said: This may be to indicate the preferable, meaning that it is preferable to dismount for the two rakʿahs of Fajr—this is in 'al-ʿInāya', and we have previously stated that this is according to the narration of its obligation. And it is permissible for the one performing voluntary prayer to lean on something—like a staff, a wall, or a servant—if he is tired, because it is an excuse. And if he wishes, he may sit, and that is without dislike.
Source pages p. 422

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah is an expansion (sharh) on the rulings of voluntary prayer (nafl) while riding an animal. The author begins by stating the basic ruling: it is permissible, even recommended, to perform voluntary prayer on a mount outside the built-up area of a town or city, gesturing (īmāʾ) towards whatever direction the animal faces. The term 'outside the city' is defined as the point where traveling begins and where shortening of prayer is allowed, though there are differing opinions on the exact distance. A key intra-Hanafi dispute arises regarding whether such prayer is also permissible inside the city. Abu Hanifa held it is not, because there is no necessity; Abu Yusuf argued it is, citing a hadith where the Prophet prayed on a donkey in Medina. The text explains that Abu Hanifa did not rebut the hadith, either out of deference or because he deemed it anomalous (shādh). Imam Muhammad agreed with Abu Yusuf in principle but disliked it in practice due to potential distractions. The passage then provides the evidence for gesturing (īmāʾ) from the hadith of Ibn Umar and Jabir, and explains the wisdom behind the concession: to avoid interrupting the prayer or the journey. It also clarifies that this applies even to emphasized regular supererogatory prayers (rawātib), though for the Fajr sunnah, Abu Hanifa reportedly considered it preferable to dismount. The text then addresses the issue of building upon (bināʾ) the prayer when one descends from the mount: if the rider dismounts without doing much extraneous action, he may complete his prayer on the ground, because his iḥrām encompassed the possibility of performing bowing and prostration via descent. This contrasts with a sick person who gestures—his iḥrām did not encompass actual bowing, so if he later becomes able, he cannot build. Finally, the passage permits leaning on something during voluntary prayer if one is tired, without dislike.

Key Terms
إيماء (īmāʾ): Gesturing with the head or body instead of full bowing and prostration; used in prayer on a mount or by a sick person.
بناء (bināʾ): Building upon a prayer already started; here it means continuing the same prayer after dismounting without interruption.
شاذ (shādh): An anomalous hadith; one narrated by a reliable person but conflicting with a stronger chain or established practice; not considered a proof in widespread matters.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah, what is the condition regarding the rider's ability to stop the animal?
A) The rider must be unable to stop the animal.
B) The rider must be able to stop the animal but chooses not to.
C) The ability to stop the animal is irrelevant; the concession applies regardless.
D) The rider must stop the animal before beginning the prayer.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits voluntary prayer on a mount outside the city with gestures, based on prophetic practice, and does not require the rider to be unable to stop the animal.

Salah — Prayer
advanced
10 min
The Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Praying on a Mount Inside the City
Explains the permissibility, conditions, and intra-Hanafi dispute of nafl on a riding animal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad regarding voluntary prayer on a mount inside the city, explain their evidence, and identify the muftā bihi position.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa disallows nafl on a mount inside the city; Abu Yusuf allows it based on a hadith; the muftā bihi follows Abu Hanifa.

One of the most interesting intra-Hanafi disputes concerns whether the concession of praying on a mount extends to inside the city. Abu Hanifa held that it does not, while his two principal students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, disagreed. This lesson dissects their arguments, the hadith at the center of the dispute, and how later Hanafis resolved the ikhtilāf.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on praying on a mount inside the city
Abu Hanifa's view: It is NOT permissible to perform voluntary prayer on a mount inside the city (al-miṣr). The concession is only for those outside the built-up area due to necessity.
This is the position preferred by the later school (muftā bihi).
2
Identify the opposing view (Sāḥibayn)
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani held that it IS permissible inside the city, though Muhammad disliked it in one narration due to potential distraction.
Their evidence is a specific hadith about the Prophet praying on a donkey in Medina.
3
Analyze the evidence for each position
Abu Yusuf cited the hadith of Ibn ʿUmar: the Prophet rode a donkey in Medina to visit Saʿd ibn ʿUbāda and prayed while riding. Abu Hanifa deemed this hadith as shādh (anomalous) because the matter is widespread (ʿumūm al-balwā) and such a hadith cannot override the general practice.
Abu Hanifa did not reject the hadith outright but considered it unsuitable for establishing a general rule.
4
Understand the concept of shādh in Hanafi usul
A hadith that is shādh (anomalous) in a matter of common occurrence is not a proof because if the ruling were correct, it would have been transmitted widely. This is a key usul principle used by Abu Hanifa.
This distinguishes the Hanafi approach from the Shafi'i, who accept the hadith as general.
5
Determine the muftā bihi and its practical consequence
The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa: inside the city, one must dismount to pray nafl. The practical difference (thamarah) is that in the city, a Hanafi cannot avail the concession.
This is the safer view and is followed in fatwa.

و«التبيين»، و«الحاشية» والإتقاني. وبنى بنزوله على ما صلى من التطوع إذا لم يحصل منه عمل كثير، كما إذا ثنى رجله فانحدر من الجانب الآخر فيتمها على الأرض؛ لأن إحرام الراكب انعقد مجوزاً الركوع والسجود بواسطة النزول، فكان له أن يأتي بالإيماء راكباً رخصة، أو ينزل بعد الإحرام راكباً، فيأتي بالركوع والسجود عزيمة، وبهذا يفرق بين بنائه وعدم بناء المريض إذا قدر على الركوع والسجود، وكان مومياً؛ لأن إحرام المريض لم يتناولهما؛ لعدم قدرته عليهما، فصار كإحرام النازل الذي افتتح الصلاة على الأرض، فلا يجوز بناء ما لم يتناوله إحرامه على ما تناوله، فلذا لا يجوز له البناء بعد ركوبه على ما صلاه نازلاً، في ظاهر الرواية عنهم، لأن افتتاحه على الأرض استلزم جميع الشروط وفي الركوب يفوت شرط الاستقبال واتحاد المكان وطهارته، وما جاز ذلك على الدابة على خلاف القياس ابتداء إلا لضرورة السير. وجاز الإيماء على الدابة لو كان بالنوافل الراتبة المؤكدة وغيرها؛ لأنها نوافل، فهي في حكمها حتى سنة الفجر، وروي عن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى أنه ينزل الراكب لسنة الفجر، لأنها أكد من غيرها. قال ابن شجاع: يجوز أن يكون هذا لبيان الأولى يعني: أن الأولى أن ينزل لركعتي الفجر، كذا في «العناية»، وقدمنا أن هذا على رواية وجوبها. وجاز للمتطوع الاتكاء على شيء كعصا وحائط وخادم إن تعب؛ لأنه عذر، وإن شاء قعد، وذلك بلا كراهة.
He may perform voluntary prayer on a mount outside the city, gesturing towards whatever direction his animal faces. Something, then he bows to be in accordance with the Sunnah. If he did not recite but stood upright and bowed, it suffices him. If he did not stand upright and bowed, it does not suffice him because it is neither bowing while standing nor bowing while sitting. End. And its accordance with the Sunnah we mentioned previously. In 'Majmaʿ al-Riwāyāt' that he (peace be upon him) used to begin supererogatory prayer standing, then sit, and when there remained from his recitation about twenty or thirty verses, he would stand and recite, then bow, then prostrate. He may perform voluntary prayer—i.e., it is permissible for him to perform supererogatory prayer, nay recommended—riding outside the city, i.e., outside built-up areas to include outside the village and outside his place of residence which when he passes it he becomes a traveler, like tents. Whether he is a traveler or a resident, he went out for a need in some areas according to the most correct view. The meaning of 'outside the city' is the place where it is permissible for a traveler to shorten the prayer, and that is the most correct view. It is said: if he goes out about two farsakhs or more, it is permissible, otherwise not. It is said: if he goes out about a mile, it is permissible. And from Abu Yusuf that it is permissible also in the city. It is narrated about Abu Yusuf that when he heard from Abu Hanifa the non-permissibility in the city, he said: So-and-so narrated to me—and he named him—from Salim from Ibn ʿUmar that he (peace be upon him) rode a donkey in Medina to visit Saʿd ibn ʿUbāda, and he was praying while riding. Abu Hanifa did not raise his head. It is said that he did not raise it out of deference to the hadith, and it is said that he did not raise it because this hadith is anomalous (shādh) regarding a matter of general necessity, and the anomalous in such a case is not a proof. So Abu Yusuf took the hadith, and Muhammad likewise, but he disliked it in one narration fearing error due to much clamor in the city, and he negated it in another due to the hadith that Abu Yusuf narrated. It is also narrated from Abu Yusuf and Abu Hanifa that it is not permissible on an animal except for a traveler specifically due to necessity, and there is no necessity in settled areas, so he prays on it gesturing towards whatever direction his animal faces, due to the saying of Ibn ʿUmar: I saw the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) praying on his mount while heading to Khaybar—narrated by Muslim and others. And due to the saying of Jabir: I saw the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) praying voluntary prayers on his mount in every direction, gesturing, but he lowers the two prostrations more than the two rakʿahs—narrated by Ibn Ḥibbān in his Ṣaḥīḥ. And because obliging him to dismount and face the qibla would cause interruption of the voluntary prayer or the caravan, unlike obligatory prayers because they are specific to their times, so dismounting to perform them is not difficult for him, and his companions support him in that. So it is not permissible except due to an excuse, such as if they did not stop for him and he feared thieves or a wild beast; then it is permissible for him to pray riding. And it is permissible for him to begin the prayer wherever his animal faces, just as it is permissible for him to pray wherever his animal faces due to necessity. And his inability to stop it is not a condition, and that is Ẓāhir al-Riwāya. And if he moves his foot or strikes his animal, there is no harm if he does not do much action—from 'al-Fatḥ', 'al-Burhān', 'al-Miʿrāj', 'al-Tabyīn', 'al-Ḥāshiya' and 'al-Itqānī'. And he builds upon his descent on what he prayed of supererogatory prayer if he did not do much action, like when he bends his leg and descends from the other side and completes it on the ground. Because the iḥrām of the rider is contracted permitting bowing and prostration by means of descending, so he may either perform gesturing while riding as a concession, or descend after iḥrām while riding and perform bowing and prostration as a determined duty. And by this is distinguished between his building and the lack of building for the sick person if he is able to bow and prostrate but was gesturing. Because the iḥrām of the sick person did not encompass them due to his inability, so it becomes like the iḥrām of one who descended and began the prayer on the ground, so it is not permissible for him to build what his iḥrām did not encompass upon what it encompassed. Therefore, it is not permissible for him to build after mounting on what he prayed while descending, according to Ẓāhir al-Riwāya from them. Because his beginning on the ground required all conditions, and in riding the condition of facing the qibla, unity of place and purity are lost, and that was permissible on the animal contrary to analogy initially except due to the necessity of travel. And gesturing on the animal is permissible even if it is for the emphasized supererogatory prayers and others, because they are voluntary prayers, so they are in their ruling, even the Sunnah of Fajr. And it is narrated from Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) that the rider should dismount for the Sunnah of Fajr because it is more emphasized than others. Ibn Shujāʿ said: This may be to indicate the preferable, meaning that it is preferable to dismount for the two rakʿahs of Fajr—this is in 'al-ʿInāya', and we have previously stated that this is according to the narration of its obligation. And it is permissible for the one performing voluntary prayer to lean on something—like a staff, a wall, or a servant—if he is tired, because it is an excuse. And if he wishes, he may sit, and that is without dislike.
Source pages p. 422

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah is an expansion (sharh) on the rulings of voluntary prayer (nafl) while riding an animal. The author begins by stating the basic ruling: it is permissible, even recommended, to perform voluntary prayer on a mount outside the built-up area of a town or city, gesturing (īmāʾ) towards whatever direction the animal faces. The term 'outside the city' is defined as the point where traveling begins and where shortening of prayer is allowed, though there are differing opinions on the exact distance. A key intra-Hanafi dispute arises regarding whether such prayer is also permissible inside the city. Abu Hanifa held it is not, because there is no necessity; Abu Yusuf argued it is, citing a hadith where the Prophet prayed on a donkey in Medina. The text explains that Abu Hanifa did not rebut the hadith, either out of deference or because he deemed it anomalous (shādh). Imam Muhammad agreed with Abu Yusuf in principle but disliked it in practice due to potential distractions. The passage then provides the evidence for gesturing (īmāʾ) from the hadith of Ibn Umar and Jabir, and explains the wisdom behind the concession: to avoid interrupting the prayer or the journey. It also clarifies that this applies even to emphasized regular supererogatory prayers (rawātib), though for the Fajr sunnah, Abu Hanifa reportedly considered it preferable to dismount. The text then addresses the issue of building upon (bināʾ) the prayer when one descends from the mount: if the rider dismounts without doing much extraneous action, he may complete his prayer on the ground, because his iḥrām encompassed the possibility of performing bowing and prostration via descent. This contrasts with a sick person who gestures—his iḥrām did not encompass actual bowing, so if he later becomes able, he cannot build. Finally, the passage permits leaning on something during voluntary prayer if one is tired, without dislike.

Key Terms
شاذ (shādh): An anomalous hadith; one narrated by a reliable person but conflicting with a stronger chain or established practice; not considered a proof in widespread matters.
إيماء (īmāʾ): Gesturing with the head or body instead of full bowing and prostration; used in prayer on a mount or by a sick person.
بلوى (balwā): A widespread matter that affects many people; used in the principle ʿumūm al-balwā to determine the acceptability of a hadith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did Abu Hanifa not raise his head when Abu Yusuf narrated the hadith about the Prophet praying on a donkey in Medina?
A) He was asleep.
B) He rejected the hadith completely.
C) He either deferred to the hadith or considered it shādh.
D) He was angry with Abu Yusuf.

Key Takeaway
The intra-Hanafi dispute on praying inside the city hinges on the classification of a hadith as shādh versus its acceptance as general evidence, with the muftā bihi following Abu Hanifa's view.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
7 min
Building (Binā') Upon Dismounting and the Sick Person's Analogy
Explains the permissibility, conditions, and intra-Hanafi dispute of nafl on a riding animal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on building (binā') a voluntary prayer when dismounting from a mount, and distinguish it from the ruling for a sick person who gestures.

Core Idea
A rider may build upon his prayer when dismounting, but a sick person may not, because the rider's iḥrām encompassed the ability to bow and prostrate via descent.

What happens if you begin a voluntary prayer on a mount and then decide to dismount? Can you continue the same prayer on the ground? The Hanafi school answers yes, based on a subtle difference in the nature of the iḥrām. This lesson explores the concept of binā' (building) and how it contrasts with the case of a sick person who gestures but later becomes able to move normally.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario for binā' on dismounting
The rider begins a voluntary prayer on the mount, then dismounts (e.g., bends his leg and slides down) without doing excessive extraneous movement. He may complete the remaining rakʿahs on the ground, building upon the initial part of the prayer.
This is valid because the iḥrām was contracted in a way that permitted both riding (gestures) and descending (actual movements).
2
Understand the reason: iḥrām encompassed the possibility of bowing and prostrating
When a rider begins prayer on a mount, his iḥrām (state of consecration) includes the permission to either gesture (as a concession) or descend and perform actual bowing and prostration (as a determined duty). Thus, the same iḥrām covers both modes.
In contrast, a sick person's iḥrām only covers gestures because they are unable to prostrate normally.
3
Compare with the sick person who becomes able to prostrate
If a sick person prays with gestures due to inability, then later becomes able to bow and prostrate, he cannot build upon his previous prayer. He must start anew, because his original iḥrām did not encompass the ability to perform full movements.
The difference is that the rider's iḥrām was from the beginning inclusive of the ability to descend and perform actual movements.
4
Identify the rules for mounting after dismounting
If a person begins prayer on the ground, then mounts an animal, he cannot build upon the earlier part because his iḥrām while on the ground required all conditions (qibla, purity, etc.), which are lost when mounting.
Thus, binā' is valid from mount to ground, but not from ground to mount.
5
Note the condition: no excessive action during transition
The dismount must not involve much extraneous movement (e.g., swinging the leg and sliding down is fine; turning around or lengthy actions break continuity).
This is consistent with the general principle that excessive movement invalidates prayer.

ولا ركوعاً قاعداً. انتهى. وموافقته للسنة ذكرناها فيما تقدم، وفي «مجمع الروايات» أنَّه عليه الصلاة والسلام كان يفتتح التطوع قائماً ثم يقعد، فإذا بقي من قراءته مقدار عشرين آية أو ثلاثين آية، قام فقرأ ثم ركع ثم سجد. ويتنفل أي: جاز له التنفل، بل ندب له راكباً خارج المصر أي: خارج العمران ليشمل خارج القرية، وخارج محل إقامته الذي إذا جاوزه يصير مسافراً، كالأخبية. وسواء كان مسافراً أو مقيماً، خرج لحاجة في بعض النواحي على الأصح، فالمراد بخارج المصر: الموضع الذي يجوز للمسافر أن يقصر فيه الصلاة، وهو على الأصح، وقيل: إذا خرج قدر فرسخين أو أكثر جاز له، وإلا فلا، وقيل: إذا خرج قدر الميل يجوز، وعن أبي يوسف بالحديث، ومحمد كذلك، ولكنه كرهه في رواية مخافة الغلط بكثرة اللغط في المصر، ونفاه في أخرى للحديث الذي رواه أبو يوسف، وروي أيضاً عن أبي يوسف وأبي حنيفة أنها لا تجوز على الدابة إلا للمسافر خاصة للضرورة، ولا ضرورة في الحضر، فيصلي عليها مومياً إلى أي جهة توجهت به دابته لقول ابن عمر: رأيت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يصلي على راحلته وهو متوجه إلى خيبر رواه مسلم وغيره. ولقول جابر: رأيت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يصلي النوافل على راحلته في كل وجه يومي إيماء ولكنَّه يخفض السجدتين من الركعتين رواه ابن حبان في صحيحه، ولأن في إلزامه النزول والتوجه انقطاعاً عن النافلة أو القافلة، بخلاف الفرائض لاختصاصها بأوقاتها، فلا يشق عليه النزول للأداء والرفقاء متظافرون معه على ذلك، فلا يجوز إلا من عذر، كما إذا لم يقفواله وخاف اللصوص أو السبع، جاز له أن يصليها راكباً، ويجوز أن يفتتح الصلاة حيثما توجهت به الدابة، Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah is an expansion (sharh) on the rulings of voluntary prayer (nafl) while riding an animal. The author begins by stating the basic ruling: it is permissible, even recommended, to perform voluntary prayer on a mount outside the built-up area of a town or city, gesturing (īmāʾ) towards whatever direction the animal faces. The term 'outside the city' is defined as the point where traveling begins and where shortening of prayer is allowed, though there are differing opinions on the exact distance. A key intra-Hanafi dispute arises regarding whether such prayer is also permissible inside the city. Abu Hanifa held it is not, because there is no necessity; Abu Yusuf argued it is, citing a hadith where the Prophet prayed on a donkey in Medina. The text explains that Abu Hanifa did not rebut the hadith, either out of deference or because he deemed it anomalous (shādh). Imam Muhammad agreed with Abu Yusuf in principle but disliked it in practice due to potential distractions. The passage then provides the evidence for gesturing (īmāʾ) from the hadith of Ibn Umar and Jabir, and explains the wisdom behind the concession: to avoid interrupting the prayer or the journey. It also clarifies that this applies even to emphasized regular supererogatory prayers (rawātib), though for the Fajr sunnah, Abu Hanifa reportedly considered it preferable to dismount. The text then addresses the issue of building upon (bināʾ) the prayer when one descends from the mount: if the rider dismounts without doing much extraneous action, he may complete his prayer on the ground, because his iḥrām encompassed the possibility of performing bowing and prostration via descent. This contrasts with a sick person who gestures—his iḥrām did not encompass actual bowing, so if he later becomes able, he cannot build. Finally, the passage permits leaning on something during voluntary prayer if one is tired, without dislike.

Key Terms
بناء (bināʾ): Building upon a prayer already started; here it means continuing the same prayer after dismounting without interruption.
إيماء (īmāʾ): Gesturing with the head or body instead of full bowing and prostration; used in prayer on a mount or by a sick person.
إحرام (iḥrām): The state of consecration in prayer; the intention and initial takbīr that mark the beginning of prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a sick person who gestures not allowed to build upon his prayer when he becomes able to bow and prostrate normally?
A) Because the sick person's illness is a punishment.
B) Because his iḥrām did not encompass the ability to perform actual movements.
C) Because he must make up the prayer later.
D) Because he should have prayed facing the qibla.

Key Takeaway
A rider may build upon his voluntary prayer when dismounting because his iḥrām included the capacity for actual movements, unlike the sick person whose iḥrām was limited to gestures.

Building upon Prayer when Dismounting vs. Mounting
Ruling on continuing supererogatory prayer after changing mode

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on continuing supererogatory prayer after dismounting versus after mounting, and explain the legal reasoning (talil) behind the distinction.

Core Idea
A rider's ihram permits ruku and sujud via dismounting; a ground-starter's ihram requires all conditions, so mounting invalidates continuation.

This lesson examines a nuanced Hanafi ruling regarding supererogatory prayer while traveling. The key is understanding how the state of ihram (consecration) is contracted differently when one begins prayer while mounted versus on the ground. The passage provides a clear talil (legal cause) to distinguish between valid continuation after dismounting and invalid continuation after mounting, and contrasts it with the case of a sick person who recovers mid-prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage addresses two cases: (1) beginning prayer while mounted and then dismounting, and (2) beginning prayer on the ground and then mounting. State the ruling for each as given in the matn.
The matn says 'and he builds upon his dismounting' (yabni bi nuzulihi) and 'it is not permissible for him to build after mounting' (la yajuz lahu al-bina' ba'da rukubihi).
2
Understand the talil for the first scenario
The reasoning: when a rider enters ihram (i.e., starts prayer), his ihram is contracted with a permission to perform ruku and sujud by means of dismounting. Therefore, if he dismounts, the prayer continues validly because he is fulfilling what his ihram permitted.
The key phrase: 'because the ihram of the rider was contracted permitting ruku and sujud by means of dismounting' (li anna ihram al-rakib in'aqada mujawwizan al-ruku' wa al-sujud bi wasitat al-nuzul).
3
Understand why mounting invalidates continuation
When one begins prayer on the ground, his ihram requires all conditions of prayer: facing qibla, a pure and stable place, etc. Mounting the animal (or vehicle) necessarily violates these conditions (e.g., changing qibla, moving from the pure spot). Therefore, the continuation after mounting is invalid.
The text mentions that the condition of facing qibla, unity of place, and purity are lost (fawta shart al-istighal wa ittihad al-makan wa taharatihi).
4
Distinguish from the sick person analogy
The passage contrasts the rider with a sick person who performs prayer with ishara (gestures). If the sick person recovers and can perform actual ruku and sujud, he does not build upon his previous gestures because his ihram did not encompass actual ruku and sujud at all. The rider's ihram did encompass them (via dismounting).
The sick person's ihram 'did not encompass them due to his inability' (lam yatana'allahuma li 'admi qudratihi 'alayhima).
5
Note the authority weight
The ruling for the second scenario (no building after mounting) is stated as the position in 'Zahir al-Riwayah' (the apparent transmission). This is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school.
The text says 'fi zahir al-riwayah 'anhum' (in the apparent transmission from them).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبنى بِنُزُولِهِ) على ما صلـى مـن التطوع إذا لم يحصل منه عمل كثير، كما إذا [ ثنى ] رجله فانحدر من الجانب الآخر فيتمها على الأرض؛ لأن إحرام الراكب انعقد مجوزاً الركوع والسجود بواسطة النزول، فكان له أن يأتي بالإيماء راكباً رخصة، أو ينزل بعد الإحرام راكباً، فيأتي بالركوع والسجود عزيمة، وبهذا يفــرق بـيـن بنائــه وعــدم بناء المريض إذا قدر على الركوع والسجود، وكان مومياً؛ لأن إحرام المريض لم يتناولهما؛ لـعــدم قدرته عليهما، فصار كإحرام النازل الذي افتتح الصلاة على الأرض، فلا يجوز بنـاء مـا لـم يتناوله إحرامه على ما تناوله، فلذا ( لا ) يجوز له البناء بعد (رُكُوبِهِ) على مــا صـلاه نازلاً، في « ظـاهـر الرواية عنهم، لأن افتتاحه على الأرض استلزم جميع الشروط وفي الركوب يفوت شرط الاستقبال واتحاد المكان وطهارته، وما جاز ذلك على الدابة على خلاف القياس ابتداء إلا لضرورة السير.
And he builds upon his dismounting the supererogatory prayer if he did not perform much action, such as when he bends his leg and descends from the other side, completing it on the ground because the ihram of the rider was contracted permitting ruku and sujud by means of dismounting. So he may either perform with ishara while riding as a concession, or dismount after ihram while riding and perform ruku and sujud as a determination. And with this is distinguished between his building and the lack of building of the sick person if he is able to do ruku and sujud and was making ishara, because the ihram of the sick person did not encompass them due to his inability, so it becomes like the ihram of one who descended and began prayer on the ground. Thus it is not permissible for him to build what his ihram did not encompass upon what it encompassed. Therefore, it is not permissible for him to build after mounting upon what he prayed while dismounted, in the apparent transmission from them, because his beginning on the ground necessitated all conditions, and in riding the condition of facing the qibla, unity of place, and purity are lost, and that was permitted on the animal against analogy initially only due to the necessity of travel.
Source pages p. 423

Commentary
This passage presents a Hanafi ruling on building (continuing) supererogatory prayer when the rider changes mode. The core principle: if a rider begins prayer while mounted, his ihram (state of consecration) permits ruku and sujud by means of dismounting. Therefore, if he dismounts, he can complete the prayer on the ground with actual ruku and sujud. However, if he begins prayer on the ground, his ihram requires all conditions (facing qibla, pure place, etc.), which are lost when he mounts. Thus, if he mounts during prayer, he cannot continue it while riding. This ruling is distinguished from the sick person who makes ishara: the sick person's ihram never included ruku and sujud, so he cannot later perform them. The authority weight is Zahir al-Riwayah as it says 'fi zahir al-riwayah.'

Key Terms
إحرام (ihram): The state of entering prayer, making the act unlawful for other things.
عزيمة (azima): The full performance of ruku and sujud without concession.
إيماء (ishaara): Gesture performed in prayer when unable to do actual ruku and sujud.
رخصة (rukhsah): A concession allowed due to necessity, such as ishaara while riding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person begins supererogatory prayer while mounted and then dismounts, what is the ruling?
A) He must restart the prayer on the ground.
B) He may continue the prayer on the ground by performing actual ruku and sujud.
C) He must continue with ishara while walking.
D) The prayer becomes invalid.

Key Takeaway
The validity of continuing prayer after changing posture depends on how the ihram was contracted: a rider's ihram permits actual ruku/sujud via dismounting, while a ground-starter's ihram requires full conditions lost on mounting.

Supererogatory Prayers on Mount and Sunnah al-Fajr
Intra-Hanafi dispute on performing Sunnah al-Fajr while riding

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the general Hanafi ruling on performing supererogatory prayers on a mount from the narrated view of Imam Abu Hanifa regarding Sunnah al-Fajr, and apply the interpretation that resolves the apparent dispute.

Core Idea
Even the Sunnah of Fajr can be performed on a mount, but dismounting is superior — the school follows the general rule for nafl.

This passage deals with a practical scenario: a traveler who is riding and wishes to pray the sunnah prayers, including the highly emphasized Sunnah of Fajr. The Hanafi school generally permits performing all supererogatory prayers on a mount using gestures (ishara). However, a narrated view from Imam Abu Hanifa suggests that the rider should dismount for Sunnah al-Fajr because of its special emphasis. Our commentator explains that this view indicates preference, not obligation, and thus the practical ruling remains flexible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general Hanafi rule for nafl prayers on a mount
Establish that all supererogatory prayers can be performed with ishara while riding, including the confirmed sunnahs (ratibah). The reasoning is that they are nafl, and nafl are given leniency.
This is the baseline ruling from which the dispute arises.
2
Note the exception: the narrated view of Imam Abu Hanifa on Sunnah al-Fajr
Recognize that Imam Abu Hanifa is reported to have said the rider should dismount for the Sunnah of Fajr. This creates an apparent conflict with the general rule.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; it does not come from another madhhab.
3
Understand the basis of Abu Hanifa's view
The reported reason is that the Sunnah of Fajr is more confirmed (akad) than other sunnahs. Hence, it deserves more care and should be performed with full ruku and sujud.
The emphasis on Fajr sunnah is widely recognized across schools.
4
Apply the interpretive response of Ibn Shuja'
Ibn Shuja' explains that Abu Hanifa's statement indicates 'al-ula' (superiority), not obligation. Thus, the general permissibility remains valid, but dismounting is better.
This harmonizes the two positions within the school.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practical consequence
The relied-upon position is that all nafl, including Fajr sunnah, can be performed on a mount. Dismounting earns more reward, but the prayer on the mount is valid.
This flexibility facilitates worship for travelers.

Commentary
This passage addresses the permissibility of performing supererogatory (nafl) prayers while riding, including the confirmed sunnah prayers (ratibah). The general rule: since they are nafl, they can be performed with ishara (gestures) on the animal. Even the Sunnah of Fajr is included. However, there is a narrated view from Imam Abu Hanifa that the rider should dismount for the Sunnah of Fajr because it is more emphasized. Ibn Shuja' interprets this as indicating preference (afdaliyyah), not obligation. The text notes that this relates to a narration that considers Sunnah al-Fajr obligatory (wajib), a minority view. The mufta bihi position is that it is permissible to perform all supererogatory prayers while riding, but dismounting for Fajr Sunnah is superior.

إيماء (ishara): Gestures for ruku and sujud, done by moving the head, on a riding animal.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits all supererogatory prayers, including Sunnah al-Fajr, to be performed on a mount, but dismounting for Fajr is more virtuous.

Leaning in Supererogatory Prayer with Excuse
Ruling on leaning in nafl with and without excuse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of leaning in nafl prayer with and without an excuse, and identify the conditions for permissibility.

Core Idea
An excuse transforms leaning in nafl from disliked to permissible.

This lesson addresses a common practical question: can one lean on something while performing supererogatory (nafl) prayer? The ruling depends on whether the worshipper has a legitimate excuse, such as fatigue. Understanding this distinction helps avoid unnecessary hardship while maintaining proper adab in prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
The act is leaning on something (stick, wall, servant) during nafl prayer. Determine the default hukm without any excuse.
The default is dislike (karahah tanzihiyyah) due to poor adab.
2
Examine the condition that changes the ruling
Identify the excuse (tiredness) that makes leaning permissible without dislike. Recognize that the excuse must be genuine.
Tiredness is a valid udhr in the Hanafi school.
3
Distinguish between leaning and sitting
Note that sitting without excuse after starting standing is different from leaning; the text distinguishes them.
Sitting without excuse after standing is not disliked in the same way.
4
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Given a scenario, determine whether leaning is permissible or disliked based on presence or absence of an excuse.
If no excuse, the act is makruh tanzihan; prayer is still valid.

However, if he leans or sits without any excuse, it is disliked (makruh tanzihan) as it shows poor etiquette. The text distinguishes this from sitting after standing in the beginning of prayer, which is different. The authority weight is not specified but likely relies on the general principles of nafl concessions.

كراهة (karahah): Dislike (reprehensibility) in prayer; here it is tanzihi (lesser dislike).

Impurity on Riding Animal Does Not Invalidate Prayer
Ruling on performance of prayer on a mount that has impurity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi majority ruling on prayer with impurity on a riding animal, explain the darurah rationale, and distinguish the minority view.

Core Idea
Necessity overrules the condition of purity of place for prayer on a mount.

When traveling, the Shari'ah relaxes several conditions of prayer, such as facing the qibla and purity of the place of prayer. This lesson addresses a specific case: an animal that has impurity on its body, saddle, or stirrups while a person prays on it. The majority of Hanafi scholars rule that the prayer remains valid, but a minority objects. We will examine the proof and the rationale behind the majority view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its normal conditions
Identify the act under consideration: prayer performed on a riding animal. Normally, a condition for valid prayer is that the place of prayer (including the surface one prays on) must be free of impurity (taharah al-makan). Determine what this condition requires.
This condition applies to the ground, but on an animal it may be relaxed.
2
State the majority Hanafi ruling
State the ruling: the prayer is valid (sahih) even if there is considerable impurity (greater than a dirham) on the animal, its saddle, or stirrups. This is the position of most mashayikh as recorded in al-Muhit and al-Kafi.
3
Analyse the proof (dalil) for the ruling
Identify the proof: necessity (darurah). The author argues that because essential pillars of prayer (like facing qibla) are dropped for the traveler, the condition of purity of place is even more appropriately dropped. This is a rational argument (dalil aqli) based on the principle that the greater exemption includes the lesser.
The proof is not a direct text but an inference from the established relaxation of other conditions.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Note the minority view from al-Tajnis and al-Mazid: they distinguish between types of impurity. If the impurity on the saddle is solid (feces, blood) and exceeds a dirham, the prayer is invalid; if it is sweat or saliva of a donkey, it is valid due to doubt. The majority rejects this distinction, asserting that donkey sweat and saliva are pure.
The majority view is mufta bihi.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The practical difference: under the majority view, one need not worry about impurity on the animal during travel. Under the minority, one must check the type of impurity. The majority view provides ease.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يمنع صحة الصَّلاةِ على الدابة نجاسة) كثيرة (عَلَيْهَا) أي: الدابة ( ولـو كـانَتْ) النجاسة التي تزيد على الدرهم ( في السَّرْجِ، والرِّكَابَيْنِ، في الأصح)، كذا في ( البحر ) ، عن ( المحيط » و « الكافي»، وهو قول أكثر مشايخنا لأنه لما سقط اعتبار الأركان الأصلية فلأن يسقط شرط طهارة المكان أولى لما فيه من الضرورة، كما في «الفتح» و المعراج» وغيرهما، وبه تعلم أن ما في «التجنيس والمزيد على قول غير الأكثر، حيث قال: إن كان على السرج نجاسة من العذرة أو الدم أكثر من قدر الدرهم () فصلاته فاسدة؛ لأنه صلـى علـى موضع نجس، وإن كان عرق الحمار أو لعابه فصلاته جائزة؛ لأنه مشكوك، هذا معنى قول أصحابنا رحمهم الله : الرجل إذا صلى على الدابة وسرجه نجس تجوز صلاته انتهى لأن هذا الحمل على غير الصحيح، لأن الصحيح طهارة عرقه ولعابه كما قدمنا )
And it does not prevent the validity of prayer on the animal if there is (considerable) impurity on it, i.e., on the animal, even if the impurity that exceeds the size of a dirham is on the saddle and the stirrups, in the most correct view. Thus in al-Bahr, from al-Muhit and al-Kafi, and it is the saying of most of our mashayikh because when the consideration of the essential pillars is dropped, then to drop the condition of purity of place is more appropriate due to the necessity in it. As in al-Fath and al-Mi'raj and others. And by this you know that what is in al-Tajnis and al-Mazid follows the saying of the non-majority, where he said: If there is impurity of feces or blood more than the size of a dirham on the saddle, his prayer is invalid because he prays on a impure place; and if it is the sweat or saliva of a donkey, his prayer is permissible because it is doubtful. This is the meaning of our associates' saying: 'The man, when he prays on the animal and his saddle is impure, his prayer is permissible.' end quote because this interpretation is upon the incorrect view, because the correct view is the purity of its sweat and saliva as we have presented.
Source pages p. 424

Commentary
This passage deals with the impurity (najis) on the riding animal during prayer. The majority of Hanafi scholars hold that even if there is an amount of impurity exceeding a dirham on the animal, its saddle, or stirrups, the prayer remains valid. The reasoning is that since the essential pillars (like facing qibla) are dropped for necessity (darurah), the condition of purity of place is even more likely to be dropped. A minority view from al-Tajnis and al-Mazid distinguishes: if the impurity is solid (e.g., blood, feces) on the saddle, the prayer is invalid because the place is impure; but if it is the sweat or saliva of a donkey (which is impure in their view), it is still valid due to doubt. The majority rejects this, affirming that sweat and saliva of a donkey are pure (tahir), as established earlier. The authority weight is the majority (akthar al-mashayikh).

Key Terms
نجاسة (najis): Impurity that prevents validity of prayer in normal circumstances.
ضرور (darurah): Necessity that permits relaxation of normal conditions.
سرج (saraj): Saddle of the riding animal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary proof (dalil) used by the majority of Hanafi scholars to permit prayer on an animal with impurity?
A) A hadith stating the Prophet prayed on a donkey with impurity.
B) A Quranic verse about purification.
C) The principle that necessity excuses the condition of purity of place, since more essential conditions are already dropped.
D) Ijma of the companions.

Key Takeaway
The majority Hanafi view permits prayer on a riding animal even with considerable impurity on its saddle or stirrups due to the necessity of travel.

Prayer of a Walking Person is Invalid by Consensus
Consensus that prayer while walking is invalid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the prayer of a walking person, explain the reasoning based on ijma, and distinguish it from the exception of riding.

Core Idea
The prayer of a walking person is invalid by Hanafi consensus because movement disrupts the required stability of the pillars.

This lesson examines a clear case of ijma (consensus) within the Hanafi school: the invalidity of prayer while walking. While other schools may allow walking under necessity, the Hanafi imams unanimously hold that any voluntary locomotion invalidates the prayer. We will unpack the reasoning and the contrast with the allowance for riding.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is 'the prayer of a walking person' (salat al-mashi). According to the text, it is invalid (batil) by consensus.
The ruling is absolute; it does not depend on intention or necessity.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is ijma (consensus) of the Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad), as reported in al-Mujtaba and Majma' al-Riwayat.
Ijma is a primary source in Hanafi usul, and here it is cited as qat'i.
3
Examine the reasoning (ta'lil)
Walking causes a change of place (ikhtilaf al-makan) and performance of pillars with contradiction (ada' al-arkan ma'a al-manafi), which invalidates prayer.
Stability (tuma'ninah) is a required condition for the pillars.
4
Contrast with the exception
Prayer on a riding animal is valid for nafl prayers when traveling, as established by the Prophet's action (sunnah). This exception does not extend to walking.
The difference is necessity: walking is not a necessity in the same way.
5
Determine the epistemological weight
This ruling is based on ijma, which is higher than individual analogy. It is binding for fatwa within the Hanafi school.
Other schools may differ, but within Hanafism it is settled.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا تصح صلاةُ الماشي، بالإجماع)، كذا في «مجمع الروايات » ، وفي ( البحر » ، عن ( المجتبى»: والمراد إجماع أئمتنا، وذلك لاختلاف المكان وأداء الأركان مع المنافي لا يصح، وأما الصلاة على الدابة فقد علمت بفعله .
And the prayer of the walking person is not valid, by consensus (ijma). Thus in Majma' al-Riwayat, and in al-Bahr, from al-Mujtaba: what is meant is the consensus of our imams (Hanafi). And that is because of the differing of the place and the performance of the pillars with contradiction does not become valid. As for the prayer on the animal, you have known its action.
Source pages p. 424

Commentary
This passage states that the prayer of a person who is walking (mashi) is invalid by consensus (ijma') among the Hanafi imams. The reason is that walking involves a change of location and movement that contradicts the requirement of stability (tuma'ninah) for performing the pillars of prayer. Unlike a person riding an animal, who may be excused due to necessity of travel, a walking person has no such excuse and must stand stationary. The text contrasts this with the permissibility of prayer on a riding animal, which has been established by the action of the Prophet (peace be upon him). The authority weight is consensus (ijma) of the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
إجماع (ijma): Consensus of the Hanafi imams on this ruling.
ماشي (mashi): A person walking on foot while performing prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Valid if he is traveling.
B) Invalid by consensus.
C) Valid if he performs all pillars properly.
D) Allowed for supererogatory prayers.

Key Takeaway
The prayer of a walking person is invalid by Hanafi consensus due to the disruption of stability required for the pillars.

Impurity on a Riding Animal and Walking Prayer Invalidity
Explains rulings on leaning, impurity on animal, and walking prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on impurity on a riding animal, explain the qiyas used to justify it, and identify the minority intra-Hanafi position.

Core Idea
Impurity on a riding animal does not invalidate prayer because necessity drops the condition of purity.

This lesson addresses several practical issues for the traveler who prays on an animal. The central question is whether impurity on the animal or its saddle invalidates the prayer. The Hanafi majority, using analogy and necessity, rule that it does not. A minority disagree, and we will examine their argument. Additionally, we cover the rulings on leaning without excuse and the invalidity of walking prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first ruling on leaning
Find where the text states that leaning without excuse is makruh tanzih. Note the reason given: bad manners.
This is not prohibited, only disliked.
2
Locate the main ruling on impurity
Find the statement that impurity on the animal does not prevent validity, even on the saddle or stirrups, in the most correct view.
The text states 'in the most correct view' indicating a preferred position.
3
Trace the dalil for the impurity ruling
The reasoning is qiyas awla: since the original pillars (standing, facing qibla) are dropped due to necessity, the condition of purity of place is dropped with even greater reason. This is based on istihsan.
The Arabic phrase 'اولى' shows the logic of priority.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
The minority (from al-Tajnis) argue that if there is dry impurity (blood, feces) on the saddle exceeding a dirham, the prayer is invalid. They distinguish between such dry impurity and sweat/saliva which are doubtful.
The commentator refutes this by stating that donkey sweat and saliva are pure in the correct view.
5
State the ruling on walking prayer
Praying while walking is invalid by consensus of Hanafi imams due to instability of place and inability to properly perform pillars.
This is contrasted with prayer on a moving animal, which is allowed by sunna.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(ولا يمنع صحة الصَّلاةِ على الدابة نجاسة) كثيرة (عَلَيْهَا ) أي: الدابة ( ولــو كـانَتْ) النجاسة التي تزيد على الدرهم ( في السَّرْجِ، والرِّكَابَيْنِ، في الأصح)، كذا في ( البحر ) ، عن ( المحيط » و « الكافي»، وهو قول أكثر مشايخنا لأنه لما سقط اعتبار الأركان الأصلية فلأن يسقط شرط طهارة المكان أولى لما فيه من الضرورة، كما في «الفتح» و المعراج» وغيرهما، وبه تعلم أن ما في «التجنيس والمزيد على قول غير الأكثر، حيث قال: إن كان على السرج نجاسة من العذرة أو الدم أكثر من قدر الدرهم () فصلاته فاسدة؛ لأنه صلــى علـى موضع نجس، وإن كان عرق الحمار أو لعابه فصلاته جائزة؛ لأنه مشكوك، هذا معنى قول أصحابنا رحمهم الله : الرجل إذا صلى على الدابة وسرجه نجس تجوز صلاته انتهى لأن هذا الحمل على غير الصحيح، لأن الصحيح طهارة عرقه ولعابه كما قدمنا ) ( ولا تصح صلاةُ الماشي، بالإجماع)، كذا في «مجمع الروايات » ، وفي ( البحر » ، عن ( المجتبى»: والمراد إجماع أئمتنا، وذلك لاختلاف المكان وأداء الأركان مع المنافي لا يصح، وأما الصلاة على الدابة فقد علمت بفعله .
And if [leaning] occurs without an excuse, it is disliked in the most apparent view, because of bad manners. And impurity on the riding animal does not prevent the validity of the prayer, even if it is on the saddle and the stirrups, in the most correct view. And the prayer of a walking person is not valid by consensus. [Commentary:] For an excuse, (and if leaning occurs without an excuse it is disliked in the most apparent view, because of bad manners), unlike sitting without an excuse after opening the prayer while standing as we presented. (And impurity on the animal does not prevent the validity of the prayer) meaning abundant impurity (on it, i.e., the animal) (even if the impurity that is more than a dirham was on the saddle and the stirrups, in the most correct view). Thus in al-Bahr, from al-Muhit and al-Kafi, and it is the saying of the majority of our mashayikh because when the consideration of the original pillars dropped, then the condition of purity of place dropping is more appropriate due to the necessity, as in al-Fath, al-Mi'raj and others. And from it you know that what is in al-Tajnis and al-Mazid is according to the saying of the non-majority, where he said: If there is impurity from feces or blood on the saddle exceeding the measure of a dirham, then his prayer is invalid because he prayed on a filthy place. And if it is the sweat or saliva of the donkey, then his prayer is permissible because it is doubtful. This is the meaning of the saying of our companions (may Allah have mercy on them): A man if he prays on a riding animal and its saddle is impure, his prayer is permissible. End quote. Because this interpretation is not correct, because the correct view is that its sweat and saliva are pure as we have presented. (And the prayer of a walking person is not valid by consensus). Thus in Majma' al-Riwayat, and in al-Bahr from al-Mujtaba: The meaning is the consensus of our imams. That is because of the difference of place and performing the pillars with a contrary factor does not validate. As for prayer on the riding animal, it is known by his action.
Source pages p. 424

Commentary
This passage from the commentary discusses several rulings related to prayer on a riding animal. First, it addresses the issue of leaning during prayer without a valid excuse: such leaning is disliked (makruh) in the most apparent view, not prohibited, because it is a breach of proper conduct, but it does not invalidate the prayer. Then it addresses impurity: if the rider or the animal has impurity on it, even a significant amount (more than a dirham), and even if the impurity is on the saddle or stirrups, the prayer is still valid according to the majority of Hanafi scholars (e.g., as reported in al-Bahr, al-Muhit, al-Kafi). The reasoning is qiyas: since the basic pillars like standing and facing the qibla are not required (due to necessity of riding), then the condition of purity of place is less important. This is istihsan based on necessity. However, there is a minority view (from al-Tajnis) that if there is dry impurity on the saddle, the prayer is invalid, but the commentator rejects this, noting that the sweat and saliva of the donkey are considered pure in the correct view. Finally, the passage states that praying while walking (i.e., moving on foot) is invalid by the consensus of the Hanafi imams. The reason is that prayer requires stability of place and proper performance of postures, which is not possible while walking.

Key Terms
الظاهر (al-ẓāhir): In this context, 'al-azhar' means the most apparent or preferred ruling among Hanafi scholars.
الأصح (al-aṣaḥḥ): The most correct view among the scholars, often indicating the stronger opinion.
مشايخنا (mashāyikhunā): Our scholars — referring to the later Hanafi authorities who transmit and weigh the founding texts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The prayer is invalid because the place is impure.
B) The prayer is valid because the condition of purity is dropped due to necessity.
C) The prayer is valid only if the impurity is from sweat rather than feces.
D) The prayer must be repeated after getting off.

Key Takeaway
Prayer on a riding animal remains valid despite impurity on the animal or saddle because the condition of purity is waived by necessity and qiyas awla.

Conditions for Obligatory Prayer on a Riding Animal
States when obligatory prayers on animal are invalid and exceptions of necessity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general rule for obligatory prayer on a riding animal, list the valid excuses (darura), and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding being capable through another's capability.

Core Idea
Obligatory prayer on an animal is invalid except for severe necessity; being capable through another's help is disputed.

Praying on a riding animal is a concession for those in genuine need. The Hanafi school sets clear limits: only supererogatory prayers are normally allowed on an animal. This lesson examines when obligatory prayers become permissible due to necessity, and a key disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples about whether finding help to dismount makes one truly capable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule and its exceptions
Read the opening sentence: 'لا يصح على الدابة صلاة الفرائض ولا الواجبات... إلا لضرورة'. Note the types of prayers included (fard, wajib, janaza, sajda tilawa) and the necessity exceptions listed.
The rule is a default prohibition; exceptions are limited.
2
Analyze each exception listed
List the excuses: fear of thief for self/animal/clothes, fear of wild beast, mud, bolting animal, inability to mount. Understand why each constitutes darura.
The common thread is real harm or severe hardship.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute on 'qadir bi-qudrat al-ghayr'
Imam Abu Hanifa says one who can get help to dismount is not capable through another's help, so he must dismount. The Sahibayn say he is capable and may stay mounted. Identify the thamarah al-khilaf.
This affects whether one must descend when help is available.
4
Apply the dispute to the woman's scenario
The text extends the logic to a woman who can only descend with a mahram. If she has a mahram, is she considered capable? The author of al-Bahr notes this is unresolved.
This shows the practical application of the ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في صلاة الفرض والواجب على الدابة والمحمل لا يصح على الدابة صلاة الفرائض ولا الواجبات كالوتر، والمنذور، وما شرع فيه نفلاً فأفسده، ولا صلاة الجنازة، وسجدة تُلِيَتْ آيتها على الأرض، إلا لضرورة، كخوفِ لص على نفسهِ، أَوْ دَابَتِهِ، أَوْ ثيابهِ لَوْ نَزَلَ، وخوفِ سَبْعٍ، وطين المكان، وجُمُوحِ الدّابة وعدمِ وِجْدَانِ مَنْ يُرْكِبُهُ لِعَجْزِهِ، والعاجز عن الركوب لو نزل إذا وجد من يركبه فهي مسألة القادر بقدرة الغير، ولا يكون قادراً بها عند الإمام خلافاً لهما، وعلى هذا المرأة إذا لم تقدر على النزول إلا بمحرم أو زوج من «الفتح»، و « العناية»، و «معراج الدراية»، و « الخانية»، و «التبيين غيرها، وقال صاحب «البحر » : لم أرَ حكـم مـا إذا كان راكباً معادلاً لامرأته أو محرمه، ولم تقدر المرأة على النزول بنفسها، أيجوز للرجل المعادل لها صلاة الفرض
Chapter on the obligatory and mandatory prayer on the riding animal and the howdah. It is not valid on the animal the prayers of obligations, nor the mandatory ones like witr, and the vowed prayer, and what one started as supererogatory then invalidated, nor the funeral prayer, nor the prostration (sajda tilawa) whose verse was recited on the ground, except due to necessity, such as fear of a thief for himself, or his animal, or his clothes if he descends, and fear of a wild beast, and mud of the place, and the bolting of the animal, and not finding someone to ride it due to his inability. And the one unable to ride if he dismounts and finds someone to ride him, this is the issue of the capable through the capability of another. He is not considered capable by it according to Imam [Abu Hanifa], contrary to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad]. And upon this, the woman if she is unable to descend except with a mahram or husband, from al-Fath, al-Inaya, Miraj al-Diraya, al-Khaniyya, al-Tabyin and others. And the author of al-Bahr said: I have not seen the ruling concerning when one is riding opposite his wife or mahram and the woman is unable to descend by herself: is it permissible for the man opposite her to pray the obligatory prayer?
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
This section (fasl) presents the general rule that obligatory (fard) and wajib prayers (like witr, nadhr, and makeup of a spoiled nafl) are not valid on a riding animal, nor is the janaza prayer or sajda tilawa, except when there is a genuine necessity (darura). The text provides examples of valid excuses: fear of a thief for one's life, animal, or belongings if one were to dismount; fear of a wild beast; excessive mud that would make prostration impossible; the animal bolting (running away uncontrollably); and inability to mount the animal (lack of someone to help mount). The passage then discusses a specific case: a person who is unable to ride, if he dismounts and finds someone to help him ride, is he considered capable (qādir) through the capability of another? Imam Abu Hanifa says he is not capable, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) say he is. This difference has practical implications for the permissibility of praying on the animal. The text extends this to a woman who cannot descend without a mahram or husband: if she is riding with them, can the man pray fard on the animal? The author of al-Bahr notes that he hasn't seen a ruling on this specific scenario, indicating an unresolved point.

Key Terms
القادر بقدرة الغير (al-qādir bi-qudrat al-ghayr): Someone who is unable to do something by themselves but can do it with another person's help.
جموح (jumūḥ): An animal bolting or running away uncontrollably, making it dangerous to ride.
محروم (maḥram): A male relative whom a woman is permanently prohibited from marrying (e.g., father, brother).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He must dismount and pray on the ground, because he is not considered capable through another's help.
B) He may continue praying on the animal because he can get help.
C) He must repeat the prayer later.
D) His prayer is valid regardless.

Key Takeaway
Obligatory prayers on a riding animal are invalid without severe necessity, and the ability gained through another's help does not remove the obligation to dismount according to the relied-upon Hanafi position.

General Rule: Fard/Wajib Prayer on an Animal is Invalid Except for Necessity
Ruling with proof on validity of obligatory prayers on animals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general Hanafi rule regarding fard/wajib prayers on an animal and identify the specific conditions that constitute valid darurah.

Core Idea
Fard and wajib prayers are invalid on an animal — only genuine necessity permits them as a concession.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah establishes the general principle: obligatory prayers (fard and wajib) are not valid when performed on an animal. However, the Shariah makes an exception for dire necessity. Understanding when necessity qualifies is crucial to applying this ruling correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling
State that fard/wajib prayers are invalid on an animal as per the opening sentence.
The ruling applies to witr, nadhr, and other wajib prayers as well.
2
List the exceptions
Note the specific necessities: fear for life/property, wild beast, mud, bolting, inability to mount.
Mere dampness is not sufficient; the mud must be severe.
3
Examine the dalil
Recall Quran 2:239 which permits prayer in fear on foot or riding.
The Hanafi school analogizes other fears to battlefield fear.
4
Apply to borderline excuses
Distinguish severe mud from light rain; the text specifies mud that soils the face or clothes.
If the animal is moving, validity depends on ability to stop.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(والصلاةُ في المَحْمِلِ) وهو ( على الدَّابَّة، كالصَّلاة عليها) أي: على الدابة في الحكم الذي علمته (سواء كانت سائرةً، أو واقفةً. ولو) أوقفها و (جعل تحت المحمِل خشبة) أو نحوها (حتى بقي قراره) أي: المحمل ( إلى الأرض) بواسطة الخشبة ونحوها ( كان ) أي: صار المحمل (بمنزلة الأرض، فتصح الفريضة فيه قائماً)، أما الصلاة على العجلة إن كان طرف العجلة على الدابة، وهي تسير أو لا تسير، فهي صلاة على الدابة، تجوز أي: الفريضة في حالة العذر، ولا تجوز في غير حالة العذر، وإن لم يكن طرف العجلة على الدابة جاز، وهو بمنزلة الصلاة على السرير، كذا في «البحر»، عن «الظهيرية»، وفي «الخلاصة».
Chapter on the prayer of obligatory (fard) and necessary (wajib) on the animal and the howdah. It is not valid on the animal: obligatory prayers nor necessary ones like witr, vowed prayers, and what one began as supererogatory and then spoiled, nor the funeral prayer, nor a prostration for recitation whose verse was recited on the ground, except for necessity, such as fear of a thief for his life, or his animal, or his clothes if he dismounts, fear of a wild beast, mud on the ground, the animal bolting, and not finding someone to mount him due to his inability. And the necessary prayers are like the obligatory. The basis for this is intense fear of the enemy during battle when they cannot pray while dismounted, and similarly other excuses, such as fear of a thief for his life, or his animal, or his clothes if he dismounts and his companions do not stop, fear of a wild beast for his life or his animal, rain, and mud in a place that submerges the face or soils it and ruins what is spread out; mere dampness does not permit that. One who has no animal prays standing in the mud with gestures, as in 'al-Tajnīs wa al-Mazīd'. The animal bolting, and not finding someone to mount his animal even if it is not bolting due to his inability to mount by himself, this is by agreement. He is not required to repeat if he becomes able to dismount, like a sick person who prays with gestures and then recovers. Similarly, if a sick person would suffer increased illness or delayed recovery from dismounting and mounting, it is permissible for him to gesture for the obligatory prayer on the animal while stationary facing the qibla if possible, otherwise as much as possible. He is not required to stop the animal in a state of fear. But if the excuse is only mud and he is able to stop it, it is not valid if it is moving; if he cannot stop it, his prayer is valid. The one incapable of mounting, if he dismounts when he finds someone to mount him, this is the issue of the capable by the capability of another. He is not considered capable according to Imam Abu Hanifa, contrary to the two companions. Upon this, the woman who cannot dismount except with a mahram or husband, from 'al-Fatḥ', 'al-ʿInāyah', 'Miʿrāj al-Dirāyah', 'al-Khāniyyah', 'al-Tabyīn', etc. And the author of 'al-Baḥr' said: I have not seen a ruling when a man is riding opposite to his wife or mahram, and the woman cannot dismount by herself, is it permissible for the man opposite her to pray the obligatory prayer on the animal? Like the woman due to the tilt of the howdah if he dismounts alone, and it should be permissible for him, as is not hidden. End. And prayer in the howdah, which is on the animal, is like prayer on it in the ruling you learned, whether it is moving or stationary. If he stops it and places a plank under the howdah so that its base reaches the ground via the plank, then the howdah becomes like the ground, so the obligatory prayer is valid in it while standing. As for prayer on a carriage: if the edge of the carriage is on the animal and it moves or not, it is prayer on the animal, permissible for the obligatory prayer in an emergency, and not permissible otherwise. If the edge of the carriage is not on the animal, it is permissible, and it is like prayer on a bed. This is in 'al-Baḥr' from 'al-Ẓahīriyyah' and 'al-Khulāṣah'.
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the Hanafi school on the validity of obligatory and necessary prayers (fard and wajib) on an animal or in a howdah (mahmil). The author begins by stating the general rule: it is not valid to perform fard or wajib prayers on an animal, including witr, vowed prayers, and prayers that were spoiled after beginning as supererogatory, as well as funeral prayer and the prostration of recitation (sajdat al-tilawah) if the verse was recited on the ground. The exception is a genuine necessity (darurah), such as fear of a thief for one's life, property, or mount; fear of a wild beast; muddy ground that soaks the face or clothes; the animal bolting; or inability to mount the animal. The proof is derived from the Quranic verse (2:239) which permits prayer on foot or riding when in fear. The author analogizes other excuses to the fear of the enemy, provided the difficulty is severe. Mere dampness does not justify the concession. A person without an animal must pray standing in the mud with gestures. The text then addresses the case of one who is unable to mount without help. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, such a person is not considered capable (qadir) by the ability of another, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the two companions) disagree. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in later sources like al-Fath and al-ʿInayah is that the person is capable and must dismount. The passage also discusses the woman who cannot dismount without a mahram or husband; the ruling for the man opposite her is that it is permissible for him to pray on the animal if dismounting would cause the howdah to tilt and endanger her. Finally, the passage explains that praying in a howdah (mahmil) follows the same ruling as praying on the animal. If a plank is placed under the howdah so it rests on the ground, it becomes like land, and fard prayers are valid while standing. A carriage attached to the animal is treated as the animal itself if any part rests on it; otherwise, it is like a bed and prayers are valid without necessity.

Key Terms
دابة (dābbah): A riding animal, such as a horse, camel, mule, or donkey.
ضرورة (ḍarūrah): A dire necessity that makes permissible what is normally forbidden, such as fear of loss of life, property, or serious hardship.
جموح (jumūḥ): The animal bolting or being unruly and uncontrollable.
إيماء (īmā’): Gestures made instead of bowing and prostrating when unable to perform them physically.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a valid excuse for praying fard on an animal?
A) Fear of a thief
B) Rain that soaks the ground moderately
C) Fear of a wild beast
D) The animal bolting

Key Takeaway
Fard and wajib prayers on an animal are invalid unless a genuine necessity exists, as derived from Quran 2:239.
