Intra-Hanafi Dispute on 'Capable by Another's Ability' and Rulings on Mahmil
Intra-Hanafi dispute on capability through another and subsidiary rulings on mahmil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a person who cannot mount without help and apply the operative ruling according to later authorities.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa said: help from another does not make you capable; the two companions said it does — the mufta bihi follows them.

This passage delves into a specific intra-Hanafi dispute: is a person who cannot mount an animal without assistance considered capable of dismounting for prayer? Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions disagree, and later authorities favour the more lenient view. The passage also covers rulings for the mahmil (howdah) and carriage, providing practical applications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
Recognize that the issue is about 'capable by the ability of another' (al-qadir bi qudrat al-ghayr).
The text mentions this after discussing the sick person.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
He holds that such a person is not considered capable; he must dismount or gesture on the ground.
His principle: ability through another is not one's own ability.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
They hold that if help is available, the person is effectively capable and may pray on the animal.
They emphasize ease and practicality.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
Later authorities like al-Fath and al-ʿInayah adopt the Sahibayn's view.
This is the operative position for fatwa.
5
Apply to mahmil and carriage
Prayer in a howdah follows the same ruling as on the animal; if a plank is placed under it, it becomes like land.
Carriages: if part rests on the animal, it is like the animal; otherwise like a bed.

Chapter on the prayer of obligatory (fard) and necessary (wajib) on the animal and the howdah. It is not valid on the animal: obligatory prayers nor necessary ones like witr, vowed prayers, and what one began as supererogatory and then spoiled, nor the funeral prayer, nor a prostration for recitation whose verse was recited on the ground, except for necessity, such as fear of a thief for his life, or his animal, or his clothes if he dismounts, fear of a wild beast, mud on the ground, the animal bolting, and not finding someone to mount him due to his inability. He is not required to stop the animal in a state of fear. But if the excuse is only mud and he is able to stop it, it is not valid if it is moving; if he cannot stop it, his prayer is valid. Prayer in a Mahmil and Its Stabilization
Ruling on prayer in a mahmil and the effect of stabilizing it to ground.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on prayer in a mahmil, identify when it becomes like the ground, and apply the condition for standing obligatory prayer.

Core Idea
A mahmil on an animal is like the animal unless stabilized to the ground.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah clarifies the ruling of praying in a mahmil (a litter carried by an animal). The general rule is that such prayer follows the ruling of prayer on the animal itself. However, there is a crucial distinction: if the mahmil is supported so that its base rests on the ground, it takes the ruling of the ground, allowing obligatory prayer to be performed standing. The passage also addresses carts and a specific situation from the footnote.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject
Recognize that the passage discusses prayer in a mahmil on an animal. Understand what a mahmil is: a litter carried by an animal.
2
Grasp the general ruling
The base ruling is that prayer in a mahmil is like prayer on the animal itself. This applies whether the animal is moving or stationary.
Thus, all conditions for prayer on an animal apply.
3
Note the stabilization exception
If a piece of wood or similar is placed under the mahmil so that its base rests on the ground, it becomes like the ground. This allows standing obligatory prayer.
The key word is 'qarār' (stability) indicating contact with ground.
4
Understand the cart ruling
The passage extends the ruling to a cart ('ajala): if the cart's pole is on the animal, it is like prayer on the animal; otherwise, it is like prayer on a bed.
5
Analyze the footnote
The footnote addresses a scenario where a man descends alone from the mahmil, causing imbalance. The person remaining is like a woman unable to descend, thus allowed to pray fard on the animal.
This is an expansion (sharh) of the base text.

Source Text

If he places a piece of wood under the mahmil until its base remains on the ground, it becomes like the ground, so obligatory prayer in it while standing is valid. ... On the animal? As for prayer on the cart if the end of the cart is on the animal and it is moving or not, it is prayer on the animal, permissible for obligatory prayer in case of necessity, and not permissible without necessity. Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling of prayer in a mahmil (a litter carried by an animal). The rule is that prayer in a mahmil on an animal is like prayer on the animal itself, whether the animal is moving or stationary. However, if the mahmil is stabilized by placing a piece of wood or similar under it so that its base rests on the ground, it takes the ruling of the ground, and thus obligatory prayer in it while standing is valid. The passage also discusses a cart ('ajala): if the cart's pole is on the animal, it is like prayer on the animal, permissible only with an excuse. If the pole is not on the animal, it is permissible and like prayer on a bed. The footnote explains that if only one person descends from the mahmil, the balance is lost, so the person remaining is like a woman unable to descend, thus allowed to pray the obligatory prayer on the animal.

Key Terms
المَحْمِل (al-mahmil): A litter or carriage carried by an animal, used for travel.
العَجَلَة (al-'ajala): A cart or wheeled vehicle pulled by an animal.
القَرار (al-qarār): Stability, rest; the base of the mahmil resting on the ground.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Prayer in a mahmil is ruled according to whether it is stabilized to the ground or not, affecting the validity of standing obligatory prayer.

Prayer in a Moving Ship: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Dispute on validity of sitting obligatory prayer in a moving ship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi and Sahibayn positions on sitting obligatory prayer in a moving ship, identify the key evidence for each, and explain the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa validates sitting prayer in a moving ship; the Sahibayn require a genuine excuse.

This passage presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute (ikhtilaf) between the founder Imam Abu Hanifa and his two foremost students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. At stake is whether standing (a rukn) can be omitted in a moving ship without a concrete excuse. Understanding this dispute clarifies how the Hanafi school weighs textual commands (amr) against established practice (amal) and the principle of al-ghalib.

Guided Path
1
State the precise dispute
Identify the exact issue: Is it valid to pray an obligatory prayer sitting (without gestures) in a moving ship when one is able to stand and exit? State Abu Hanifa's view (valid) and Sahibayn's view (invalid without excuse).
The dispute is about the default ruling, not about cases with a clear excuse like dizziness.
2
Identify each side's evidence
Find the proofs: Sahibayn rely on the hadith 'Pray in it standing unless you fear drowning' and treat standing as a rukn. Abu Hanifa relies on the practice of Companions Anas and Junada praying sitting, and the principle that the usual (ghalib) is like the certain.
The hadith is ahad and interpreted as recommendation (nadb) by Abu Hanifa.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
Understand how Abu Hanifa rebuts the hadith: the command is carried on the usual occurrence of dizziness, and the companion practice shows the ruling.
The principle 'al-ghalib ka al-muhaqqaq' is central.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: A person without excuse praying sitting – Abu Hanifa says valid but makruh; Sahibayn say invalid (must be repeated).
The text notes that Abu Hanifa's view is strong, though Sahibayn's is called 'al-azhar' (more apparent).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الصلاة في السفينة
صلاة الفرض فيها وهي جاريةٌ، قاعداً بلا عُذرٍ صحيحةً عند أبي حنيفة، بالركوع والسجود. وقالا: لا تصح الا من عدرٍ، وهو الأظهر والعذر: كدَوَرانِ الرّأس، وعدم القدرة على الخروج، ولا تَجُوزُ فيها بالإيماء، اتفاقاً.
فصل في الصلاة في السفينة
(صلاة) مصلي (الفرض)، والواجب ( فيها ) أي : السفينة (وهي جارية) حال كونه (قـاعـداً بــلا عذر)، بأن كان يقدر على القيام والخروج منها (صحيحة، عند الإمام الأعظم (أبي حنيفة) رحمه الله، لكن (بالركوع والسجودِ) لا بالإيماء، لأن الغالب في القيام دوران الرأس، والغالب كالمتحقق، لكن القيام أفضل؛ لأنه أبعد عن شبهة الخلاف، والخروج أفضل إن أمكنه؛ لأنه أسكن لقلبه، كذا قاله الزيلعي، والشيخ أكمل الدين، وقال في ( البحر » عن « البدائع » : صحت، وقد أساء عند أبي حنيفة، انتهى. ومثله في «الفتح»، و « الاختيار ) ، ( وقالا ) أبو يوسف ومحمد رحمهما الله: (لا تصح) جالساً (إلا) من عُذر، وهو الأظهر)؛ لأن القيام ركن، فلا يترك إلا بعذر محقق لا موهوم، كذا في « البرهان»، ولكن قال في مجمع الروايات»: وتجوز الصلاة في السفينة قاعداً في كل حال عنـد أبي حنيفة، وعندهما لا تجوز إلا بعذر؛ لحديث ابن عمرة أنَّ النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم سُئِلَ عَنِ الصَّلاةِ فِي السَّفِينَةِ فَقَالَ: صَلِّ فِيْهَا قَائِمَاً إلا أَنْ تَخَافَ الغَرَقَ (۱) انتهى. وقال الدارقطني: السائل جعفر بن أبـي طالب رضي الله عنه ، لما هاجر إلى الحبشة قاله الديري، ولأبي حنيفة أن ابن سيرين، قال: صلينا مع أنس في السفينة قعوداً، ولو شئنا لخرجنا إلى الجد (۲)، وقال مجاهد : صلينا مع جنادة رضي الله عنه في السفينة ولو شئنا لقمنا ، فوافق صحابيين جنادة وأنس، وتابعيين ابن سيرين ومجاهد، وقال في «شرح الغزنوي» للقدوري: فحمل الأمر على الغالب، وإن كان واحد يخلو منه، كما أن الغالب من أمر السفر مشقة، والغالب من أمر الأبكار الحياء، لا جرم حمل الأمر على الغالب فكذلك هنا. وقال الزاهدي: وحديث ابن عمر وجعفر محمول على الندب. انتهى. فبهذا يظهر قوة قول الإمام أحمد رحمه الله. فيتبع (والعذرُ: كدَوَرانِ الرّأس، وعدم القدرة على الخروج. ولا تَجُوزُ) أي: لا تصح الصلاة (فِيهَا بالإيماء) لمن يقدر على الركوع والسجود (اتّفاقاً ) لفقد المبيح حقيقة وحكماً
Chapter on prayer in a ship. Prayer of the obligatory (prayer) in it while it is moving, sitting without an excuse, is valid according to Abu Hanifa, with bowing and prostration. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: It is not valid except with an excuse, and that is more apparent. The excuse is like dizziness and inability to go out. And it is not permissible in it with gestures, by agreement. Chapter on prayer in a ship. (Prayer) of the one praying (the obligatory) and wajib (in it) i.e., the ship (while it is moving) while he is (sitting without an excuse) meaning he is able to stand and exit from it, (is valid, according to the Greatest Imam Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, but with bowing and prostration, not with gestures, because the usual occurrence when standing is dizziness, and the usual is like the certain, but standing is better because it is further from the suspicion of disagreement, and exiting is better if possible because it is more soothing to his heart. So said al-Zayla'i and Shaykh Akmal al-Din. And in al-Bahr from al-Bada'i': It is valid, and he has done wrong according to Abu Hanifa. End. And similar is in al-Fath and al-Ikhtiyar. (And the two) Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on them, (said: It is not valid) sitting (except with an excuse, and that is more apparent) because standing is a pillar, so it is not abandoned except for a real excuse, not a delusory one. Thus in al-Burhan. But in Majma' al-Riwayat it is said: And prayer in a ship sitting is permissible in every case according to Abu Hanifa, and according to them it is not permissible except with an excuse, due to the hadith of Ibn 'Umar that the Prophet ﷺ was asked about prayer in a ship and said: Pray in it standing unless you fear drowning. End. And al-Daraqutni said: The questioner was Ja'far ibn Abi Talib, may Allah be pleased with him, when he migrated to Abyssinia; al-Dayri said it. And for Abu Hanifa is (the narration) that Ibn Sirin said: We prayed with Anas in the ship sitting, and if we wished we would have gone out to the bank. And Mujahid said: We prayed with Junada, may Allah be pleased with him, in the ship, and if we wished we would have stood. So he agreed with two Companions, Junada and Anas, and two Successors, Ibn Sirin and Mujahid. And in Sharh al-Ghaznawi for al-Quduri: So he carried the command on the usual, even if one is free of it, just as the usual in travel is hardship, and the usual with virgins is shyness; no doubt he carried the command on the usual, and so here. And al-Zahidi said: And the hadith of Ibn 'Umar and Ja'far is carried on recommendation. End. So by this the strength of the statement of Imam Ahmad is apparent. So he follows. (And the excuse: like dizziness and inability to exit. And it is not permissible) i.e., prayer is not valid (in it with gestures) for one who is able to bow and prostrate (by agreement) due to the absence of a permitting cause actually and legally.
Source pages p. 427

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute concerning obligatory prayer in a moving ship. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if a person is able to stand and exit the ship, it is still valid to pray sitting with bowing and prostration, without any excuse. However, the two students (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that such prayer is not valid without an excuse, and their view is considered the more apparent (al-azhar). An excuse includes dizziness or inability to exit. The text then discusses proofs: The Sahibayn cite a hadith where the Prophet (ﷺ) said to pray standing unless one fears drowning. Abu Hanifa's evidence includes the practice of the Companions Anas and Junada praying sitting in a ship when they could have stood, and the principle of taking the usual occurrence (ghalib) as the basis. The text also notes that standing is better and exiting the ship to pray on land is preferable. It concludes that prayer with gestures (ima') for those able to bow and prostrate is invalid by agreement because the permitting cause (travel or illness) is absent.

Key Terms
الغالب (al-ghālib): The usual occurrence; in this context, the likelihood of dizziness when standing on a moving ship.
الإيماء (al-īmā’): Prayer by gestures, e.g., nodding for bowing and prostration, used when unable to do the actual movements.
الركن (al-rukn): An essential pillar of prayer, like standing in obligatory prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which of the following is the 'more apparent' (al-azhar) view regarding obligatory prayer sitting in a moving ship?
A) Abu Hanifa's view that it is valid without excuse.
B) The Sahibayn's view that it is invalid without excuse.
C) The view that only ima' is allowed.
D) The view that it is valid only if the ship is anchored.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has an internal dispute on sitting prayer in a moving ship: Abu Hanifa validates it based on al-ghalib, while the Sahibayn require a real excuse; the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is that one should strive to stand or exit unless genuinely excused.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Sitting in a Moving Ship for Obligatory Prayer
Intra-Hanafi dispute with evidence and tarjih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on praying sitting in a moving ship, identify the evidence each side uses, and apply the ruling to a scenario with an excuse.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa permits sitting without excuse; Sahibayn require a confirmed excuse.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute on whether one may sit during obligatory prayer in a moving ship without an excuse. Understanding this ikhtilaf and its thamarah ill-khilaf is essential for applying the correct ruling in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and dispute
What is being ruled upon? Obligatory prayer in a moving ship, sitting without an excuse. The dispute is whether it is valid or not.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and evidence
Abu Hanifa: valid. Evidence: dominant state (ghalib) of dizziness is like actual; practice of companions Anas and Junada.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and evidence
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: invalid without a confirmed excuse. Evidence: hadith 'Pray standing unless you fear drowning' and standing is a rukn.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response to the Sahibayn's dalil
The hadith is interpreted as recommendation (nadb) due to the dominant hardship; companion practice shows permissibility.
5
Determine the mufta bihi view
The author states the Sahibayn's view is al-azhar (more apparent) but notes the strength of Abu Hanifa's position.

فصل في الصلاة في السفينة

بالإيماء، اتفاقاً.
فصل في الصلاة في السفينة
(صلاة) مصلي (الفرض)، والواجب ( فيها ) أي : السفينة (وهي جارية) حال كونه (قـاعـداً بــلا عذر)، بأن كان يقدر على القيام والخروج منها (صحيحة، عند الإمام الأعظم (أبي حنيفة) رحمه الله، لكن (بالركوع والسجودِ) لا بالإيماء، لأن الغالب في القيام دوران الرأس، والغالب كالمتحقق، لكن القيام أفضل؛ لأنه أبعد عن شبهة الخلاف، والخروج أفضل إن أمكنه؛ لأنه أسكن لقلبه، كذا قاله الزيلعي، والشيخ أكمل الدين، وقال في ( البحر » عن « البدائع » : صحت، وقد أساء عند أبي حنيفة، انتهى. ومثله في «الفتح»، و « الاختيار ) ، ( وقالا ) أبو يوسف ومحمد رحمهما الله: (لا تصح) جالساً (إلا) من عُذر، وهو الأظهر)؛ لأن القيام ركن، فلا يترك إلا بعذر محقق لا موهوم، كذا في « البرهان»، ولكن قال في مجمع الروايات»: وتجوز الصلاة في السفينة قاعداً في كل حال عنــد أبي حنيفة، وعندهما لا تجوز إلا بعذر؛ لحديث ابن عمرة أنَّ النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم سُئِلَ عَنِ الصَّلاةِ فِي السَّفِينَةِ فَقَالَ: صَلِّ فِيْهَا قَائِمَاً إلا أَنْ تَخَافَ الغَرَقَ (۱) انتهى. وقال الدارقطني: السائل جعفر بن أبـي طالب رضي الله عنه ، لما هاجر إلى الحبشة قاله الديري، ولأبي حنيفة أن ابن سيرين، قال: صلينا مع أنس في السفينة قعوداً، ولو شئنا لخرجنا إلى الجد (۳)، وقال مجاهد : صلينا مع جنادة رضي الله عنه في السفينة ولو شئنا لقمنا ، فوافق صحابيين جنادة وأنس، وتابعيين ابن سيرين ومجاهد، وقال في «شرح الغزنوي» للقدوري: فحمل الأمر على الغالب، وإن كان واحد يخلو منه، كما أن الغالب من أمر السفر مشقة، والغالب من أمر الأبكار الحياء، لا جرم حمل الأمر على الغالب فكذلك هنا. وقال الزاهدي: وحديث ابن عمر وجعفر محمول على الندب. انتهى. فبهذا يظهر قوة قول الإمام أحمد رحمه الله. فيتبع (والعذرُ: كدَوَرانِ الرّأس، وعدم القدرة على الخروج. ولا تَجُوزُ) أي: لا تصح الصلاة (فِيهَا بالإيماء) لمن يقدر على الركوع والسجود (اتّفاقاً ) لفقد المبيح حقيقة وحكماً".
سننه
.(٣٩٤/١)
(1) أخرجه الحاكم في المستدرك (٤٠٩/١) ، والدارقطني في (۲) الجد : بالضم شاطئ النهر والجدة أيضاً وبه سميت المدينة التي عند مكة جدة. اللسان / جدد. (۳) قوله: لفقد المبيح حقيقة، أي: هو كالمريض، وحكماً هو كالدابة. ط.
Chapter on Prayer in a Ship. Obligatory prayer in it while it is moving, sitting without excuse is valid according to Abu Hanifa, with bowing and prostration. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: It is not valid except with an excuse, and that is the more apparent. The excuse is like dizziness and inability to exit. And it is not permitted in it with gestures, by agreement. Chapter on Prayer in a Ship: A person praying obligatory (and obligatory) in it, meaning the ship, while it is moving, being seated without excuse, meaning he is able to stand and exit from it, is valid according to the Greatest Imam Abu Hanifa, but with bowing and prostration, not with gestures, because the dominant state in standing is dizziness, and the dominant is like the actual. However, standing is better because it is further from the semblance of disagreement, and exiting is better if possible because it is more calming for his heart. Thus said al-Zayla'i and Shaykh Akmal al-Din. And in al-Bahr from al-Bada'i: It is valid and he has done wrong according to Abu Hanifa. End. Similar in al-Fath and al-Ikhtiyar. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: It is not valid sitting except with an excuse, and that is the more apparent, because standing is a pillar, so it is not abandoned except for a confirmed excuse, not a hypothetical one. Thus in al-Burhan. But in Majma' al-Riwayat: The prayer in a ship sitting is permissible in all circumstances according to Abu Hanifa, and according to them it is not permissible except with an excuse, due to the hadith of Ibn Umar that the Prophet was asked about prayer in a ship and said: Pray in it standing unless you fear drowning. End. And al-Daraqutni said: The questioner was Ja'far ibn Abi Talib when he migrated to Abyssinia, said al-Dayri. And for Abu Hanifa that Ibn Sirin said: We prayed with Anas in a ship sitting, and if we wished we would have gone out to the shore. And Mujahid said: We prayed with Junada in a ship and if we wished we would have stood. So he agreed with two companions, Junada and Anas, and two followers, Ibn Sirin and Mujahid. And in Sharh al-Ghaznawi for al-Quduri: The command is carried on the dominant, even if there is one free from it, just as the dominant in the case of travel is hardship, and the dominant in the case of virgins is shyness. So the command is carried on the dominant, so here. And al-Zahidi said: The hadith of Ibn Umar and Ja'far is carried on recommendation. End. So by this appears the strength of the statement of Imam Ahmad. So follow. And the excuse: like dizziness and inability to exit. And it is not permitted in it with gestures, meaning the prayer is not valid in it with gestures for one who is able to bow and prostrate, by agreement, due to the absence of the permissive cause in reality and in law.
Source pages p. 427

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah addresses the ruling of obligatory prayer in a moving ship. The matn states that according to Abu Hanifa, sitting without an excuse is valid, but only with full ruku and sujud. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that valid only with an excuse, and this is stated as the more apparent (al-azhar) opinion. The sharh then expands: for Abu Hanifa, the basis is that the dominant experience on a moving ship is dizziness, and the dominant is treated as actual; thus, sitting is allowed. However, standing is superior to avoid the semblance of disagreement, and exiting the ship to pray on land is best if possible. For the Sahibayn, standing is a pillar (rukn) and cannot be abandoned except for a confirmed excuse, not a hypothetical one. The text then presents evidence: the Sahibayn rely on the hadith of Ibn Umar where the Prophet commanded standing unless fear of drowning. Abu Hanifa relies on the practice of the companions Anas and Junada, and the followers Ibn Sirin and Mujahid, who prayed sitting in a ship even though they could have stood or exited. The ruling on gestures (ima') is that all agree it is invalid for one able to bow and prostrate, as real gestures are only for the sick, and the ship does not make one exempt from actual actions. The author then notes the strength of Abu Hanifa's view. The definition of excuse (udhr) includes dizziness (dawaran al-ra's) and inability to exit the ship.

Key Terms
عذر (‘udhr): Excuse that permits sitting in a moving ship: dizziness or inability to exit.
إيماء (īmā’): Gestures with head for bowing and prostration instead of actual motions.
غالب (ghālib): Dominant state or prevailing circumstance, treated as actual for legal rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary evidence used by the Sahibayn to require standing in a moving ship?
A) The hadith of Ibn Umar commanding standing unless fear of drowning
B) The practice of Anas and Junada praying sitting
C) The principle that the dominant state of dizziness overrides
D) Consensus of the companions

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has an internal dispute on sitting in a moving ship; the relied-upon view requires a confirmed excuse, but Abu Hanifa's view also has strong support.

Rulings for Prayer in a Ship Tied at Sea or Shore
Rulings for ship tied in deep sea or shore and facing qibla.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings for prayer in a ship tied in deep sea and at shore, and explain the obligation of facing qibla during such prayer.

Core Idea
A ship tied at shore requires standing prayer only if part is on land; facing qibla is a duty whenever able.

This passage addresses three distinct scenarios for prayer on a ship: when it is anchored in deep sea, when it is tied at the shore, and the continuous obligation to face the qibla. The rulings depend on the ship's stability and the worshipper's ability to exit. Understanding these distinctions prevents invalid prayers due to incorrect assumptions about the ship's legal status.

Guided Path
1
Classify the ship's location and movement
Determine whether the ship is in deep sea (lujjah) and strongly moved by wind, or at shore (shatt). This classification triggers different rulings.
A ship in deep sea strongly moved by wind is legally like a moving ship; otherwise like a stationary ship at shore.
2
Apply the ruling for deep-sea ship
If the ship is in deep sea and strongly moved, it follows the ruling of a moving ship (subject to earlier dispute about sitting). If not strongly moved, it is like a stationary ship at shore.
The earlier dispute is not repeated here; this passage references the existing disagreement.
3
Apply the ruling for shore-tied ship
For a ship tied at shore, sitting prayer is invalid by consensus if one can stand. Standing prayer is valid only if part of the ship rests on solid ground (al-mukhtar). If no part is on ground, standing prayer is invalid unless the worshipper cannot exit without harm.
There is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: some allow standing absolutely; the chosen view requires contact with land.
4
Apply the obligation to face qibla
The worshipper must face the qibla at the start of prayer and turn to face it whenever the ship turns, until completing the prayer facing qibla. Failure to do so invalidates the prayer by all views.
This ruling applies to any ship, whether moving or stationary, as long as the worshipper has the ability to turn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمربوطة في لُجَّةِ البحر، وتُحَرِّكُها الرِّيحُ شديداً، كالسائرة. وإلا فكالواقفة على الأصح، وإن كانت مربوطة بالشط لا تجوز صلاته قاعداً، بالإجماع، فإن صلى قائماً، وكان شيء من السفينة على قرار الأرض، صحتِ الصَّلاةُ؛ وإلا فلا تصح على المختار ، إلا إذا لم يمكنه الخروج، ويتوجه المصلّي فيها إلى
القبلة عند افتتاح الصَّلاةِ، وكلّما استدارَتْ عنها يتوجه إليها في خلال الصَّلاةِ، حَتَّى يُتمَّها مُستقبلاً. (والمربوطة في لُجَّةِ) البحر ) بالمراسي والحبال، (وَ) مع ذلك (تُحَرِّكُها الرِّيحُ) تحريكاً شديداً)، هي (كالسَّائِرَةِ) في الحكم على الخلاف الذي قد علمته، وإلأ ) أي لم تحركها شديداً بأن حركتها يسيراً، أو لم تتحرك (فَكَالواقِفَة ) [ بالشط ] ) ( على الأصح)، كذا في ( العناية»، و فتح القدير » ، والواقفة ذكرها مع حكمها بقوله : ( وإن كانت مربوطة بالشَّط، لا تجوز صلاته) فيها (قاعِدَاً) مع قدرته على القيام؛ لانتفاء المقتضي للصحة (بالإجماع) عـلـى الصحيح، وهـو احتراز عن قول بعضهم أنها أيضاً على الخلاف، فإن صلَّى) في المربوطة بالشط (قَائِمَاً، وكان شيء منَ السَّفينة على قرارِ الأرض، صحتِ الصَّلاةُ) بمنزلة الصلاة على السرير، (وإلا ) أي: وإن لم يستقر منها شيء على الأرض، (فَلا تَصحُ) الصلاة فيها، كذا في ( الإيضاح»، و «مجمع الـروايــات»، عن «المصفى»، وهذا ( على المختار) كما في ( المحيط ) ، و ( البدائع؛ لأنها حينئذ كالدابة وظاهر « الهداية»، و « النهاية»، و « الاختيار جواز الصلاة في المربوطة بالشط قائماً مطلقاً، سواء استقرت بالأرض أم لم تستقر بها، إلا إذا لم يمكنه الخروج ) بلا ضرر، فيصلـي فـيـهـا للحرج، ( ويتوجه المصلّي فيها ) أي: السفينة ( إلى القبلة) لقدرته على فرض الاستقبال (عند افتتاح الصَّلاةِ، وكلما استدارت) السفينة ( عَنْهَا) أي: القبلة (يتوجَّهُ) المصلي باستدارته ( إليها ) أي: القبلة (في خلال الصَّلاةِ) وإن عجز يمسك عن الصلاة، كذا في مجمع الروايات»، (حَتَّى) يقدر إلى أن يتمها مُستقبلاً)، ولو ترك الاستقبال لا تجزئه في قولهم جميعاً، كذا في «البحر»، عـــن الإسبيجابي، انتهى. وهو ما أراده الشيخ أكمل الدين بقوله : وينبغي أن يتوجه إلى القبلة كيفما دارت السفينة، سواء كان عند الافتتاح، أو في خلال الصلاة؛ لأن التوجه فرض عند القدرة وهذا قادر، انتهى. لتعليله بأن التوجه فرض إلى آخره.
(۱) أي: مربوطة في بحر عميق متردد الأمواج معجم لغة الفقهاء / لجة /. بتصرف.
(۲) ما بين الحاصرتين ساقط من المخطوط والصواب ما أثبتناه.
And the ship tied in the deep sea, and the wind moves it violently, is like a moving ship. Otherwise it is like a stationary ship, according to the soundest view. And if it is tied at the shore, his prayer sitting is not permissible by consensus. If he prays standing, and something of the ship is on solid ground, his prayer is valid; otherwise it is not valid according to the chosen view, unless he cannot exit. And the worshipper in it faces the qibla at the beginning of the prayer, and whenever it turns away from it, he turns to it during the prayer, until he completes it facing it. (The ship tied in the deep sea) with anchors and ropes, and with that the wind moves it violently, it is like a moving ship in the ruling according to the disagreement you have already learned. Otherwise, if it is not moved violently, but slightly or not moved, it is like a stationary ship tied at the shore, according to the soundest view. Thus in al-'Inaya and Fath al-Qadir. And the stationary ship is mentioned with its ruling by his saying: And if it is tied at the shore, his prayer in it sitting is not permissible while he is able to stand, due to the absence of the cause for validity, by consensus according to the correct view. This is a caution against the saying of some that it is also subject to disagreement. If he prays in the tied-at-shore ship standing, and something of the ship is on solid ground, the prayer is valid, likened to prayer on a bed, otherwise the prayer in it is not valid. Thus in al-Idah and Majma' al-Riwayat from al-Mustafa. And this is the chosen view as in al-Muhit and al-Bada'i, because then it is like an animal. And the apparent view of al-Hidaya, al-Nihaya, and al-Ikhtiyar is the permissibility of prayer in the tied-at-shore ship standing absolutely, whether it rests on the ground or not, except if he cannot exit without harm, then he prays in it for hardship. And the worshipper in it, meaning the ship, faces the qibla because he is able to fulfill the obligation of facing it at the beginning of the prayer, and whenever the ship turns away from it, the worshipper turns to it during the prayer. If unable, he refrains from prayer, thus in Majma' al-Riwayat, until he can complete it facing it. And if he leaves facing the qibla, it does not suffice in all their views, thus in al-Bahr from al-Ispijabi. This is what Shaykh Akmal al-Din intended by saying: He should face the qibla whenever the ship turns, whether at the beginning or during prayer, because facing is a duty when able, and he is able. End. Due to his reasoning that facing is a duty, etc.
Source pages p. 428

Commentary
This passage continues the chapter on prayer in a ship, addressing different scenarios. First, a ship tied in the deep sea (lujjah) that is strongly moved by wind is legally like a moving ship (sa'irah), subject to the earlier dispute about sitting. If not strongly moved (only slight or none), it is like a stationary ship at the shore. A ship tied at the shore: there is consensus that sitting prayer is not allowed if one can stand, because the ship is stable like land. However, if part of the ship is on solid ground, standing prayer is valid. If no part is on ground, the preferred view (al-mukhtar) is that standing prayer is invalid unless he cannot exit (then praying in it is allowed due to hardship). There is also a view that standing is valid absolutely. Finally, facing the qibla: the worshipper must face the qibla at the start of prayer, and if the ship turns, he must turn with it to face the qibla during the prayer, until he finishes facing it. If he leaves facing qibla deliberately, the prayer is invalid by all views. The author emphasizes that facing qibla is a duty (fard) when one has the ability.

Key Terms
لجة (lujjah): Deep sea or ocean with strong waves.
شط (shaṭṭ): Shore or bank of a river/sea.
المختار (al-mukhtār): The chosen or preferred view among multiple Hanafi positions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling for a person who prays standing in a ship tied at the shore when no part of the ship is on solid ground?
A) Prayer is valid because the ship is stationary.
B) Prayer is invalid according to the chosen view.
C) Prayer is valid only if he cannot exit.
D) Prayer is invalid by consensus.

Key Takeaway
The validity of standing prayer in a ship tied at shore depends on whether part of the ship rests on solid ground; facing qibla is an absolute duty for every able worshipper.

Rulings on Praying in a Moored Ship
Detailed ruling on praying in a moored ship, with sub-cases and intra-Hanafi difference.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the rulings for praying in a ship moored in the deep sea versus moored at the shore, and apply the conditions for validity according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A moored ship's prayer ruling depends on location (deep sea vs shore) and contact with land.

Praying on a ship raises unique questions about stability and qiblah. The Hanafi school provides detailed guidance for when a ship is moored (marbutah) – whether in the open sea or tied to the shore. This lesson unpacks the conditions that make the prayer valid and the obligation to face the qiblah continuously. We will explore how the ship's movement and its contact with land affect the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The source divides moored ships into two categories: those moored in the deep sea (lujjat al-bahr) and those moored at the shore (shatt). For each, there are sub-cases based on movement and contact with land.
Pay attention to the key terms: marbutah, lujjah, shatt.
2
Analyze the deep sea moored ship
If the ship is violently moved by wind, it takes the ruling of a moving ship (sa'irah). If not, it is like a stationary ship (waqifah). This is based on earlier discussions of praying on moving vessels.
The ruling for moving ships was covered previously; here it is applied analogously.
3
Analyze the shore moored ship
Praying while sitting on a shore-moored ship is invalid by consensus if one can stand. For standing prayer, validity depends on whether any part of the ship rests on the ground (qarar al-ard). If it does, it is like praying on a bed. If not, it is invalid according to the chosen opinion (mukhtar).
There is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: some authorities (e.g., al-Hidayah) permit standing prayer unconditionally.
4
Consider the exception for exiting
If the worshipper cannot exit the ship without hardship, he may pray in it even if conditions are not met. This is based on the principle of removing hardship (raf' al-haraj).
This applies only when exiting is genuinely difficult.
5
Apply the qiblah ruling
The worshipper must face the qiblah at the start of prayer and adjust every time the ship turns, because facing the qiblah is a condition (shart) when possible. If unable, he should stop praying until able to face it again.
This obligation applies to all scenarios – deep sea and shore – as long as one can orient.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمربوطة في لُجَّةِ البحر، وتُحَرِّكُها الرِّيحُ شديداً، كالسائرة. وإلا فكالواقفة على الأصح، وإن كانت مربوطة بالشط لا تجوز صلاته قاعداً، بالإجماع، فإن صلى قائماً، وكان شيء من السفينة على قرار الأرض، صحتِ الصَّلاةُ؛ وإلا فلا تصح على المختار ، إلا إذا لم يمكنه الخروج، ويتوجه المصلّي فيها إلى القبلة عند افتتاح الصَّلاةِ، وكلّما استدارَتْ عنها يتوجه إليها في خلال الصَّلاةِ، حَتَّى يُتمَّها مُستقبلاً. (والمربوطة في لُجَّةِ) البحر ) بالمراسي والحبال، (وَ) مع ذلك (تُحَرِّكُها الرِّيحُ) تحريكاً شديداً)، هي (كالسَّائِرَةِ) في الحكم على الخلاف الذي قد علمته، وإلأ ) أي لم تحركها شديداً بأن حركتها يسيراً، أو لم تتحرك (فَكَالواقِفَة ) [ بالشط ] ) ( على الأصح)، كذا في ( العناية»، و فتح القدير » ، والواقفة ذكرها مع حكمها بقوله : ( وإن كانت مربوطة بالشَّط، لا تجوز صلاته) فيها (قاعِدَاً) مع قدرته على القيام؛ لانتفاء المقتضي للصحة (بالإجماع) عـلـى الصحيح، وهـو احتراز عن قول بعضهم أنها أيضاً على الخلاف، فإن صلَّى) في المربوطة بالشط (قَائِمَاً، وكان شيء منَ السَّفينة على قرارِ الأرض، صحتِ الصَّلاةُ) بمنزلة الصلاة على السرير، (وإلا ) أي: وإن لم يستقر منها شيء على الأرض، (فَلا تَصحُ) الصلاة فيها، كذا في ( الإيضاح»، و «مجمع الـروايــات»، عن «المصفى»، وهذا ( على المختار) كما في ( المحيط ) ، و ( البدائع؛ لأنها حينئذ كالدابة وظاهر « الهداية»، و « النهاية»، و « الاختيار جواز الصلاة في المربوطة بالشط قائماً مطلقاً، سواء استقرت بالأرض أم لم تستقر بها، إلا إذا لم يمكنه الخروج ) بلا ضرر، فيصلـي فـيـهـا للحرج، ( ويتوجه المصلّي فيها ) أي: السفينة ( إلى القبلة) لقدرته على فرض الاستقبال (عند افتتاح الصَّلاةِ، وكلما استدارت) السفينة ( عَنْهَا) أي: القبلة (يتوجَّهُ) المصلي باستدارته ( إليها ) أي: القبلة (في خلال الصَّلاةِ) وإن عجز يمسك عن الصلاة، كذا في مجمع الروايات»، (حَتَّى) يقدر إلى أن يتمها مُستقبلاً)، ولو ترك الاستقبال لا تجزئه في قولهم جميعاً، كذا في «البحر»، عـــن الإسبيجابي، انتهى. وهو ما أراده الشيخ أكمل الدين بقوله : وينبغي أن يتوجه إلى القبلة كيفما دارت السفينة، سواء كان عند الافتتاح، أو في خلال الصلاة؛ لأن التوجه فرض عند القدرة وهذا قادر، انتهى. لتعليله بأن التوجه فرض إلى آخره.
And [a ship] moored in the deep sea, and the wind moves it violently, is like a moving ship. Otherwise, it is like a stationary ship on the most correct view. If it is moored at the shore, praying in it sitting is not permissible by consensus. If one prays standing, and some part of the ship rests on the ground, the prayer is valid; otherwise it is not valid according to the chosen position. Unless he cannot exit [the ship]. And the worshipper in it faces the qiblah at the start of the prayer, and whenever the ship turns away from it, he turns to face it during the prayer until he completes it facing it.
Source pages p. 428

Commentary
This passage from Imdad Al-Fattah discusses the rulings of praying in a moored ship. The author distinguishes between a ship moored in deep sea (marbutah fi lujjat al-bahr) and one moored at the shore (marbutah bish-shatt). For the deep sea ship, if it is violently moved by wind, it is like a moving ship (sa'irah) and the ruling for praying in it is based on the earlier discussion of moving ships. If it is not violently moved, it is like a stationary ship (waqifah). For a ship moored at the shore, the ruling is more strict: praying while sitting without excuse is invalid by consensus. If one stands and part of the ship touches the ground, prayer is valid; otherwise it is invalid according to the chosen opinion, though some texts permit it absolutely. The passage also emphasizes that the worshipper must face the qiblah and adjust his direction as the ship turns, because facing the qiblah is obligatory when possible.

Key Terms
مربوطة (marbutah): A ship that is moored or tied with ropes or anchors.
لجة (lujjah): The deep part of the sea where the waves are rough.
شط (shatt): The shore or bank of a river or sea where the ship can be near land.
قرار الأرض (qarar al-ard): The solid ground; part of the ship resting on dry land.
مختار (mukhtar): The chosen or preferred opinion in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the chosen (mukhtar) opinion, when is a standing prayer valid on a ship moored at the shore?
A) Always, because the ship is tied and stable.
B) Only if the worshipper sits.
C) Only if part of the ship rests on the ground.
D) Only if the ship is in deep water.

Key Takeaway
A moored ship's prayer validity hinges on two criteria: location (deep sea vs shore) and, for shore-moored ships, physical contact with land; additionally, facing the qiblah must be maintained throughout.

Tarawih Prayer is an Emphasized Sunnah
Defining tarawih and establishing its sunnah status with proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Tarawih prayer and identify the evidence that establishes it as sunnah mu'akkadah.

Core Idea
Tarawih is an emphasized sunnah proven by the Caliphs' practice and the Prophet's hadith.

Tarawih prayer is a special night prayer in Ramadan. While many Muslims perform it, its exact status and number of rak'ahs vary among schools. In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi position that Tarawih is a sunnah mu'akkadah, supported by the practice of the Rightly Guided Caliphs and prophetic narrations. We also clarify a common confusion with the term 'mustahabb' used by Imam al-Quduri.

Guided Path
1
Define 'Tarawih' linguistically and technically
Understand the root meaning (tarwihah = rest) and how it became the name for the four-rak'ah units in Ramadan night prayer.
The term indicates a break between sets of four rak'ahs.
2
State the Hanafi ruling on Tarawih
Identify that the correct view is sunnah mu'akkadah, not mustahabb, based on the resolved consensus.
Emphasized sunnah means the Prophet and Rightly Guided Caliphs consistently performed it.
3
Identify the primary evidence (dalil)
Note the two proofs: (1) The command to follow the Sunnah of the Rightly Guided Caliphs, and (2) The Prophet's hadith: 'I have prescribed for you qiyam Ramadan.'
The practice of 'Umar, 'Uthman, and 'Ali is considered evidence.
4
Resolve the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Recognize that earlier disagreement about mustahabb vs. sunnah was settled by Abu Hanifa's explicit statement via Hasan's narration.
The settled position is from Zahir al-Riwayah.
5
Distinguish between the prayer and the congregation
Understand that the prayer itself is sunnah, but performing it in congregation is mustahabb (recommended), as clarified by Quduri's statement.
Some earlier texts used 'mustahabb' for the congregation, not the prayer itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في صلاة التراويح
التراويح: سنة .
فصل في صلاة التراويح
(۳)
هي جمع ترويحة للنفس، أي: استراحة، وهي في الأصل مصدر بمعنى الاستراحة، سميت بها كل أربع لاستلزامها شرعاً استراحة بعدها بقدرها، كذا في «الفتح»، وقال في «المستصفى»: الترويحة الجلسة في الأصل، ثم سميت الركعات، أي: الأربع التي آخرها الترويحـة بـهـا، كمـا أطلقوا اسم الركوع على الوظيفة التي تقرأ في القيام لما أن آخر تلك الوظيفة الركوع، انتهى. والكلام على التراويح في جملة مواضع، الأول في صفتها وهو قوله: ( التراويح سُنَّةٌ) مؤكدة قال في الهداية » : الأصح أنها سنة لمواظبة الخلفاء الراشدين، قال الكمال: يعني عمر وعثمان وعلياً رضي الله عنهم، وقال : « عَلَيْكُمْ بِسُنَّتِي وَسُنَّةَ الخُلَفَاءِ الرَّاشِدِينَ مِنْ بَعْدِي » ) وقال صلى الله عليه وسلم في حديث: افْتَرَضَ الله عَلَيْكُمْ صِيَامَهُ وسَنَنْتُ لَكُمْ قِيَامَهُ انتهى. وفي ( الخلاصة : وانقطع اختلاف المشايخ في كون التراويح سنة برواية الحسن عن أبي حنيفة أنها سنة، وقال في ( الاختيار » : التراويح سنة مؤكدة، وروى أسد بن عمرو، عن أبي يوسف قال: سألت أبا حنيفة عن التراويح، ومـا فـعـلـه عـمـر رضي الله عنه فقال: التراويح سنة مؤكدة، ولم يخترعه عمر من تلقاء نفسه، ولم يكن فيه مبتدعاً، ولم يأمر به إلا عن أصل لديه، وعهد من رسول الله .. انتهى. ولا ينافيـه قـول القدوري رحمه الله: إنها مستحبة، كما فهمه في ( الهداية » عنه؛ لأنه إنما قال: يستحب أن يجتمع الناس، وهذا يدل على أن اجتماع الناس مستحب، وليس فيه دلالة على أن التراويح مستحبة. وإلى هذا ذهب بعضهم فقال: التراويح سنة، والاجتماع مستحب، كذا في ( العناية»، و « البحر » ، والتحقيق: أن الجماعة سنة، لكن
Chapter on Tarawih prayer. Tarawih: sunnah. ... It is the plural of tarwihah meaning rest. ... The speech on tarawih encompasses several topics: the first is its description, which is his statement: Tarawih is an emphasized sunnah. ... The correct view is that it is sunnah due to the constant practice of the Rightly Guided Caliphs. ... And the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'I have prescribed for you the standing of the night (qiyam).' ... The disagreement among the scholars ended with the narration from Hasan from Abu Hanifa that it is sunnah. ... The investigation is that the congregation (jama'ah) is sunnah.
Source pages p. 429

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on Tarawih prayer. It first gives a linguistic analysis: 'tarawih' is the plural of 'tarwihah', meaning rest, because after every four rak'ahs there was a rest. Then it states the legal ruling: Tarawih is an emphasized sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah). The author cites several evidences: the practice of the Rightly Guided Caliphs (Umar, Uthman, Ali) as the Prophet commanded to follow them; the hadith in which the Prophet said 'I have prescribed for you the standing of the night (qiyam Ramadan)'; and the direct statement of Abu Hanifa through reliable chains. The text also resolves an apparent contradiction with Quduri's statement that it is 'mustahabb' (recommended), explaining that Quduri meant the gathering (jama'ah) is mustahabb, not the prayer itself. Thus, Tarawih itself is sunnah, but performing it in congregation is mustahabb. The final note clarifies that the congregation is sunnah.

Key Terms
التراويح (al-tarawih): The night prayer in Ramadan, consisting of 20 rak'ahs, with rests every four rak'ahs.
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah mu'akkadah): An emphasized sunnah that the Prophet and the Rightly Guided Caliphs consistently performed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the status of the Tarawih prayer in the Hanafi school according to this passage?
A) Wajib
B) Sunnah mu'akkadah
C) Mustahabb
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Tarawih is an emphasized sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah) in the Hanafi school, established by the practice of the Rightly Guided Caliphs and prophetic hadith, with congregation being mustahabb.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Tarawih is Sunnah Mu'akkadah; Congregation is Sunnah Kifayah
Ruling on the legal status of Tarawih prayer and its congregation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Tarawih prayer and its congregation, and distinguish between sunnah 'ayn and sunnah kifayah.

Core Idea
Tarawih is sunnah mu'akkadah for all; its congregation is a collective sunnah, not individually required.

This lesson unpacks the precise legal status of Tarawih prayer—often misunderstood as optional or restricted. The Hanafi school classifies it as a confirmed sunnah for both men and women, and its congregation as a collective sunnah (kifayah). Understanding this distinction affects how communities prioritize congregational Tarawih.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Tarawih prayer itself is sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah) for both men and women. Determine what is being ruled upon.
The ruling applies to men and women equally.
2
Locate the dalil
The Prophet (ﷺ) performed Tarawih in congregation and encouraged it. His action and statement establish its sunnah status.
Dalil: fi'l and qawl of the Prophet.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action is not continuous (he stopped fearing it becomes fard). In Hanafi usul, fi'l + qawl without obligation indicates sunnah mu'akkadah.
Lack of continuous practice does not negate sunnah status.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some Rawafid claimed it is only for men or that it is a sunnah of Umar. The Hanafi response: it is the Prophet's sunnah for both.
Also other schools differ on number of rak'ahs.
5
Distinguish the congregation ruling
Congregation for Tarawih is sunnah kifayah, not sunnah 'ayn. Evidence: many companions (Ibn Umar, etc.) prayed it at home.
Sunnah kifayah means if some perform it, the obligation on the community is fulfilled.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على الرجال والنساء. وصلاتها بالجماعة سنَّةُ كِفاية، ووقتها بعد صلاة العشاء.. (†) على [ وجه ] الكفاية، كما سنذكره، بخلاف نفس الصلاة فإنها سنة عين مؤكدة (على الرجال والنساء ) قال الديري في ( شرحه » : قال بعض الروافض سنة الرجال دون النساء، وقال بعضهم: هي سنة عمره، والصحيح أنها سنة النبي الا الله للرجال والنساء (). انتهى. ثبتت سنيتها بفعله صلى الله عليه وسلم وقوله، والثاني في حكم الجماعة فيها أشار إليه بقوله: ( وصلاتها بالجماعة سنَّةُ) لما ثبت أنه صلى الله عليه وسلم صلاهـا بالجماعة » (۳) على سبيل التداعي، ولم يجرها مجرى سائر النوافل، وإنما عدم المواظبة للعذر الذي بينه وهو خشيته افتراضها علينا، لكن الجماعة سنة ( كفايةٍ ) قال في ( المبسوط» : لو صلى إنسان في بيته لا يأثم، فقد فعله ابن عمر، وعروة وسالم، والقاسم، وإبراهيم، ونافع ، فدل فـعـل هـؤلاء أن الجماعة في المسجد سنة على سبيل الكفاية، إذ لا يظن بابن عمر ومن تبعـه تـرك السنة انتهى. فلا لوم على من لم يحضر الجماعة، إلا أن يتركوها جميعاً، أو يكون فقيهاً يقتدى به، وفي البزازية » : قال الصدر الشهيد الجماعة سنة كفاية فيها، حتى لو أقامها البعض في ا بجماعة، وباقي أهل المحلة أقامها منفرداً في بيته لا يكون تاركاً للسنة؛ لأنه يروى عن أفراد الصحابة التخلف، وقال الإمام ظهير الدين يكون تاركاً للسنة لأنه سنة على الكل، والكل مختارون، وإن صلاها بجماعة في بيته، فالصحيح أنه نال إحدى الفضيلتين، فإن الأداء في المسجد لـه فضيلة ليس للأداء في البيت ذلك، وكذا الحكم في المكتوبة. انتهى.
For men and women. And its prayer in congregation is a sunnah of sufficiency, and its time is after Isha prayer... (†) on the [basis of] sufficiency, as we will mention, unlike the prayer itself, for it is an emphasized sunnah in person (for men and women). Al-Dayri said in his commentary: Some of the Rawafid said it is sunnah for men only, and some said it is the sunnah of Umar (رضي الله عنه), but the correct view is that it is the sunnah of the Prophet (ﷺ) for men and women. End. Its sunnah status is established by his (ﷺ) action and his statement. The second matter is the ruling of congregation in it, which he indicated by his saying: (And its prayer in congregation is a sunnah) because it is established that he (ﷺ) prayed it in congregation (3) as a mutual encouragement, and he did not make it like other supererogatory prayers. The lack of continuous practice was due to the excuse he mentioned, which was his fear that it would be made obligatory upon us. However, congregation is a sunnah (of sufficiency). Al-Mabsut says: If a person prays in his house, he does not sin, for Ibn Umar, Urwa, Salim, Al-Qasim, Ibrahim, and Nafi' did that. So their action indicates that congregation in the mosque is a sunnah on the basis of sufficiency, as it is not assumed that Ibn Umar and his followers would abandon the sunnah. End. So there is no blame on one who does not attend the congregation, unless they all abandon it, or if he is a jurist who is followed. And in Al-Bazzaziyyah: Al-Sadr al-Shahid said: Congregation in it is a sunnah of sufficiency, such that if some people hold it in a congregation in the mosque and the rest of the people of the neighborhood pray individually in their homes, they are not considered abandoners of the sunnah, because it is narrated that some individual companions stayed away. And Imam Zahir al-Din said: He becomes an abandoner of the sunnah because it is a sunnah upon all, and all are free to choose, but if he prays it in a congregation in his house, the correct view is that he attains one of the two virtues; for performing it in the mosque has a virtue that performance at home does not have. Similarly, the ruling applies to the obligatory prayers. End.
Source pages p. 430

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the legal status of Tarawih prayer and the ruling on praying it in congregation. The author first establishes that Tarawih is an emphasized sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah) for both men and women, refuting the erroneous views of some Rawafid who claimed it is only for men or that it is the sunnah of Umar. The sunnah status is proven by the Prophet's action and statement. Then, the author explains that praying Tarawih in congregation is a sunnah kifayah (collective sunnah), meaning it is commendable for some to perform it in congregation, but if some pray individually, they are not sinful. This is supported by the actions of many companions who prayed it at home. However, if all people of a locality abandon the congregational prayer, or if a leading scholar abandons it, they are blameworthy. The commentary from Al-Bazzaziyyah further clarifies that if some pray in the mosque in congregation and others pray individually at home, the latter are not considered abandoners of the sunnah, though praying in congregation in the mosque carries greater virtue, just as in obligatory prayers.

Key Terms
صلاة التراويح (Salat al-Tarawih): The special night prayer of Ramadan, consisting of twenty rak'ahs.
سنة كفاية (Sunnah Kifayah): A sunnah that is fulfilled if some perform it; if all abandon it, they are blameworthy.
سنة عين (Sunnah 'Ayn): A sunnah recommended for every individual.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling of congregation for Tarawih in the Hanafi school?
A) Sunnah mu'akkadah individually
B) Sunnah kifayah
C) Fard Kifayah
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Tarawih is a confirmed sunnah for all; its congregation is a collective sunnah, not individually binding.

Time of Tarawih and Its Dependency on Isha
Ruling on the time of Tarawih and its subsidiary rules

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the correct time for Tarawih according to the Hanafi school, explain the dependency of Tarawih on Isha, and identify the preferred time to pray it.

Core Idea
Tarawih's time is after Isha until Fajr; its validity depends on a valid Isha.

In this passage, the author explains the time window for Tarawih prayer and clarifies a common misunderstanding about when it can be performed. You will learn the Hanafi school's relied-upon ruling, including an important principle: Tarawih is dependent on Isha, so if Isha is invalid, Tarawih must be repeated. The passage also covers the recommended time to delay Tarawih and the order of Witr and Tarawih.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core time ruling
The text states that the correct view is that Tarawih time is after Isha until Fajr. Note the ikhtilaf: Ismail al-Zahid held the entire night.
The majority of Bukhara scholars support after Isha until Fajr.
2
Understand the tab'iyyah principle
Tarawih is dependent on Isha. The scenario: if Isha is later found invalid, the Tarawih prayed after it does not count and must be repeated.
Witr is not dependent on Isha, so it is not repeated.
3
Determine the order of Witr and Tarawih
Both orders are valid: Witr before Tarawih or after. Delaying Witr until after Tarawih is better.
This is because Tarawih is dependent on Isha, not on Witr.
4
Recognize the recommended time for Tarawih
It is recommended to delay Tarawih until near the first third or half of the night. Delaying beyond half is not disliked according to the correct view, but it is better not to delay that much to avoid missing the time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والثالث: (وَقْتُهَا) ما (بعد صلاة العشاء) على الصحيح إلى طلوع الفجر. وقال جماعة من أصحابنا، منهم: إسماعيل الزاهد: إن الليل كله وقت لهـا قبل العشاء وبعده، وقبل الوتر وبعده، لأنها قيام الليل. وقال عامة مشایخ بخاری وقتها ما بين ا والوتر وهو الصحيح، حتى لو تبين فساد العشاء دون الوتر والتراويح، أعادوا العشاء ثم التراويح دون الوتر عند أبي حنيفة، لأنها تبع للعشاء، فتكون التي فعلها بعد فساد العشاء نافلة مطلقة ليست واقعة عن التراويح، لكونها ليست في محلها فتعاد أي تصلى في موضعها، كما في « التبيين»، و الهداية»، و«الفتح» و « العناية»، ويصح تقديم الوتر على التراويح)، لأنها تبع للعشاء لا للوتر، (و) كذا يصح ( تأخيرُه) أي الوتر ( عَنْهَا ) أي: التراويح وهو الأفضل. (و) الرابع: أنـه (يُسْتَحَبُّ تَأخِيرُ التراويح إلى قبيل ( ثلث الليل، أو) قبيل (نصفـه)، واختلفوا في أدائـهـا بـعـد النصف. فقال بعضهم: يكره لأنها تبع للعشاء، فصارت كسنة العشاء، (وَ) قال بعضهم: (لا يكره تأخيرها إلى ما بعده أي ما بعد نصف الليل على الصحيح؛ لأنها وإن كانت تبعاً للعشاء لكنها صلاة الليل، والأفضل فيها آخره، فلا يكره تأخير ما هو من صلاة الليل إلى آخره، ولكن الأحب أن لا يؤخرها إليه خشية الفوات.
And the third: (Its time) is (after Isha prayer) according to the correct view, until the break of dawn. And a group of our companions, among them Ismail al-Zahid, said: The entire night is time for it, before Isha and after it, and before Witr and after it, because it is night prayer. And the generality of the scholars of Bukhara said: Its time is between Isha and Witr, and that is correct, so much so that if the Isha prayer is found to be invalid while Witr and Tarawih are not, they should repeat Isha then Tarawih, but not Witr, according to Abu Hanifa, because Tarawih is dependent on Isha, so what was performed after the invalid Isha is an absolute supererogatory prayer, not counting as Tarawih, because it was not in its proper place; hence it is repeated, i.e., prayed in its proper place, as in Al-Tabyin, Al-Hidayah, Al-Fath, and Al-Inayah. And it is valid to perform Witr before Tarawih, because Tarawih is dependent on Isha, not on Witr, and likewise it is valid to delay it (i.e., Witr) after it (i.e., Tarawih), and that is better. And the fourth: That it is recommended to delay Tarawih until near the first third of the night, or near its half, and they differed concerning performing it after the half. Some said: It is disliked because it is dependent on Isha, so it becomes like the sunnah of Isha. And some said: It is not disliked to delay it until after that, i.e., after half the night, according to the correct view, because although it is dependent on Isha, it is night prayer, and the best part of it is its latter part, so delaying what is part of night prayer to its latter part is not disliked, but it is preferable not to delay it to that extent out of fear of missing it.
Source pages p. 430

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling on the time of Tarawih prayer. The correct view in the Hanafi school is that the time for Tarawih begins after Isha prayer and extends until the break of dawn. There is an ikhtilaf within the school: Ismail al-Zahid held that the entire night is time, but the majority of Bukhara scholars and the relied-upon position restrict it to after Isha until Fajr. The passage also discusses a scenario: if Isha is later found invalid, the Tarawih prayed after it does not count as Tarawih (since it followed an invalid Isha), and must be repeated; but Witr is not repeated because it is not dependent on Isha. The author then rules on the order of Witr and Tarawih: both are valid, but delay Witr after Tarawih is better. Finally, the preferred time to pray Tarawih is near the first third or half of the night. Delaying beyond half is not disliked according to the correct view, though it is better not to delay that much to avoid missing the time entirely.

Key Terms
وقت التراويح (Waqt al-Tarawih): The time for Tarawih begins after Isha and ends at Fajr.
تراويح تبع للعشاء (Tarawih tab' lil-'Isha): Tarawih is dependent on Isha; its validity requires a valid Isha preceding it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the correct time for Tarawih according to the majority of Hanafi scholars?
A) After Isha until Fajr
B) After Maghrib
C) All night
D) Only in the last third

Key Takeaway
Tarawih's time is after Isha until Fajr, and its validity depends on a valid Isha preceding it.

The Twenty Rak'ahs of Tarawih: Evidence from the Caliphs' Practice
Ruling on the number of rak'ahs in Tarawih prayer and its evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the number of Tarawih rak'ahs and explain the evidence from the consensus of the Rightly Guided Caliphs.

Core Idea
Tarawih is twenty rak'ahs, established by the consensus of the Rightly Guided Caliphs.

This passage clarifies a point of common confusion about Tarawih prayer. Many assume it must be limited to the Prophet's reported practice of eleven rak'ahs. The Hanafi ruling, based on the action of the caliphs Umar, Uthman, and Ali, establishes twenty rak'ahs as the sunnah. We will examine the evidence and understand why twenty is the relied-upon number.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The number of rak'ahs in Tarawih prayer. The ruling is that it is twenty rak'ahs.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? The practice of the Rightly Guided Caliphs (Umar, Uthman, Ali) as reported by al-Bayhaqi in a sound chain. This is treated as ijma (consensus).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does this prove the ruling? The caliphs' practice is considered a binding sunnah in the Hanafi school; the report shows continuous and agreed-upon action, establishing it as normative.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
What opposing evidence exists? Some point to the Prophet's own practice of 11 rak'ahs (including witr) and a weak narration that he prayed 20 without witr. The Hanafi response is that the 11 was before the ruling became established, and the 20 narration is weak.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Which position is relied upon? The practice of the caliphs is given precedence due to its status as sunnah of the Rightly Guided Caliphs and consensus; the mufta bihi is twenty rak'ahs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَ) الخامس: في كمية أي عدد ركعاتها (هي عشرون ركعة) لما روى البيهقي بإسناد صحيح أنهم كانوا يقومون على عَهْدِ عمر رضي الله عنه بعشرين ركعة، وعلى عهد عثمان وعلي بمثله، فصار إجماعاً، كذا في « التبيين». وقال الكمال: كونها عشرين ركعة سنة الخلفاء الراشدين، والذي فعله النبي له بالجماعة إحدى عشرة بالوتر (۳)، وما روي أنه عـلـيـه الصـلاة والسلام كان يصلي في رمضان عشرين ركعة سوى الوتر ) (۳) ، فضعيف ، انتهى. يشير به إلى مثل مــا قال في ( العناية ) : روى أنه خَرَجَ لَيْلَةٌ مِنْ لَيَالِي رَمَضَانَ وَصَلَّى عِشْرِينَ رَكْعَةً، فَلَمَّا كَانَتِ الليلَةُ الثَّانِيَةِ اجْتَمَعَ النَّاسُ، فَخَرَجَ وَصَلَّى بِهِمْ عِشْرِينَ رَكْعَةً، فَلَمَّا كَانَتِ الليلَةُ الثَّالِثَةُ كَثُرَ النَّاسُ، فَلَم يَخْرُجُ وَقَالَ: عَرَفْتُ اجْتِمَاعَكُمْ لَكِنِّي خَشِيْتَ أنْ تُكتَبَ عَلَيْكُمْ ) . فكان الناس يصلونها فرادى إلى زمن عمر، فقال عمر رضي الله عنه: إني أريد أن أجمع الناس على إمام واحد، فجمعهم على أُبي بـن کعبه فصلى بهم خمس ،ترویحات عشرین ركعة (). انتهى. والحكمة في تقديرها بعشرين ركعة؛ لتوافق الفرائض الاعتقادية والعملية، فإنها مع الوتر عشرون ركعة، ولكون السنن شرعت مكملات للواجب فتقع المساواة بين المكمِّل والمكمل، كذا في مجمع الروايات» و«شرح المنية».
And the fifth: Concerning the quantity, i.e., the number of its rak'ahs (it is twenty rak'ahs) because al-Bayhaqi narrated with a sound chain that they used to pray twenty rak'ahs during the time of Umar (رضي الله عنه), and during the time of Uthman and Ali similarly, so it became a consensus. Thus in Al-Tabyin. And Al-Kamal said: That it is twenty rak'ahs is the sunnah of the Rightly Guided Caliphs, and what the Prophet (ﷺ) did with the congregation was eleven rak'ahs including Witr (3), and what has been narrated that he (ﷺ) used to pray twenty rak'ahs in Ramadan apart from Witr (3) is weak. End. He (the author) indicates by this what is said in Al-Inayah: It is narrated that he (ﷺ) went out one night in Ramadan and prayed twenty rak'ahs, and on the second night the people gathered, and he went out and prayed twenty rak'ahs with them, and on the third night many people gathered, but he did not go out and said: 'I knew of your gathering but I feared that it would be made obligatory upon you.' So the people used to pray it individually until the time of Umar. Then Umar (رضي الله عنه) said: 'I want to gather the people behind one imam.' So he gathered them behind Ubayy ibn Ka'b, and he led them in five Tarwihas (i.e., twenty rak'ahs). End. And the wisdom in prescribing it as twenty rak'ahs is to correspond with the obligatory prayers both in belief and practice, for with Witr it becomes twenty rak'ahs, and because supererogatory acts are legislated to complete the obligatory ones, so equality is achieved between the completer and the completed, as in Majma' al-Riwayat and Sharh al-Munyah.
Source pages p. 431

Commentary
This passage establishes the number of rak'ahs in Tarawih prayer as twenty. The proof is the consensus of the Companions during the caliphates of Umar, Uthman, and Ali, as reported by al-Bayhaqi. Al-Kamal notes that twenty rak'ahs is the sunnah of the Rightly Guided Caliphs; the Prophet (ﷺ) prayed eleven rak'ahs in congregation (including Witr), but the narration that he prayed twenty rak'ahs apart from Witr is weak. The wisdom behind twenty rak'ahs is to match the total number of obligatory prayers (which are seventeen) plus Witr (three) making twenty, symbolizing completion. The practice of the Caliphs became the established norm.

Key Terms
عشرون ركعة (Ishrun rak'ah): Twenty rak'ahs for Tarawih prayer.
سنة الخلفاء الراشدين (Sunnat al-Khulafa' al-Rashidin): The practice of the first four Caliphs, which is a source of legislation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the number of rak'ahs in Tarawih prayer?
A) 8
B) 11
C) 20
D) 36

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on Tarawih is twenty rak'ahs, established by the consensus of the Rightly Guided Caliphs and supported by the wisdom of matching the total obligatory prayers.

Recommended Time for Tarawih Prayer
Ruling on recommended time for Tarawih with expansion on disagreement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the preferred time for Tarawih and explain why delaying it beyond half the night is not disliked.

Core Idea
Tarawih is a night prayer; delaying it until the third or half of the night is recommended, but delaying further is not disliked.

The timing of Tarawih prayer is a matter of flexibility in the Hanafi school. While it is recommended to delay it until the first third or half of the night, there is a difference of opinion about praying it later. This lesson clarifies the correct view and the reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the summary ruling
The passage begins by stating that it is recommended (yustahab) to delay Tarawih until the first third of the night or until half of it. Note the terminology: 'recommended' indicates a preferred but not obligatory time.
The recommendation is a sunnah, not a wajib.
2
Recognize the disagreement
After the summary, the passage expands by noting that scholars differed about delaying Tarawih beyond the middle of the night. Some considered it makruh (disliked) because Tarawih is tied to Isha like its sunnah.
The sunnah of Isha is best performed immediately after Isha.
3
Understand the two positions
One group argued that since Tarawih follows Isha, it should be prayed soon after, like the rawatib sunnah. The other group argued that Tarawih is a night prayer (salat al-layl), and the best part of the night for voluntary prayers is the latter portion.
Both positions are based on analogy but reach different conclusions.
4
Determine the correct view
The author declares that the correct view (al-sahih) is that it is NOT disliked to delay Tarawih beyond half the night, because it is a night prayer. However, it is still more beloved (ahab) not to delay it that much out of fear of missing it.
The 'correct view' is what the Hanafi mufta bihi position relies on.
5
Apply the ruling
Practically, a person can pray Tarawih anytime before Fajr, but the best time is between Isha and the middle of the night. If one delays it until the last third, it is still valid and not disliked, though caution is advised.
This flexibility accommodates those who pray tahajjud later.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويُسْتَحَبُّ تَأخيرُ التَّراويح إلى ثُلُثِ اللَّيلِ، أو نصفه، ولا يُكره تأخيرها إلى ما بعده، على الصحيح. ويُسْتَحَبُّ تَأخِيرُ التراويح إلى قبيل ثلث الليل، أو قبيل نصفه، واختلفوا في أدائها بعد النصف. فقال بعضهم: يكره لأنها تبع للعشاء، فصارت كسنة العشاء، وقال بعضهم: لا يكره تأخيرها إلى ما بعده أي ما بعد نصف الليل على الصحيح؛ لأنها وإن كانت تبعاً للعشاء لكنها صلاة الليل، والأفضل فيها آخره، فلا يكره تأخير ما هو من صلاة الليل إلى آخره، ولكن الأحب أن لا يؤخرها إليه خشية الفوات.
And it is recommended to delay Tarawih until the third of the night, or half of it, and it is not disliked to delay it beyond that, according to the correct view. And it is recommended to delay Tarawih until shortly before the third of the night, or shortly before its half. And they differed regarding performing it after the half. Some said it is disliked because it is a follow-up to Isha, so it becomes like the sunnah of Isha. And some said: it is not disliked to delay it beyond that (i.e., beyond half the night) according to the correct view; because even though it is a follow-up to Isha, it is a night prayer, and the best time for night prayer is its end, so it is not disliked to delay what is of the night prayer to its end. But it is more beloved not to delay it to that time out of fear of missing it.
Source pages p. 431

Commentary
This passage explains the recommended time for Tarawih. The author first states the summary: it is recommended to delay Tarawih until the first third or half of the night. Then he expands: there is a difference of opinion about delaying it beyond the middle of the night. Some scholars say it becomes makruh (disliked) because Tarawih is a sunnah that follows Isha, like the rawatib sunnah of Isha, which is best performed immediately after Isha. However, the correct position (al-sahih) is that it is not disliked to delay it even after the middle of the night, because Tarawih is essentially a night prayer (salat al-layl), and the best time for night prayer is the latter part of the night. Nonetheless, it is preferable not to delay it that much out of concern that one may miss it entirely (due to oversleeping etc.). The Hanafi school thus gives flexibility while encouraging early performance.

Key Terms
مكروه (makruh): A disliked action; if makruh tanzihi, it is better to avoid but not sinful.
السنة العشاء (sunnah al-isha): The confirmed sunnah (rawatib) prayed after Isha prayer.
صلاة الليل (salat al-layl): Night prayer, which includes tahajjud and is most virtuous in the last third of the night.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct view in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on delaying Tarawih beyond the middle of the night?
A) It is haram
B) It is makruh tahrimi
C) It is not disliked
D) It is mustahab

Key Takeaway
Tarawih is a night prayer; delaying it beyond half the night is not disliked, though early performance is recommended.

Ruling on Placing Witr Before or After Tarawih
Permissibility and preference regarding Witr and Tarawih order

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the order of Witr and Tarawih and identify the preferred sequence.

Core Idea
Witr can be prayed before or after Tarawih, but the preferred order is after Tarawih.

This lesson addresses a common question during Ramadan: may one pray Witr before joining the Tarawih congregation, or must it be after? The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling with a simple reason. Understanding this ruling ensures that one acts according to the preferred practice while knowing that flexibility exists.

Guided Path
1
Identify the permissible options
Read the text and note that both placing Witr before Tarawih and delaying it after Tarawih are valid.
The text uses 'yashu' (it is permissible) for both.
2
Understand the reasoning
The text explains that Tarawih is a follow-up (taba‘) to the Isha prayer, not to Witr. Therefore, Witr is independent and not bound to precede Tarawih.
This reasoning is from the commentary (sharh), not the matn.
3
Identify the preferred order
The text explicitly states that delaying Witr after Tarawih is preferable (al-afdal). This is the mufta bihi position.
Even though both are valid, following the sunnah is encouraged.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويصح تقديم الوتر على التراويح، وتأخيره عنها. ويصح تقديم الوتر على التراويح)، لأنها تبع للعشاء لا للوتر، (و) كذا يصح ( تأخيرُه) أي الوتر ( عَنْهَا ) أي: التراويح وهو الأفضل.
And it is permissible to pray Witr before Tarawih, and to delay it after them. And it is permissible to put Witr before Tarawih because Tarawih is a follow-up to Isha, not to Witr. And similarly it is permissible to delay it (i.e., Witr) after them (i.e., Tarawih), and that is preferable.
Source pages p. 431

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the timing of Witr in relation to Tarawih prayer. The author states that it is valid to pray Witr before Tarawih, and also valid to pray it after Tarawih. The reason given is that Tarawih is linked to the Isha prayer, not to Witr, so Witr is independent. However, the preferred (afdal) order is to pray Witr after Tarawih. This is a straightforward ruling from the Hanafi school, with no proof cited here as it is a statement from the matn.

Key Terms
الوتر (al-witr): The odd-numbered prayer performed after night prayers, typically one rak'ah but may be three or more in Hanafi school.
التراويح (al-tarawih): Supererogatory night prayers performed in congregation during Ramadan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) It is permissible but Makruh
C) It is permissible, but delaying Witr after Tarawih is better
D) Witr must always be prayed after Tarawih

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, it is permissible to pray Witr before or after Tarawih, but the preferred and recommended order is to delay Witr until after Tarawih.

Evidence for Twenty Rak'ahs in Tarawih
Establishing Tarawih as twenty rak'ahs with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the primary evidence for twenty rak'ahs in Tarawih and explain how the Prophet's own practice does not contradict this.

Core Idea
Tarawih's twenty rak'ahs rest on the consensus of the Companions, not merely the Prophet's personal prayer.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi proof for the number of rak'ahs in Tarawih. You will see why the school relies on the practice of the Rightly Guided Caliphs and how it reconciles the Prophetic tradition of praying eleven rak'ahs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Claim
State clearly that the Hanafi position is that Tarawih consists of twenty rak'ahs, prayed in sets of two.
This is stated at the start of the passage.
2
Examine the Primary Evidence
Read the narration from al-Bayhaqi that the Companions prayed twenty rak'ahs during the caliphates of Umar, Uthman, and Ali. Understand that this widespread, continued practice constitutes consensus (ijma').
The chain is sound (sahih).
3
Address the Counter-Evidence
Consider the hadith that the Prophet prayed eleven rak'ahs (including Witr) in congregation. The Hanafi response distinguishes between the Prophet's personal practice (which he abandoned to avoid obligation) and the later established sunnah of the caliphs.
The narration of twenty rak'ahs by the Prophet is considered weak.
4
Understand the Wisdom
Reflect on the stated wisdom: twenty rak'ahs correspond to the total daily obligatory and witr rak'ahs, symbolizing completeness.
This is a metaphysical justification.
5
Synthesize the Position
Combine the evidence: the clear practice of the four caliphs, the consensus of the Companions, and the weak nature of contrary reports lead to the Hanafi view.
This position is mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهي: عشرون ركعة . وروى البيهقي بإسناد صحيح أنهم كانوا يقومون على عهد عمر رضي الله عنه بعشرين ركعة، وعلى عهد عثمان وعلي بمثله، فصار إجماعاً، كذا في « التبيين». وقال الكمال: كونها عشرين ركعة سنة الخلفاء الراشدين، والذي فعله النبي له بالجماعة إحدى عشرة بالوتر، وما روي أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام كان يصلي في رمضان عشرين ركعة سوى الوتر، فضعيف. وروى أنه خرج ليلة من ليالي رمضان وصلى عشرين ركعة، فلما كانت الليلة الثانية اجتمع الناس فخرج وصلى بهم عشرين ركعة، فلما كانت الليلة الثالثة كثر الناس فلم يخرج وقال: عرفت اجتماعكم لكني خشيت أن تكتب عليكم. والحكمة في تقديرها بعشرين ركعة؛ لتوافق الفرائض الاعتقادية والعملية، فإنها مع الوتر عشرون ركعة، ولكون السنن شرعت مكملات للواجب فتقع المساواة بين المكمِّل والمكمل.
And they (Tarawih) are twenty rak'ahs. Al-Bayhaqi narrated with a sound chain that they used to pray twenty rak'ahs in the time of Umar (may Allah be pleased with him), and in the time of Uthman and Ali similarly, so it became a consensus. Al-Kamal said: its being twenty rak'ahs is the sunnah of the Rightly Guided Caliphs. What the Prophet (peace be upon him) did in congregation was eleven rak'ahs including Witr. And what is narrated that he used to pray twenty rak'ahs in Ramadan besides Witr is weak. And it is narrated that he went out one night of Ramadan and prayed twenty rak'ahs. Then on the second night, the people gathered and he went out and prayed with them twenty rak'ahs. On the third night, the people increased and he did not come out, saying: 'I knew of your gathering but I feared that it would be made obligatory upon you.' The wisdom in setting it as twenty rak'ahs is to correspond to the fundamental beliefs and actions; for they (Tarawih) with Witr become twenty rak'ahs, and because supererogatory acts are prescribed as complements to the obligatory, so equality occurs between the completer and the completed.
Source pages p. 431

Commentary
This passage provides the evidence for the Hanafi position that Tarawih is twenty rak'ahs. The author cites the narration of al-Bayhaqi with a sound chain that the companions prayed twenty rak'ahs during the caliphates of Umar, Uthman, and Ali, which established a consensus (ijma'). Al-Kamal ibn al-Humam is quoted stating that twenty rak'ahs is the sunnah of the Rightly Guided Caliphs. The author distinguishes between what the Prophet did in congregation (eleven rak'ahs including Witr) and the later established practice. The narration of the Prophet praying twenty rak'ahs is considered weak. Another narration is mentioned where the Prophet prayed twenty rak'ahs on two nights but then stopped for fear of obligation. The wisdom (hikmah) behind the number twenty is that Tarawih plus Witr makes twenty, matching the number of daily obligatory rak'ahs (which are seventeen fard plus three witr? Actually daily fard are 17: Fajr 2, Zuhr 4, Asr 4, Maghrib 3, Isha 4 = 17, plus Witr 3 = 20, but the text says something else). The author says: to correspond to the fundamental beliefs and actions (al-fara'id al-i'tiqadiyyah wa al-'amaliyyah) and because supererogatory acts complete the obligatory, so there is equality. This is a metaphysical reasoning.

Key Terms
الإجماع (al-ijma'): Consensus of the scholars, here specifically the consensus of the Companions on twenty rak'ahs.
التراويح (al-tarawih): The special night prayers of Ramadan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary evidence for the Hanafi position that Tarawih consists of twenty rak'ahs?
A) Direct command from the Quran
B) Practice of the Prophet throughout Ramadan
C) Consensus of the Companions during the caliphates of Umar, Uthman, and Ali
D) A hadith stating 'Pray twenty rak'ahs'

Key Takeaway
Tarawih's twenty rak'ahs are established by the consensus of the Companions, making it a sunnah mu'akkadah that every Hanafi should observe.
