The Established Method of Tarawih and Rulings on Deviations
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the validity of praying Tarawih in sets of four or all twenty with one taslim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the established method of Tarawih (two rak'ahs per taslim) and identify the Hanafi rulings on praying four or twenty rak'ahs with one taslim, including the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Tarawih is transmitted as twenty rak'ahs with ten taslims; any deviation is valid but disliked.

In this lesson, we examine the specific method of performing Tarawih prayer as transmitted from the Salaf. The standard practice is to pray two rak'ahs and then say the taslim, repeated ten times. However, the Hanafi school also addresses valid deviations and their consequences. Understanding these rulings helps preserve the sunnah while accommodating unintentional variations.

Guided Path
1
State the established method
The passage affirms that Tarawih is 20 rak'ahs with 10 taslims, as inherited (mutawarith). This is the benchmark from which all deviations are measured.
Note the term 'mutawarith' underscores the transmission from the Salaf.
2
Analyze the case of praying four rak'ahs with one taslim (no sitting)
If someone prays four rak'ahs continuously without sitting after the second, different Hanafi scholars give different rulings. The correct view (sahih) is that it suffices for one taslim (two rak'ahs).
Abu Ja'far and Ibn al-Fadl's view is adopted as sahih.
3
Analyze the case of praying four rak'ahs with one taslim but sitting after the second
If the person sits (performs tashahhud) after the second rak'ah but continues without taslim, the correct view is that it suffices for two taslims, meaning the four rak'ahs count as two separate units.
This is the general opinion (qawl al-'ammah).
4
Analyze the case of praying all twenty with one taslim
If one prays all twenty rak'ahs with a single taslim but sits after every two rak'ahs, the most correct view is that it suffices for all, but it is disliked (makruh) because it contradicts the transmitted practice.
The majority of later scholars uphold this view.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is to follow the established method: two rak'ahs per taslim. Deviations are valid but disliked. The correct view among the variations is that praying four with one taslim without sitting counts only as two rak'ahs.
This preserves the sunnah while acknowledging the prayer's validity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهي: عشرون ركعة . بعشر تسليمات، كما هو المتوارث، يسلم على رأس كل ركعتين. فلو صلى أربعاً بتسليمة، ولم يقعد في الثانية، فأظهر الروايتين عن أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف عدم الفساد، وقال أبو الليث تنوب عن تسليمتين. وقال أبو جعفر وابن الفضل: تنوب عن واحدة، وهو الصحيح. ولو قعد على رأس الركعتين، فالصحيح أنه يجوز عن تسليمتين، وهو قول العامة. وفي « المحيط » : لو صلى التراويح كلها بتسليمة واحدة، وقعد على رأس كل ركعتين فالأصح أنه يجوز عن الكل. والصحيح أنه إن تعمد ذلك يكره. وعامة المتأخرين على أنه يجوز عن الكل، لكنه يكره لمخالفته المأثور. وإذا لم يقعد إلا في آخر العشرين قال محمد لم تجز عن شيء، وعليه قضاء ركعتين. وعلى الصحيح عندهما تجوز عن تسليمة أي ركعتين.
And they (Tarawih) are twenty rak'ahs with ten taslims, as is inherited, giving salutation at the end of every two rak'ahs. If one prays four with one taslim and does not sit in the second, then the more apparent of the two narrations from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf is that it is not corrupt. Abu al-Layth said it suffices for two taslims. Abu Ja'far and Ibn al-Fadl said it suffices for one, and that is the correct view. And if one sits at the end of the two rak'ahs, the correct view is that it suffices for two taslims, and that is the general opinion. In al-Muhit: If one prays all of Tarawih with one taslim, and sits at the end of every two rak'ahs, the most correct is that it suffices for all. The correct view is that if he does that intentionally, it is disliked. The majority of later scholars hold that it suffices for all, but it is disliked due to contradicting the transmitted practice. And if he does not sit except at the end of the twenty, Muhammad said it does not suffice for anything, and he must make up two rak'ahs. According to the correct view of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it suffices for one taslim, i.e., two rak'ahs.
Source pages p. 432

Commentary
This passage deals with the method (sifah) of Tarawih in terms of how many rak'ahs per taslim (salutation). The established and inherited practice (al-mutawarith) is to pray two rak'ahs and then say the taslim, totaling ten taslims for twenty rak'ahs. The commentary then examines cases of deviation: if someone prays four rak'ahs continuously with one taslim and does not sit after the second rak'ah (i.e., no tashahhud), there is a difference among Hanafi scholars. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf have two narrations: the more apparent is that it is not corrupt (i.e., the prayer is valid but may be incomplete). Abu al-Layth said it suffices for two taslims (i.e., counts as two units of two). Abu Ja'far and Ibn al-Fadl said it suffices for one taslim (i.e., only two rak'ahs counted), and that is the correct view (al-sahih). If one does sit after the second rak'ah (i.e., performs tashahhud) but then continues without taslim, the correct view is that it suffices for two taslims, meaning the four rak'ahs count as two sets of two, which is the general opinion. Further, if one prays all twenty rak'ahs with a single taslim but sits at the end of every two rak'ahs, the most correct opinion is that it suffices for all, though it remains disliked because it contradicts the transmitted method. Imam Muhammad (al-Shaybani) held that if one does not sit except at the very end of the twenty rak'ahs, then none of the rak'ahs are valid and he must repeat two rak'ahs. But the correct view according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (in another narration) is that it suffices for one taslim, i.e., counts as two rak'ahs. This shows the Hanafi school's detailed analysis with multiple opinions, but the relied-upon practice is to pray in twos with taslim after each pair.

Key Terms
تسليمة (taslimah): The concluding salutation of the prayer; here, a single occurrence of saying the taslim.
ترويحة (tarwihah): A unit of Tarawih; usually a set of four rak'ahs with a rest, or sometimes a set of two.
تراويح (tarawih): The night prayer performed in Ramadan, consisting of twenty rak'ahs according to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Four rak'ahs
B) Two rak'ahs
C) The prayer is invalid
D) It counts as two taslims (four rak'ahs)

Key Takeaway
The established Hanafi method for Tarawih is two rak'ahs per taslim; deviations are valid but disliked, and only the correct number of rak'ahs is counted based on the presence of tashahhud.

Sitting During Tarawih: Sunnah, Not Obligatory
Recommends sitting and details its options.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on sitting between Tarawih sets and identify the recommended acts during the break.

Core Idea
Sitting after every four rak'ahs is sunnah, not wajib, and the break is for flexible worship.

In Tarawih prayer, after every four rak'ahs, a sitting for rest is a well-known practice. This lesson clarifies that this sitting is recommended (sunnah) and not obligatory, based on the tradition of the early Muslims and the very name 'Tarawih' (derived from rest). You will also learn the various permissible actions during these breaks.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
The text begins with 'yustahabbu al-julus' (it is recommended to sit). Identify that the act is sitting, and the ruling is mustahab (recommended/sunnah). Note that it is not wajib.
2
Trace the Evidence
The author gives three pieces of evidence: it is inherited from the salaf, narrated from Abu Hanifa, and the name 'tarawih' itself suggests rest. Understand that these are the bases for the recommendation.
3
List the Options During Sitting
The text states that during the sitting, one is free (mukhayyar) in doing tasbih, recitation, praying four rak'ahs individually (furada), or remaining silent. Note that these are all permissible.
Praying four individually means separate two-rak'ah units, not a set of four.
4
Acknowledge Regional Variations
The text mentions that the people of Mecca would perform tawaf and pray two rak'ahs, while the people of Medina would pray four rak'ahs individually. Recognize that these were practices based on local custom, not binding rulings.
5
Distinguish Sunnah from Wajib
The core point: the sitting is sunnah muakkadah, not wajib. If omitted, the prayer remains valid and no compensation is needed. Understand the distinction.
This is a common area of confusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويُستحَبُّ الجُلوس بـعـد كل أربـع بقدرِها، وكذا بينَ التَّرويحة الخامسة والوتر؛ لأنه المتوارث من السلف، وهكذا روي عن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى؛ ولأن اسم التراويح يغني عن ذلك لأنه مأخوذ من الاستراحة، ثم هم مخيرون في حال الجلوس، بين التسبيح والقراءة وصلاة أربع فرادى والسكوت، وأهل مكة يطوفون أسبوعاً ويصلون له ركعتين، وأهل المدينة يصلون أربع ركعات فرادى.
And it is recommended to sit after every four (rak'ahs) for a period equal to them, and likewise between the fifth tarwihah and Witr; because it is inherited from the predecessors, and thus it is narrated from Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him); and because the name 'tarawih' indicates that, as it is derived from 'rest'. Then they are free in the state of sitting, between tasbih, recitation, praying four rak'ahs individually, or silence. The people of Mecca circumambulate seven rounds and pray two rak'ahs for it, and the people of Medina pray four rak'ahs individually.
Source pages p. 432

Commentary
This passage discusses the recommended acts during Tarawih, specifically the sitting (julus) for rest. The author says it is mustahab (recommended) to sit after every four rak'ahs for a duration equal to the prayer itself. This sitting is also recommended between the fifth tarwihah (set of four) and the Witr prayer. The reason given is that this practice is inherited from the early generations (salaf) and is narrated from Abu Hanifa. Additionally, the very name 'tarawih' is derived from 'tarwihah' meaning rest, so the practice is linguistically suggested. During these sitting periods, one may engage in various acts: glorifying Allah, reciting Quran, praying voluntary prayers individually, or remaining silent. The author then notes the different practices of the people of Mecca (who perform tawaf) and the people of Medina (who pray four rak'ahs individually) during these breaks. This shows regional variations but the core ruling remains: the sitting is recommended, not obligatory.

Key Terms
الترويحة (al-tarwihah): A set of four rak'ahs in Tarawih, after which a rest is taken.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on sitting after every four rak'ahs in Tarawih?
A) It is wajib
B) It is sunnah (mustahab)
C) It is makruh
D) It is not established

Key Takeaway
Sitting during Tarawih is recommended but not obligatory, and one may use the break for worship or silence.

Recommendation to Complete the Quran in Tarawih
Recommendation to complete one full recitation of Quran per month in Tarawih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on completing the Quran during Tarawih, identify its level (sunnah), and cite the authority.

Core Idea
It is sunnah to complete the Quran once during Tarawih — not wajib, but a recommended practice.

Tarawih is a distinctive prayer of Ramadan, and the recitation of the Quran is its core. The Hanafi school, following the majority, recommends that the imam aim to complete one full recitation (khatm) over the month. This practice is sunnah, not obligatory, and is based on the transmission from al-Hasan ibn Ziyad from Abu Hanifa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act
Recognize that the act in question is the recitation of the Quran during the Tarawih prayer in Ramadan.
Tarawih is a sunnah prayer performed after Isha.
2
State the Ruling
The ruling is that it is sunnah (recommended) to complete one full recitation of the Quran during the month.
The text explicitly says 'sunna khatm al-Quran'.
3
Note the Authority
Identify that this is the correct view ('ala al-sahih) and the saying of the majority, narrated from Abu Hanifa via al-Hasan ibn Ziyad.
Al-Hasan ibn Ziyad is known for narrating the nawadir (rare transmissions) of Abu Hanifa.
4
Recognize the Hukm Level
Distinguish between sunnah and wajib: this act is recommended but not obligatory. No sin is incurred for omitting it.
Sunnah muakkadah in the Hanafi school is a confirmed sunnah, but still not fard or wajib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسن ختم القرآن فيها مرة، في الشهر، على الصحيح. وهو قول الأكثر، ورواه الحسن عن أبي حنيفة، يقرأ الإمام في كل ركعة عشر آيات أو.

Commentary
This passage addresses the recommended amount of Quran recitation during Tarawih. The author states that it is sunnah (recommended) to complete one full recitation (khatm) of the Quran during the month of Ramadan within the Tarawih prayers. This is the correct view (al-sahih) and the opinion of the majority of Hanafi scholars, and it is narrated from al-Hasan ibn Ziyad from Abu Hanifa. The imam can recite approximately ten verses per rak'ah to achieve this. The text cuts off but the meaning is clear: the practice of completing the Quran once in Tarawih is established. Additional details, such as how to divide the recitation over the nights, are found in other works.

Key Terms
ختم (khatm): Complete recitation of the entire Quran from beginning to end.

Tarawih: Proper Method and Ruling on Deviations
Intra-Hanafi dispute on Tarawih method

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the prescribed method of Tarawih and explain the Hanafi ruling on deviations, distinguishing between valid and invalid practices.

Core Idea
Twenty rak'ahs with ten taslims is the transmitted method; deviations are valid but disliked if intentional.

The Tarawih prayer is a sunnah of Ramadan, and its method has been transmitted from the early generations. This passage from Imdad al-Fattah clarifies the proper number of taslims and addresses what happens if one deviates. Understanding this ruling prevents confusion between what is invalid and what is merely suboptimal, ensuring that one upholds the sunnah without wrongly invalidating the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the transmitted method
The passage begins by stating the established practice: Tarawih is performed with twenty rak'ahs and ten taslims, meaning one taslim after every two rak'ahs. This is the sunnah that has been handed down.
2
Recognize the deviation: four rak'ahs with one taslim
The text then examines a scenario where someone prays four rak'ahs with a single taslim without sitting after the first two. This diverges from the transmitted pattern and triggers an intra-Hanafi dispute.
3
Trace the early Hanafi positions
According to the most apparent narration from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, such a prayer is not invalid (fasad). However, there is disagreement on whether it counts as one or two taslims. Abu al-Layth said it counts as two, while Abu Ja'far and Ibn al-Fadl said it counts as one, and the latter became the relied-upon fatwa.
4
Understand the more extreme deviation: all twenty with one taslim
The passage later discusses praying all twenty rak'ahs with a single taslim while sitting after every two rak'ahs. The later majority consider this valid but disliked because it contradicts the transmitted practice, even though the pillars are complete.
5
Extract the underlying principle
The core principle is that deficiency in the number of taslims does not affect the essence (dhat) or cause (sabab) of the prayer; thus, the prayer remains valid. However, intentionally opposing the transmitted method is makruh tanzihan (disliked).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بِعَشْرِ تَسْلِيمَاتٍ، كَمَا هُوَ الْمُتَوَارِثُ، يُسَلِّمُ عَلَى رَأْسِ كُلِّ رَكْعَتَيْنِ، قَالَ فِي « الْبَحْرِ » : فَلَوْ صَلَّى أَرْبَعًا بِتَسْلِيمَةٍ، وَلَمْ يَقْعُدْ فِي الثَّانِيَةِ، فَأَظْهَرُ الرِّوَايَتَيْنِ عَنْ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَأَبِي يُوسُفَ عَدَمُ الْفَسَادِ، وَقَالَ أَبُو اللَّيْثِ تَنُوبُ عَنْ تَسْلِيمَتَيْنِ. وَقَالَ أَبُو جَعْفَرٍ وَابْنُ الْفَضْلِ: تَنُوبُ عَنْ وَاحِدَةٍ، وَهُوَ الصَّحِيحُ، كَذَا فِي الظَّهِيرِيَّةِ»، وَ « الْخَانِيَّةِ »، وَفِي (الْمُجْتَبَى» : وَعَلَيْهِ الْفَتْوَى، وَلَوْ قَعَدَ عَلَى رَأْسِ الرَّكْعَتَيْنِ، فَالصَّحِيحُ أَنَّهُ يَجُوزُ عَنْ تَسْلِيمَتَيْنِ، وَهُوَ قَوْلُ الْعَامَّةِ، وَفِي « الْمُحِيطِ » : لَوْ صَلَّى التَّرَاوِيحَ كُلَّهَا بِتَسْلِيمَةٍ وَاحِدَةٍ، وَقَعَدَ عَلَى رَأْسِ كُلِّ رَكْعَتَيْنِ فَالْأَصَحُّ أَنَّهُ يَجُوزُ عَنِ الْكُلِّ؛ لِأَنَّهُ قَدْ أَكْمَلَ الصَّلَاةَ وَلَمْ يُخِلَّ بِشَيْءٍ مِنَ الْأَرْكَانِ، إِلَّا أَنَّهُ جَمَعَ الْمُتَفَرِّقَ وَاسْتَدَامَ التَّحْرِيمَةَ، وَكَانَ أَوْلَى بِالْجَوَازِ؛ لِأَنَّهُ أَشَقُّ وَأَتْعَبُ لِلْبَدَنِ. انْتَهَى. وَالصَّحِيحُ أَنَّهُ إِنْ تَعَمَّدَ ذَلِكَ يُكْرَهُ، كَمَا فِي « النِّصَابِ» وَ «خِزَانَةِ الْفَتَاوَى » ، وَفِي (الْبَزَّازِيَّةِ» . عَامَّةُ الْمُتَأَخِّرِينَ عَلَى أَنَّهُ يَجُوزُ عَنِ الْكُلِّ، لَكِنَّهُ يُكْرَهُ لِمُخَالَفَتِهِ الْمَأْثُورَ، وَالنَّافِي بَنَاهُ عَلَى أَنَّ الزِّيَادَةَ عَلَى الثَّمَانِيَةِ بِتَسْلِيمَةٍ - يَعْنِي: فِي مُطْلَقِ النَّافِلَةِ- نَاقِصٌ عِنْدَهُ، وَعَلَى الْأَرْبَعِ نَاقِصٌ عِنْدَهُمَا، وَعَلَى السِّتِّ فِي رِوَايَةِ الْجَامِعِ عِنْدَهُ، فَلَا يَتَأَدَّى الْكَامِلُ. قُلْنَا: النُّقْصَانُ لَا يَرْجِعُ إِلَى الذَّاتِ، وَلَا إِلَى السَّبَبِ، فَصَحَّ الْأَدَاءُ، وَكُرِهَ لِمُخَالَفَةِ الْمَأْثُورِ. انْتَهَى. وَإِذَا لَمْ يَقْعُدْ إِلَّا فِي آخِرِ الْعِشْرِينَ قَالَ مُحَمَّدٌ لَمْ تَجُزْ عَنْ شَيْءٍ، وَعَلَيْهِ قَضَاءُ رَكْعَتَيْنِ وَعَلَى الصَّحِيحِ عِنْدَهُمَا تَجُوزُ عَنْ تَسْلِيمَةٍ أَيْ رَكْعَتَيْنِ، بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا قَعَدَ عَلَى رَأْسِ كُلِّ رَكْعَتَيْنِ كَمَا فِي « الْخُلَاصَةِ».
With ten taslims, as transmitted, he makes the taslim at the end of every two rak'ahs. He said in Al-Bahr: If he prayed four with one taslim and did not sit in the second, the more apparent of the two narrations from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf is that it is not invalid. And Abu al-Layth said it counts for two taslims. And Abu Ja'far and Ibn al-Fadl said it counts for one, and that is the correct view, thus in Al-Zahiriyya and Al-Khaniyya, and in Al-Mujtaba: and upon it is the fatwa. And if he sat at the end of the two rak'ahs, the correct view is that it is valid for two taslims, and it is the common saying. And in Al-Muhit: If he prayed the entire Tarawih with one taslim and sat at the end of every two rak'ahs, the most correct is that it is valid for all; because he has completed the prayer and omitted nothing of the pillars, except that he has combined the separate and continued the tahrima, and it is more deserving of validity because it is more difficult and tiring for the body. End. And the correct view is that if he does that intentionally, it is disliked, as in Al-Nisab and Khizanat al-Fatawa, and in Al-Bazzaziyya. The majority of later scholars hold that it is valid for all, but it is disliked due to contradicting the transmitted practice. And the one who negates it based it on the fact that increasing beyond eight with one taslim—meaning in absolute supererogatory prayer—is deficient according to him, and beyond four is deficient according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and beyond six according to the narration of Al-Jami' according to him, so the complete is not performed. We say: the deficiency does not affect the essence nor the cause, so the performance is valid, and disliked due to contradicting the transmitted. End. And if he did not sit except at the end of the twenty, Muhammad said it does not count for anything, and he must make up two rak'ahs, and according to the correct view of them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it counts for one taslim, i.e., two rak'ahs, contrary to when he sits at the end of every two rak'ahs as in Al-Khulasa.
Source pages p. 432

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the proper method of Tarawih and the validity of deviations. The proper method, as transmitted from the Salaf, is to pray 20 rak'ahs with a taslim every two rak'ahs, resulting in ten taslims. The discussion then addresses cases where one prays four rak'ahs with a single taslim. According to the most apparent narration from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, this is not invalid, but there is disagreement among later scholars whether it counts as one or two taslims. The relied-upon fatwa is that it counts for one taslim (two rak'ahs) if one sits after two; if not, it's still valid but disliked. The extreme case of all 20 rak'ahs with one taslim while sitting every two is considered valid by later scholars, though disliked for opposing the transmitted practice. Imam Muhammad's view is stricter: if one only sits at the end, it counts for nothing, but the correct view according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad is that it counts for one taslim. The key principle is that the deficiency does not affect the essence or cause of the prayer.

Key Terms
تَسْلِيمَة (taslimah): The final salutation ending a prayer; in Tarawih, used to count units (one per two rak'ahs).
تَرَاوِيح (tarawih): Plural of tarwiha; the night prayers of Ramadan, consisting of twenty rak'ahs in the Hanafi school.
تَحْرِيمَة (tahrima): The initial takbir (allahu akbar) that begins the prayer and establishes the state of ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Invalid and requires full repetition
B) Valid but disliked (makruh)
C) Valid and recommended
D) Valid only if he intended to follow a different school

Key Takeaway
The transmitted method of Tarawih is 20 rak'ahs with 10 taslims; praying otherwise is valid but disliked, as deficiency does not affect the essence.

Recommended Sitting in Tarawih: After Every Four and Between Fifth Tarwiha and Witr
Explains recommended sitting intervals and options in Tarawih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sitting during Tarawih and identify the permissible and disliked actions during the breaks.

Core Idea
Recommended sitting after every four rak'ahs in Tarawih is a transmitted practice; during the break, one may pray four individually, but praying individually between every two pairs is disliked.

In this lesson, we examine the seventh point of Tarawih: the recommended sitting intervals. The Hanafi school prescribes sitting after every four rak'ahs and between the fifth tarwiha and witr, based on the Salaf's practice and the very meaning of Tarawih (rest). We also explore what actions are recommended or disliked during these breaks, including a caution against certain innovations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended sitting intervals
Read the source to find when it is recommended (mustahabb) to sit: after every four rak'ahs and between the fifth tarwiha and witr.
The fifth tarwiha is the last four-rak'ah set before witr.
2
Recognize the basis for the recommendation
Note the two reasons given: transmission from the Salaf and the derivation of 'Tarawih' from rest (tarvih).
This shows the ruling is grounded in transmitted practice, not mere opinion.
3
List the permissible actions during the sitting
Identify the four options: tasbih, recitation, praying four rak'ahs individually, or silence.
Praying four rak'ahs individually is permitted but must not be in congregation.
4
Differentiate the disliked action
Understand that praying individually between every two pairs (i.e., after every two rak'ahs) is disliked, as it is considered an innovation and opposes the imam.
This distinction is crucial to avoid confusion with the recommended practice.
5
Note regional variations
Observe that people of Makkah and Madinah had different practices during the break (tawaf vs. four rak'ahs individually), but all are permissible.
This illustrates flexibility within the recommended framework.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالسَّابِعُ: (وَيُسْتَحَبُّ الْجُلُوسُ بَعْدَ صَلَاةِ كُلِّ أَرْبَعٍ بِقَدْرِهَا)، (وَكَذَا) يُسْتَحَبُّ الْجُلُوسُ بِقَدْرِ الْأَرْبَعِ ( بَيْنَ التَّرْوِيحَةِ الْخَامِسَةِ وَالْوِتْرِ)؛ لِأَنَّهُ الْمُتَوَارِثُ مِنَ السَّلَفِ، وَهَكَذَا رُوِيَ عَنْ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى؛ وَلِأَنَّ اسْمَ التَّرَاوِيحِ يُغْنِي عَنْ ذَلِكَ لِأَنَّهُ مَأْخُوذٌ مِنَ الِاسْتِرَاحَةِ، ثُمَّ هُمْ مُخَيَّرُونَ فِي حَالِ الْجُلُوسِ، بَيْنَ التَّسْبِيحِ وَالْقِرَاءَةِ وَصَلَاةِ أَرْبَعٍ فَرَادَى وَالسُّكُوتِ، وَأَهْلُ مَكَّةَ يَطُوفُونَ أُسْبُوعاً وَيُصَلُّونَ لَهُ رَكْعَتَيْنِ، وَأَهْلُ الْمَدِينَةِ يُصَلُّونَ أَرْبَعَ رَكَعَاتٍ فَرَادَى، كَذَا فِي « التَّبْيِينِ»، وَ « الْبُرْهَانِ»، وَ«فَتْحِ الْقَدِيرِ ) وَبِهِ يُعْلَمُ مَا فِي قَوْلِهِ فِي شَرْحِ الْمُنْيَةِ : يُكْرَهُ الصَّلَاةُ مُنْفَرِداً بَيْنَ كُلِّ شَفْعَيْنِ، وَهُوَ فِعْلُ بَعْضِ الْجُهَّالِ؛ لِأَنَّهَا بِدْعَةٌ مَعَ مُخَالَفَةِ الْإِمَامِ، ذَكَرَهُ السُّرُوجِيُّ عَنْ «خِزَانَةِ الْفِقْهِ» انْتَهَى.
And the seventh: (And it is recommended to sit after every four [rak'ahs] for the duration of them), and likewise it is recommended to sit for the duration of four (between the fifth tarwiha and the witr); because it is transmitted from the Salaf, and thus it is narrated from Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him; and because the name 'Tarawih' suffices for that, as it is derived from rest. Then they have a choice during sitting between tasbih, recitation, praying four individually, and silence. And the people of Makkah perform tawaf of one week and pray two rak'ahs for it, and the people of Madinah pray four rak'ahs individually, thus in Al-Tabyin, Al-Burhan, and Fath al-Qadir. And by this is known what is in his saying in Sharh al-Munya: It is disliked to pray individually between every two pairs, and it is the action of some ignorant people; because it is an innovation with opposition to the imam, mentioned by al-Saruji from Khizanat al-Fiqh. End.
Source pages p. 432

Commentary
This passage presents the seventh point: the recommended sitting in Tarawih. It is recommended to sit after every four rak'ahs for a duration equal to the prayer, and also between the fifth tarwiha (i.e., after the 20th rak'ah) and the witr prayer. This practice is transmitted from the Salaf and attributed to Abu Hanifa. The name 'Tarawih' itself implies rest. During these sitting breaks, the congregation may engage in tasbih, recitation, praying four rak'ahs individually (i.e., not in congregation), or silence. The text notes regional practices: Makkans perform tawaf and pray two rak'ahs, while Madinans pray four separate rak'ahs. It further clarifies that praying individually between each pair of rak'ahs (i.e., after every two rak'ahs) is disliked, as it opposes the imam's method and is considered an innovation by some scholars.

Key Terms
تَرْوِيحَة (tarwiha): A set of four rak'ahs in Tarawih; the fifth tarwiha is the last set before witr
شَفْع (shaf'): A pair of rak'ahs

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Obligatory
B) Recommended (mustahabb)
C) Permissible without preference
D) Disliked

Key Takeaway
Sitting after every four rak'ahs and between the fifth tarwiha and witr is recommended, with a choice of activities; praying individually between every two pairs is disliked.

Salah — Prayer

Recitation in Tarawih: Sunnah of Khatm and Adjustment for Congregation
Explains the Sunnah of khatm and the permissibility of shortening recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on completing the Quran in Tarawih and explain when shortening recitation is preferred over the full khatm.

Core Idea
Completing Quran once in Tarawih is Sunnah, but avoiding congregation's hardship takes precedence.

This lesson addresses two interrelated rulings: first, the default Sunnah of reciting the entire Quran over the month of Ramadan in Tarawih prayers; second, the important exception that when the congregation is wearied, the imam should shorten the recitation to three short verses or one long verse per rak'ah. The passage draws on the calculation of total rak'ahs and verses, a hadith on the virtues of Ramadan, and later Hanafi fatwa practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Default Ruling
The act is recitation in Tarawih. The default ruling is Sunnah to complete the Quran once during the month, based on the correct view (al-sahih).
The calculation: 600 rak'ahs (20 per night × 30) and ~6000 verses → 10 verses per rak'ah achieves one khatm.
2
Examine the Evidence
The dalil includes the hadith that Ramadan's beginning is mercy, middle forgiveness, end emancipation, and the practice of 'Umar (30 verses per rak'ah for three khatms).
The hadith is zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalala; it supports the virtue but does not command a specific amount.
3
Note the Scholarly Difference
Some recommend 30 verses per rak'ah for three completions, citing 'Umar and the ten-day virtues. Others prefer completing on the 27th night for Laylat al-Qadr.
The intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is over what is more virtuous, not over validity.
4
Apply the Principle of Congregational Ease
If the people are wearied by lengthy recitation, the imam should recite an amount that does not alienate them. Increasing the congregation is better than lengthening recitation.
Later fatwa: three short verses or one long verse after al-Fatihah is sufficient. Restricting to less than three short verses is disliked.
5
Determine the Operative Ruling (Mufta Bihi)
The mufta bihi is to complete the Quran once if possible, but if hardship arises, shorten to avoid tanfir. The minimum is al-Fatihah plus three short verses or equivalent.
This is based on Al-Mukhtar, Al-Ikhtiyar, Al-Muhit, and later Hanafi scholars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالثَّامِنُ: أَشَارَ إِلَيْهِ بِقَوْلِهِ: (سُنَّ حَتْمُ الْقُرْآنِ فِيهَا ) أَيِ التَّرَاوِيحِ (مَرَّةً، فِي الشَّهْرِ، عَلَى الصَّحِيحِ) وَهُوَ قَوْلُ الْأَكْثَرِ، وَرَوَاهُ الْحَسَنُ عَنْ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ، يَقْرَأُ الْإِمَامُ فِي كُلِّ رَكْعَةٍ عَشْرَ آيَاتٍ أَوْ نَحْوَهَا؛ لِأَنَّ عَدَدَ رَكَعَاتِهَا فِي جَمِيعِ الشَّهْرِ سِتَّ مِائَةٍ، إِنْ كَانَ كَامِلاً، أَوْ خَمْسَ مِئَةٍ وَثَمَانِينَ، إِنْ كَانَ نَاقِصاً، وَعَدَدُ آيِ الْقُرْآنِ سِتَّةُ آلَافٍ وَشَيْءٌ ) ، فَإِذَا قَرَأَ فِي كُلِّ رَكْعَةٍ عَشْرَ آيَاتٍ يَحْصُلُ الْخَتْمُ فِيهَا، وَقَالَ بَعْضُهُمْ: يَقْرَأُ فِي كُلِّ رَكْعَةٍ ثَلَاثِينَ آيَةً؛ لِأَنَّ عُمَرَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ أَمَرَ بِذَلِكَ ) فَيَقَعُ الْخَتْمُ ثَلَاثَ مَرَّاتٍ؛ لِأَنَّ كُلَّ عَشْرٍ مَخْصُوصٌ بِفَضِيلَةٍ عَلَى حِدَةٍ، كَمَا جَاءَتْ بِهِ السُّنَّةُ، أَنَّهُ «شَهْرٌ أَوَّلُهُ رَحْمَةٌ، وَأَوْسَطُهُ مَغْفِرَةٌ، وَآخِرُهُ عِتْقٌ مِنَ النَّارِ ) ، وَمِنْهُمْ مَنِ اسْتَحَبَّ الْخَتْمَ لَيْلَةَ السَّابِعِ وَالْعِشْرِينَ رَجَاءَ مُوَافَقَةِ لَيْلَةِ الْقَدْرِ، وَعَنْ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ أَنَّهُ كَانَ يَخْتِمُ إِحْدَى وَسِتِّينَ خَتْمَةً فِي كُلِّ يَوْمٍ خَتْمَةً، وَفِي كُلِّ لَيْلَةٍ خَتْمَةً، وَفِي كُلِّ التَّرَاوِيحِ خَتْمَةً وَالْمَشْهُورُ عَنْهُ أَنَّهُ صَلَّى الْفَجْرَ بِوُضُوءِ الْعِشَاءِ أَرْبَعِينَ سَنَةً، (وَإِنْ مَلَّ بِهِ أَيْ بِخَتْمِ الْقُرْآنِ فِي الشَّهْرِ ( الْقَوْمُ قَرَأَ بِقَدْرِ مَا لَا يُؤَدِّي إِلَى تَنْفِيرِهِمْ، فِي الْمُخْتَارِ)، لِأَنَّ الْأَفْضَلَ فِي زَمَانِنَا مَا لَا يُؤَدِّي إِلَى تَنْفِيرِ الْجَمَاعَةِ، كَذَا فِي «الِاخْتِيَارِ»، وَفِي الْمُحِيطِ » : الْأَفْضَلُ فِي زَمَانِنَا أَنْ يُقْرَأَ بِمَا لَا يُؤَدِّي إِلَى تَنْفِيرِ الْقَوْمِ عَنِ الْجَمَاعَةِ؛ لِأَنَّ تَكْثِيرَ الْقَوْمِ أَفْضَلُ مِنْ تَطْوِيلِ الْقِرَاءَةِ، كَذَا فِي شَرْحِ الدِّيرِيِّ لِلْكَنْزِ ، وَفِي مَجْمَعِ الرِّوَايَاتِ»، قَالَ الزَّاهِدِيُّ: وَقِيلَ: يَقْرَأُ كَمَا فِي الْمَغْرِبِ، وَقِيلَ ثَلَاثُ آيَاتٍ قِصَارٍ، أَوْ آيَةٌ طَوِيلَةٌ، أَوْ آيَتَانِ مُتَوَسِّطَتَانِ بَعْدَ الْفَاتِحَةِ، وَعَنْ أَبِي ذَرٍّ آيَتَانِ. قَالَ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ : وَالْمُتَأَخِّرُونَ كَانُوا يُفْتُونَ فِي زَمَانِنَا بِثَلَاثِ آيَاتٍ قِصَارٍ، أَوْ آيَةٍ طَوِيلَةٍ، حَتَّى لَا يَمَلَّ الْقَوْمُ، وَلَا يَلْزَمُ تَعْطِيلُهَا، وَهَذَا حَسَنٌ فَإِنَّ الْحَسَنَ رَوَى عَنْ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ: إِذَا قَرَأَ فِي الْمَكْتُوبَةِ بَعْدَ الْفَاتِحَةِ ثَلَاثَ آيَاتٍ فَقَدْ أَحْسَنَ وَلَمْ يُسِئْ فَهَذَا فِي الْمَكْتُوبَةِ فَمَا ظَنُّكَ فِي غَيْرِهَا. وَقَالَ فِي عُيُونِ الْمَذَاهِبِ» : قِيلَ : الْأَفْضَلُ أَنْ يَقْرَأَ فِي كُلِّ رَكْعَةٍ مَا لَا يُؤَدِّي إِلَى تَنْفِيرِ الْجَمَاعَةِ، وَبِهِ يُفْتَى وَالِاقْتِصَارُ عَلَى مَا دُونَ الْفَاتِحَةِ وَثَلَاثِ آيَاتٍ قِصَارٍ، أَوْ آيَةٍ طَوِيلَةٍ يُوجِبُ الْكَرَاهَةَ، وَعَلَيْهِ الْفَتْوَى فِي زَمَانِنَا. انْتَهَى.
And the eighth: he pointed to it with his saying: (It is Sunnah to complete the Quran in it) i.e., Tarawih (once, in the month, on the correct view). It is the saying of the majority, and al-Hasan narrated it from Abu Hanifa. The imam recites ten verses or so in every rak'ah; because the number of its rak'ahs in the entire month is six hundred, if complete, or five hundred and eighty, if incomplete, and the number of verses of the Quran is six thousand and something. So if he recites ten verses in every rak'ah, the completion is attained in it. And some said: he recites thirty verses in every rak'ah; because 'Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, ordered that, so the completion occurs three times; because every ten is specified with a distinct virtue, as came in the Sunnah, that it is 'a month whose beginning is mercy, its middle is forgiveness, and its end is emancipation from the Fire.' And among them is one who recommended completing on the night of the twenty-seventh hoping to coincide with Laylat al-Qadr. And from Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, that he used to complete sixty-one completions: a completion every day, a completion every night, and a completion in every Tarawih. And the famous from him is that he prayed the Fajr with the wudu of 'Isha' for forty years. (And if the people are wearied by it, i.e., by completing the Quran in the month, he recites to the extent that does not lead to their alienation, in Al-Mukhtar), because the best in our time is what does not lead to alienating the congregation, thus in Al-Ikhtiyar. And in Al-Muhit: the best in our time is to recite what does not lead to alienating the people from the congregation; because increasing the people is better than lengthening the recitation, thus in Sharh al-Dairi lil-Kanz, and in Majma' al-Riwayat. Al-Zahidi said: and it was said: he recites as in Maghrib, and it was said: three short verses, or one long verse, or two medium verses after al-Fatihah. And from Abu Dharr: two verses. He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: and the later scholars used to give fatwa in our time with three short verses or one long verse, so that the people do not become weary, and it is not necessary to suspend it. And this is good, for al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him: if he recites in the obligatory prayer after al-Fatihah three verses, he has done well and not wrong; this is in the obligatory, so what do you think about other than it? And he said in 'Uyun al-Madhahib: it was said: the best is that he recites in every rak'ah what does not lead to alienating the congregation, and by this fatwa is given. And restricting to less than al-Fatihah and three short verses or one long verse necessitates dislike, and upon it is the fatwa in our time. End.
Source pages p. 432

Commentary
This passage is the eighth point: the Sunnah of completing the Quran in Tarawih. The correct view is that it is Sunnah to complete the Quran once during the month of Ramadan in Tarawih. The calculation is based on 600 rak'ahs (20 per night for 30 nights) and approximately 6000 verses, so 10 verses per rak'ah achieves a complete recitation. Some recommend 30 verses per rak'ah for three completions, citing 'Umar's instruction and the hadith about the first, middle, and last ten days of Ramadan. Others recommend completing on the 27th night hoping for Laylat al-Qadr. The text notes Abu Hanifa's personal devotion. However, the primary principle is that if the congregation is wearied by lengthy recitation, the imam should recite to the extent that does not alienate them. This is the best in later times, as increasing the congregation takes precedence over lengthy recitation. Various suggestions for recitation amount are given: like Maghrib prayer, three short verses, one long verse, etc. The fatwa in later times is that it is disliked to recite less than al-Fatihah and three short verses or one long verse.

Key Terms
خَتْمُ الْقُرْآنِ (khatm al-Qur'an): Completing the recitation of the entire Quran from beginning to end
تَنْفِير (tanfir): Alienation or driving away (the congregation) by lengthy recitation

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on completing the Quran in Tarawih during Ramadan?
A) Wajib
B) Sunnah
C) Mubah
D) Haram

Key Takeaway
The default is Sunnah to complete the Quran once in Tarawih, but if the congregation is wearied, the imam should shorten recitation to avoid driving them away.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
Sending Salawat in Tashahhud of Tarawih and Recitation Rules
States ruling on salawat in tashahhud and warns against hasty recitation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sending salawat in the tashahhud of Tarawih and identify the warnings against hasty recitation and lack of tranquility.

Core Idea
Sending salawat in every tashahhud is a stressed sunnah, not fard; proper recitation and tranquility are essential.

This passage addresses two practical concerns in Tarawih prayer: the recommendation to send salawat upon the Prophet in every tashahhud, and the warning against careless recitation and lack of composure. While some scholars consider salawat obligatory, the Hanafi school classifies it as a stressed sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah). The passage also condemns hasty reading (hadhramah) and neglect of tranquility (tuma'minah), which are common mistakes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its occasion
The act is sending salawat upon the Prophet. It is to be done in every tashahhud of Tarawih prayer. Note that this is the ninth point in the author's list of recommended acts for Tarawih.
Tashahhud occurs in the second and final rak'ahs of each Tarawih cycle.
2
Determine the Hanafi ruling
According to the Hanafi school, this act is a stressed sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah). The phrase 'sunnah mu'akkadah' means it is highly recommended but not obligatory; omission does not invalidate the prayer.
The text contrasts this with the view of some other mujtahids who consider it fard (obligatory).
3
Understand the warning about recitation
The passage warns against leaving 'tartil' (measured, clear recitation) and against 'hadhramah' (hasty, sloppy reading). This applies to the Quran recited in prayer, especially in Tarawih where longer passages are read.
Hadhramah is disliked (makruh); proper tartil is sunnah.
4
Recognize the importance of tranquility (tuma'minah)
Leaving tranquility in the postures is also condemned. Tuma'minah is wajib (obligatory) in the Hanafi school; omitting it requires sajdah sahw (prostration of forgetfulness).
The warning includes 'other things' – i.e., all necessary elements of prayer.
5
Apply the lesson to practice
When leading or performing Tarawih, ensure to send salawat in each tashahhud, recite with measured clarity, and maintain stillness in each posture. Avoid rushing through the prayer.
If an imam recites too fast without proper articulation, it is makruh and may affect the congregation's concentration.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وَ) التَّاسِعُ: أَنَّهُ ( لَا يَتْرُكُ الصَّلَاةَ عَلَى سَيِّدِنَا النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فِي كُلِّ تَشَهُّدٍ مِنْهَا؛ لِأَنَّهَا فَرْضٌ عَلَى قَوْلِ بَعْضِ الْمُجْتَهِدِينَ)، وَسُنَّةٌ مُؤَكَّدَةٌ عَلَى قَوْلِنَا، وَكَذَا يُحْذَرُ مِنْ تَرْكِ تَرْتِيلِ الْقُرْآنِ، كَمَا يَحْصُلُ مِنْ بَعْضِ الْجُهَّالِ مِنَ الْهَذْرَمَةِ ) وَتَرْكِ الطُّمَأْنِينَةِ فِي الْأَرْكَانِ وَغَيْرِهَا،
(And) the ninth: that (he does not leave sending salawat upon our master the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, in every tashahhud of it; because it is obligatory according to the saying of some mujtahids), and a stressed sunnah according to our saying. And likewise one is cautious against leaving the tartil (measured recitation) of the Quran, as happens from some ignorant people of hadhramah (hasty reading) and leaving tranquility (tuma'minah) in the postures and other things.
Source pages p. 433

Commentary
This is the ninth point: it is recommended to send salawat upon the Prophet (peace be upon him) in every tashahhud of Tarawih. According to the Hanafi school, this is a stressed sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah), though some other scholars consider it obligatory. The text then warns against leaving proper recitation (tartil) and tranquility (tuma'minah) in the prayer postures, which is a problem among some ignorant people who recite hastily (hadhramah).

Key Terms
تَشَهُّد (tashahhud): The sitting posture and recitation of the testimony of faith in prayer
هَذْرَمَة (hadhramah): Hasty, rapid recitation of Quran without proper articulation
طُمَأْنِينَة (tuma'minah): Tranquility and stillness in prayer postures; a wajib element

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on sending salawat upon the Prophet in the tashahhud of Tarawih?
A) Fard (obligatory)
B) Sunnah mu'akkadah (stressed sunnah)
C) Makruh (disliked)
D) Mubah (permissible)

Key Takeaway
Sending salawat in every tashahhud is a stressed sunnah, not fard; proper recitation (tartil) and tranquility (tuma'minah) are essential elements of prayer.

Recitation Length and Salawat in Tarawih
Guidelines for recitation length and salawat in Tarawih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on recitation length in Tarawih when the congregation becomes bored, and explain the status of sending blessings (salawat) in every tashahhud as sunnah mu'akkadah, distinguishing it from the Shafi'i view of obligation.

Core Idea
Balancing recitation to retain congregation outweighs lengthy recitation; salawat in every tashahhud is sunnah mu'akkadah, not fard.

This lesson tackles two practical issues in Tarawih prayer: how much the imam should recite if the congregation grows weary, and whether sending blessings on the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam) is obligatory or recommended in every tashahhud. The passage from Imdad al-Fattah provides the Hanafi position with proofs and fatwa of later scholars, emphasizing that keeping the congregation engaged is more important than lengthy recitation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two distinct rulings
The passage addresses (1) the extent of recitation in Tarawih if the congregation becomes bored, and (2) the obligation/emphasis of sending blessings (salawat) in every tashahhud. Label each and note the condition for the first ruling.
The first ruling is conditional on the congregation's boredom (tanfir).
2
Analyze the recitation guideline and its basis
From the matn and commentary, extract the recommended amount: three short verses, one long verse, or two medium verses after al-Fatiha. Understand that this is the mufta bihi fatwa from later scholars to avoid driving people away. Note the hadith and practice of Umar (radiyallahu anhu) as proof for completing the Quran multiple times, but with flexibility.
The key principle: increasing the number of worshippers is better than lengthening the recitation.
3
Determine the ruling on salawat in tashahhud
The matn says: 'he does not abandon sending blessings... because it is obligatory according to some mujtahids, and a confirmed sunnah according to us.' Identify the Hanafi position (sunnah mu'akkadah) and the opposing view (fard, e.g., Shafi'i).
'Us' refers to the Hanafi school.
4
Examine the evidence for both rulings
For recitation: the hadith 'Month of mercy...' and the report from Umar (radiyallahu anhu) ordering thirty verses per rak'ah. For salawat: the text does not cite an explicit dalil but relies on the general emphasis on sending blessings. Note the authority level: later fatwa for recitation, standard Hanafi position for salawat.
The dalil_block in the toolbox cites the hadith as a proof for abundant worship, but the direct proof for salawat is not quoted here.
5
Apply the principles to a modern scenario
Imagine an imam in a Tarawih prayer where the congregation is restless. According to the fatwa, he should recite a moderate amount (e.g., three short verses) to keep them engaged. Similarly, he must ensure he sends blessings upon the Prophet in every tashahhud, as it is sunnah mu'akkadah.
This balances sunnah and congregation well-being.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن مل به القوم، قرأ بقَدْرِ ما لا يؤدي إلى تنفيرهم، في المختار ولا يتركُ الصَّلاةَ على سيدنا النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في كل تشهد منها ...
نحوها؛ لأن عدد ركعاتها في جميع الشهر ست مائة، إن كان كاملاً، أو خمس مئة وثمانون، إن كان ناقصاً، وعدد آي القرآن ستة آلاف وشيء ، فإذا قرأ في كل ركعة عشر آيـات يحصـل الخـتـم فـيـهـا، وقال بعضهم: يقرأ في كل ركعة ثلاثين آية؛ لأن عمر رضي الله عنه أمر بذلك فيقع الختم ثلاث مرات؛ لأن كل عشر مخصوص بفضيلة على حدة، كما جاءت به السنة، أنه «شهر أوله رحمة، وأوسطه مغفرة، وآخره عتق من النار»، ومنهم من استحب الختم ليلة السابع والعشرين رجاء موافقة ليلة القدر، وعن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله أنه كان يختم إحدى وستين ختمة في كل يوم ختمة، وفي كل ليلة ختمة، وفي كل التراويح ختمة والمشهور عنه أنه صلى الفجر بوضوء العشاء أربعين سنة، (وإن مل به أي بختم القرآن في الشهر القومُ قرأ بقَدْرِ ما لا يؤدي إلى تنفيرهم، في المختار)، لأن الأفضل في زماننا ما لا يؤدي إلى تنفير الجماعة، كذا في «الاختيار»، وفي المحيط : الأفضل في زماننا أن يُقرأ بما لا يؤدي إلى تنفير القوم عن الجماعة؛ لأن تكثير القوم أفضل من تطويل القراءة، كذا في شرح الديري للكنز ، وفي مجمع الروايات، قال الزاهدي: وقيل: يقرأ كما في المغرب، وقيل ثلاث آيات قصار، أو آية طويلة، أو آيتان متوسطتان بعد الفاتحة، وعن أبي ذره آيتان. قال رحمه الله : والمتأخرون كانوا يفتون في زماننا بثلاث آيات قصار، أو آيـة طويلة، حتّى لا يمل القوم، ولا يلزم تعطيلها، وهذا حسن فإن الحسن روى عن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله: إذا قرأ في المكتوبة بعد الفاتحة ثلاث آيات فقد أحسن ولم يسيء فهذا في المكتوبة فما ظنك في غيرها. وقال في عيون المذاهب: قيل : الأفضل أن يقرأ في كل ركعة مـا لا يـؤدي إلى تنفير الجماعة، وبه يفتي والاقتصار على ما دون الفاتحة وثلاث آيات قصار، أو آية طويلة يوجب الكراهة، وعليه الفتوى في زماننا. انتهى. (و) التاسع: أنه ( لا يتركُ الصَّلاةَ على سيدنا النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في كل تشهد منها؛ لأنها فرض على قول بعض المجتهدين)، وسنة مؤكدة على قولنا، وكذا يحذر مـن ترك ترتيل القرآن، كما يحصل من بعض الجهال من الهذرمة وترك الطمأنينة في الأركان وغيرها،
And if the congregation becomes bored due to it, he recites to the extent that does not lead to their aversion, according to the chosen view. And he does not abandon sending blessings on our master the Prophet, peace be upon him, in every tashahhud... because the number of its rak'ahs in the whole month is six hundred, if complete, or five hundred and eighty, if deficient, and the number of verses of the Quran is six thousand and something. So if he recites ten verses in every rak'ah, the completion of the Quran is achieved in them. And some said: He recites thirty verses in every rak'ah because Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, ordered that, so the completion occurs three times because every ten has a specific virtue, as the Sunnah has come: 'It is a month whose beginning is mercy, its middle is forgiveness, and its end is emancipation from the Fire.' And among them is one who recommended completion on the night of the twenty-seventh hoping to coincide with the Night of Qadr. And it is reported from Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, that he completed sixty-one completions: one completion every day, one every night, and one in the tarawih. The well-known from him is that he prayed Fajr with the ablution of Isha for forty years. (And if the congregation becomes bored, i.e., with the completion of the Quran in the month, he recites to the extent that does not lead to their aversion, according to the chosen view), because the better in our time is what does not lead to aversion of the congregation. Thus in al-Ikhtiyar. And in al-Muhit: The better in our time is that he recite what does not lead to aversion of the people from the congregation because increasing the number of people is better than lengthening the recitation. Thus in Sharh al-Dayri li al-Kanz. And in Majma' al-Riwayat, al-Zahidi said: It is said: He recites as in Maghrib; and it is said: three short verses, or one long verse, or two medium verses after al-Fatiha; and from Abu Dharr: two verses. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: The later scholars used to give fatwa in our time of three short verses or one long verse so that the congregation does not become bored and its abandonment is not necessitated. This is good because al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him: If he recites in the obligatory prayer after al-Fatiha three verses, he has done well and not done evil. This is in the obligatory prayer, so what do you think about other prayers? And he said in Uyun al-Madhahib: It is said: The better is that he recite in every rak'ah what does not lead to aversion of the congregation, and with this fatwa is given. And restricting to less than al-Fatiha and three short verses or one long verse necessitates dislike, and upon this is fatwa in our time. End. (And) the ninth: That he does not abandon sending blessings on our master the Prophet, peace be upon him, in every tashahhud because it is obligatory according to some mujtahids, and a confirmed sunnah according to us. And similarly, he is warned against abandoning the tartil of the Quran, as occurs from some ignoramuses of hasty recitation, and abandoning tranquility in the pillars and other things.
Source pages p. 433

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Sharh of Nur al-Idah. The author addresses two issues in tarawih: the length of recitation when the congregation becomes bored, and the obligation of salawat in every tashahhud. For recitation, the matn states that if people are bored, the imam should recite a moderate amount to avoid driving them away. The commentary elaborates: the ideal is to balance recitation so that the congregation does not leave; increasing the number of worshippers is better than prolonging the prayer. Various opinions are given: some say to recite as in Maghrib, others three short verses or one long verse. The relied-upon fatwa in the author's time is three short verses or one long verse per rak'ah, as this prevents boredom without abandoning the sunnah. The proof cited includes the practice of Umar (radiyallahu anhu) ordering thirty verses per rak'ah to achieve three completions, and the hadith about the month's virtues. The ninth ruling then states that salawat on the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam) must not be left in any tashahhud; it is obligatory according to some scholars (like Shafi'i) and a confirmed sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah) in the Hanafi school. The commentary warns against abandoning tartil (measured recitation) and tranquility (tuma'ninah) in the pillars, as these are essential.

Key Terms
التراويح (al-tarawih): The night prayers performed in congregation during Ramadan, consisting of 20 rak'ahs per night.
الختم (al-khatm): The complete recitation of the entire Quran from beginning to end.
تنفير (tanfir): Aversion or driving away; the congregation becoming bored and leaving.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on sending blessings upon the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam) in every tashahhud of tarawih?
A) It is fard (obligatory).
B) It is sunnah mu'akkadah (confirmed sunnah).
C) It is makruh (disliked).
D) It is only recommended in the last tashahhud.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school teaches that preserving the congregation's comfort by reciting moderately in Tarawih is better than lengthy recitation, and that sending blessings in every tashahhud is a confirmed sunnah, not an obligation.

Rulings for the Imam in Tarawih: Thana, Tasbih, Dua, and Qada
Rulings for the imam on thana, tasbih, and dua, and that missed tarawih is not made up

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings for the imam regarding thana, tasbih, and dua in tarawih, and explain why missed tarawih prayers are not made up.

Core Idea
The imam must not omit thana and tasbih for boredom; dua may be shortened; missed tarawih cannot be made up.

In this passage, the author presents four key rulings for the imam leading tarawih prayers. These rulings balance the rights of the congregation with the obligation to maintain the sunnah acts. Understanding these rules helps avoid common errors in leading Ramadan prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first ruling
Read the passage and identify the ruling about thana (opening glorification). The author states that the imam does not abandon thana even if the congregation is bored.
Thana is required from every worshipper, so it should not be omitted for laziness.
2
Identify the second ruling
Find the ruling about tasbih in ruku' and sujud. The author says it is a confirmed sunnah and should not be abandoned.
The passage mentions that some consider it fard, but Hanafis hold it as sunnah mu'akkadah.
3
Identify the third ruling
Locate the ruling about supplication (dua) before salam. The imam should avoid lengthy dua if the congregation is bored, but he should still make a short dua to maintain the sunnah.
The key is to shorten the dua, not omit it entirely.
4
Identify the fourth ruling
Find the ruling about making up missed tarawih. The author states that tarawih are not made up after their time, whether individually or in congregation.
The reason given is that qada is only for obligatory acts; tarawih is sunnah.
5
Understand the reasoning
Each ruling is supported by a reason: for thana and tasbih, they are required acts; for dua, it is to avoid hardship for the congregation; for missed tarawih, qada is not applicable to sunnah acts.
The passage also includes a discussion on whether tarawih is a sunnah of time or fasting, concluding it is of time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو مل القوم، على المختار ولا يَتْرُكُ الثَّناء، وتسبيح الركوع والسجود ، ولا يأتي بالدعاء، إن مل القوم. ولا تُقضى التراويح بفواتها، منفرداً ولا بجماعة.
(ولو مل القومُ) بذلك عَلَى المختار)، لأنه عين الكسل منهم فلا يتبع (وَ) العاشر: أنه ( لا يَتْرُكُ الثناء) في افتتاح كل شفع؛ لأنه مطلوب من كل مصل، سواء كان إماماً أو مؤتماً أو منفرداً كما قدمنا. (و) الحادي عشر : أنه لا يترك ( تسبيح الركوع والسجودِ)؛ لما قدمنا أنه فرض عند البعض، وهـو سنة مؤكدة عندنا، فلا يُترك للكسل. (وَ) الثاني عشر : ( لا يَأْتِي) الإمام (بالدعاء) قبل السلام ( إن مل القوم به، وينبغي له الدعاء بما قصر لئلا يترك السنة. (و) الثالث عشر: أنه ( لا تُقضى التراويح) أصلاً بفَواتِهَا) عن وقتها، منفرداً ولا بجماعة) على الأصح؛ لأن القضاء من خصائص الواجبات، وإن قضاها كان نفلاً مستحباً لا تراويح. تنبيه: قدمنا صحة صلاة التراويح جالساً مع القدرة على القيام في الصحيح، لكن مع الكراهة، كما يكره للمقتدي أن يقعد فيها، فإذا أراد الإمام أن يركع يقوم، لما فيه من إظهار التكاسل في الصلاة، والتشبه بالمنافقين، قال تعالى: ﴿ وَإِذَا قَامُوا إِلَى الصَّلَوةِ قَامُوا كُسَالَى [النساء : ١٤٢] كذا في «شرح المنية»، وهذا بخلاف المتهجد، إذا صلى جالساً ثم قام، كما قدمنا (۱) في صفة تهجد النبي ، وذلك لما فيه من مخالفة الإمام، ولما فيه من القول بلزوم القيام في التراويح، وتكره مع غلبة النوم، فينصرف حتى يستيقظ لأن في الصلاة مع النوم تهاوناً، وغفلة، وترك التدبر، ولا خصوصية لها بهذا بل كل الصلوات كذلك، وقال في زاد الأئمة» : اختلفوا في التراويح أنها سنة الوقت أم سنـة الصوم، والأصح أنها سنة الوقت؛ لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: ( وقيام ليله » (۳)، حتى إن المريض المفطر والمسافر والحائضة والنفساء إذا طهرتا، والكافر إذا أسلم في آخر اليوم، يُسن لهم التراويح، فكيف يعذر المقيم الصحيح الصائم في تركها ؟ وذكر البقالي عن أبي حفص فيمن وجد القوم في الصلاة، ولا يدري أنها المكتوبة أم التراويح أنه يكبر وينوي صلاة الإمام مقتدياً بــه، فإن كان في المكتوبة فهي هي، وإن كانت ترويحة فإنه يفرغ منها، ثم يصلي العشاء؛ لعدم التردد في أصل النية، كذا في مجمع الروايات» والله أعلم.
And if the congregation becomes bored, according to the chosen view, he does not abandon the thana, and the tasbih of ruku' and sujud, and he does not perform the supplication if the congregation becomes bored because of it. And tarawih is not made up if its time passes, individually or in congregation. (And if the congregation becomes bored with that according to the chosen view) because it is from their laziness, so it is not followed. (And) the tenth: That he does not abandon the thana in the opening of every pair (of rak'ahs) because it is required from every person praying, whether imam, follower, or alone, as we have presented. (And) the eleventh: That he does not abandon the tasbih of ruku' and sujud because we have presented that it is obligatory according to some, and it is a confirmed sunnah according to us, so it is not abandoned due to laziness. (And) the twelfth: That the imam does not perform the supplication before the salutation if the congregation becomes bored because of it, and he should make a brief supplication so as not to leave the sunnah. (And) the thirteenth: That tarawih is not made up at all if its time passes, individually or in congregation, according to the most correct view, because making up is a characteristic of obligations, and if he makes it up, it becomes a recommended supererogatory prayer, not tarawih. A note: We have previously presented the validity of praying tarawih while sitting despite ability to stand according to the correct view, but with dislike, just as it is disliked for the follower to sit in it. So when the imam wants to bow, he stands, because of showing laziness in prayer and resembling hypocrites. Allah says: 'And when they stand up for prayer, they stand up lazily' [4:142]. Thus in Sharh al-Munya. And this is different from the tahajjud if he prays sitting then stands, as we have presented in the description of the Prophet's tahajjud. And that is because of opposing the imam and because of the statement that standing in tarawih is necessary. And it is disliked when overcome by sleep, so he should leave until he wakes up, because praying while sleepy involves negligence, heedlessness, and lack of reflection. And this is not specific to tarawih; rather all prayers are like that. And it was said in Zad al-A'imma: They differed concerning tarawih: is it a sunnah of the time or a sunnah of fasting? The most correct is that it is a sunnah of the time, due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'And its night prayer' [reference], so much so that the sick person who is not fasting, the traveler, the menstruating woman and the postpartum woman if they become pure, and the disbeliever who becomes Muslim at the end of the day, tarawih is prescribed for them. So how can the resident healthy fasting person be excused for abandoning it? And al-Baqqali mentioned from Abu Hafs regarding one who finds the congregation in prayer and does not know whether it is the obligatory prayer or tarawih: he should say takbir and intend the prayer of the imam following him. If it is the obligatory prayer, then it is that; if it is a tarawih rak'ah, then he completes it and then prays Isha, because there is no confusion in the basic intention. Thus in Majma' al-Riwayat. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 434

Commentary
This passage presents several rulings for the imam of tarawih. It starts by summarizing that if the congregation becomes bored, the imam should still not abandon the opening glorification (thana) and the tasbih of ruku' and sujud; but he should not make a long supplication (dua) if the congregation is bored. Then it details each: the tenth ruling: thana is not abandoned because it is required in every prayer. The eleventh: tasbih of ruku' and sujud is a confirmed sunnah, not to be left for laziness. The twelfth: the imam should avoid lengthy dua if the congregation is bored, but should still make a short one to maintain the sunnah. The thirteenth ruling: missed tarawih are not made up after their time; if one prays them later, they count as nafl (voluntary) not as tarawih. Then a note elaborates: praying tarawih while sitting with ability to stand is valid but disliked, especially for the follower, as it resembles hypocrisy. The imam should stand when bowing. Also, praying when overcome with sleep is disliked; one should wait until alert. The commentary concludes with a discussion of whether tarawih is a sunnah of time or of fasting; the correct view is that it is a sunnah of the night time, so even those not fasting (sick, traveler, etc.) should pray it. Finally, a practical ruling: if one joins a congregation unsure if it is tarawih or fard, he follows the imam with general intention.

Key Terms
الثناء (al-thana): The opening glorification (subhanaka allahumma wa bihamdika...) recited after the takbir in prayer.
التسبيح (al-tasbih): The glorifications (subhana rabbiya al-azim, subhana rabbiya al-a'la) said in ruku' and sujud.
القضاء (al-qada): Performing a missed act of worship after its designated time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person misses tarawih during Ramadan, can he make it up later?
A) Yes, it is wajib to make up.
B) Yes, but it counts as tarawih only if made up in congregation.
C) No, it cannot be made up as tarawih; but he can pray nafl.
D) No, it is lost and cannot be reclaimed.

Key Takeaway
In tarawih, the imam must preserve the sunnah acts of thana and tasbih, may shorten dua for congregation, and missed tarawih are not made up because qada is only for obligations.

Salah — Prayer

Rulings on Taraweeh: Persisting in Dhikr and Not Making Qada
Setting out rulings of taraweeh: persisting in dhikr, avoiding du'a when congregation tired, and no makeup.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on omitting thana' and tasbih due to congregation boredom, and explain why taraweeh is not made up after its time.

Core Idea
Taraweeh's sunan are not abandoned for laziness, and it is never made up because qada is only for wajib.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah presents three key rulings regarding taraweeh prayer in the Hanafi school. The first emphasizes that the opening praise (thana') and the tasbih of bowing and prostration must not be omitted even if the congregation is bored. The second advises the imam to shorten but not omit the supplication before salam when the congregation is tired. The third and most significant ruling states that missed taraweeh is never made up, whether individually or in congregation, because making up (qada) is a characteristic of obligatory acts only. These rulings demonstrate the structured yet flexible nature of taraweeh as a confirmed voluntary prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three main rulings
Read the passage and extract the three distinct rulings: (1) not leaving thana' and tasbih, (2) not reciting long du'a if congregation is bored, (3) taraweeh is not made up after its time.
2
Understand the basis for not leaving thana' and tasbih
Note that the text gives two reasons: thana' is required from every person praying (imam, follower, alone), and tasbih is a confirmed sunna (sunna mu'akkada) in the Hanafi school, not to be abandoned due to laziness.
Some scholars consider tasbih fard; Hanafis treat it as sunna mu'akkada.
3
Analyze the ruling on du'a before salam
The imam should avoid a lengthy supplication if the congregation is bored, but he should still make a brief du'a to preserve the sunna. This balances the sunna with consideration for the congregation.
4
Grasp the principle behind no qada
The key principle: qada (making up) is a characteristic of wajib acts, not sunan. Since taraweeh is a sunna, if one performs it later, it becomes a recommended nafl, not taraweeh. This is the relied-upon view (al-ashah).
The passage also notes that praying taraweeh while sitting is valid but disliked, and discusses joining an unknown congregation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو مل القوم، على المختار ولا يَتْرُكُ الثَّناء، وتسبيح الركوع والسجود ، ولا يأتي بالدعاء، إن مل القوم. ولا تُقضى التراويح بفواتها، منفرداً ولا بجماعة.
(ولو مل القومُ) بذلك عَلَى المختار)، لأنه عين الكسل منهم فلا يتبع (وَ) العاشر: أنه ( لا يَتْرُكُ الثناء) في افتتاح كل شفع؛ لأنه مطلوب من كل مصل، سواء كان إماماً أو مؤتماً أو منفرداً كما قدمنا. (و) الحادي عشر : أنه لا يترك ( تسبيح الركوع والسجودِ)؛ لما قدمنا أنه فرض عند البعض، وهـو سنة مؤكدة عندنا، فلا يُترك للكسل. (وَ) الثاني عشر : ( لا يَأْتِي) الإمام (بالدعاء) قبل السلام ( إن مل القوم به، وينبغي له الدعاء بما قصر لئلا يترك السنة. (و) الثالث عشر: أنه ( لا تُقضى التراويح) أصلاً بفَواتِهَا) عن وقتها، منفرداً ولا بجماعة) على الأصح؛ لأن القضاء من خصائص الواجبات، وإن قضاها كان نفلاً مستحباً لا تراويح. تنبيه: قدمنا صحة صلاة التراويح جالساً مع القدرة على القيام في الصحيح، لكن مع الكراهة، كما يكره للمقتدي أن يقعد فيها، فإذا أراد الإمام أن يركع يقوم، لما فيه من إظهار التكاسل في الصلاة، والتشبه بالمنافقين، قال تعالى: ﴿ وَإِذَا قَامُوا إِلَى الصَّلَوةِ قَامُوا كُسَالَى [النساء : ١٤٢] كذا في «شرح المنية»، وهذا بخلاف المتهجد، إذا صلى جالساً ثم قام، كما قدمنا (۱) في صفة تهجد النبي ، وذلك لما فيه من مخالفة الإمام، ولما فيه من القول بلزوم القيام في التراويح، وتكره مع غلبة النوم، فينصرف حتى يستيقظ لأن في الصلاة مع النوم تهاوناً، وغفلة، وترك التدبر، ولا خصوصية لها بهذا بل كل الصلوات كذلك، وقال في زاد الأئمة» : اختلفوا في التراويح أنها سنة الوقت أم سنـة الصوم، والأصح أنها سنة الوقت؛ لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: ( وقيام ليله » (۳)، حتى إن المريض المفطر والمسافر والحائضة والنفساء إذا طهرتا، والكافر إذا أسلم في آخر اليوم، يُسن لهم التراويح، فكيف يعذر المقيم الصحيح الصائم في تركها ؟ وذكر البقالي عن أبي حفص فيمن وجد القوم في الصلاة، ولا يدري أنها المكتوبة أم التراويح أنه يكبر وينوي صلاة الإمام مقتدياً بــه، فإن كان في المكتوبة فهي هي، وإن كانت ترويحة فإنه يفرغ منها، ثم يصلي العشاء؛ لعدم التردد في أصل النية، كذا في مجمع الروايات» والله أعلم.
(۱) ص .(٤١٨)
(۲) تقدم تخريجه ص (٤٢٨)، بلفظ: «وَسَنَنْتُ لَكُمْ قِيَامَهُ».
And if the congregation becomes bored, according to the preferred view he does not leave the thana' (opening praise), and the tasbih of bowing and prostration, and he does not come with the supplication if the congregation is bored. And taraweeh is not made up after its time passes, whether individually or in congregation. (And if the congregation becomes bored) with that according to the preferred view, because it is the essence of laziness from them so they are not followed. And the tenth: that he does not leave the thana' at the beginning of each set of two rak'ahs, because it is required from every person praying, whether imam, follower, or alone as we have presented. And the eleventh: that he does not leave the tasbih of bowing and prostration, because we have presented that it is fard according to some, and it is a confirmed sunna according to us, so it is not left due to laziness. And the twelfth: the imam does not come with the supplication before the salam if the congregation is bored with it, and he should supplicate briefly so as not to leave the sunna. And the thirteenth: that taraweeh is not made up at all after its time passes, whether individually or in congregation, according to the most correct view, because making up is a characteristic of obligatory acts, and if he makes it up, it becomes a recommended nafl, not taraweeh. A note: we have presented the validity of praying taraweeh while sitting despite ability to stand according to the correct view, but with dislike, just as it is disliked for the follower to sit in it, so when the imam intends to bow he stands, because there is in it an appearance of laziness in prayer and resemblance to the hypocrites, Allah said: {And when they stand for prayer they stand lazily} [al-Nisa: 142]. Thus in Sharh al-Munyah, and this is contrary to the one who prays at night, if he prays sitting then stands, as we have presented in the description of the Prophet's night prayer, because of the opposition to the imam, and because of the statement that standing is necessary in taraweeh. And it is disliked when sleep overcomes one, so he should leave until he wakes up, because prayer with sleep is carelessness, heedlessness, and lack of reflection, and this is not specific to taraweeh but all prayers are like that. And it is said in Zad al-A'immah: They disagreed about taraweeh whether it is a sunna of the time or a sunna of fasting, and the correct view is that it is a sunna of the time, because of his saying, peace be upon him: 'And standing its night' (3) such that even the sick who breaks fast, the traveler, the menstruating woman and the woman in post-partum bleeding when they become pure, and the disbeliever if he accepts Islam at the end of the day, taraweeh is sunna for them. So how can the resident healthy fasting person be excused in leaving it? And al-Baqqali narrated from Abu Hafs about one who finds the people in prayer and does not know whether it is the obligatory prayer or taraweeh, that he says the takbir and intends to pray with the imam following him. If it is the obligatory prayer, then it is that. If it is a taraweeh, he finishes it then prays the 'Isha, because there is no hesitation in the original intention. Thus in Majma' al-Riwayat. And Allah knows best. (1) p. 418. (2) Its takhrij preceded on p. 428, with the wording: 'I prescribed for you its standing (qiyam).'
Source pages p. 434

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah presents several rulings regarding taraweeh prayer as a Sharh on Nur al-Idah. It begins by stating that if the congregation becomes bored, the imam should not omit the thana' (the opening praise) or the tasbih of bowing and prostration. The reason given is that laziness of the followers is not a valid excuse to abandon these sunan acts. The thana' is required from every person praying, and the tasbih, though considered a confirmed sunna (sunna mu'akkada) in the Hanafi school, is not to be left. Next, the imam is advised not to recite a long du'a before salam if the congregation is bored, but he should still make a brief supplication to preserve the sunna. Then the most significant ruling: taraweeh is not made up after its time passes, whether individually or in congregation, because qada (making up) applies only to wajib acts, and taraweeh is a voluntary sunna. The commentator then adds a note: although praying taraweeh while sitting is valid even when one can stand, it is disliked, as it shows laziness and resembles hypocrites. The text then cites a quote from Zad al-A'immah clarifying that taraweeh is a sunna of the time (specifically the nights of Ramadan), not of fasting, as evidenced by the fact that those who are not fasting (e.g., sick, traveler, menstruating women) may still perform it. Finally, a practical ruling is given for one who joins a congregation not knowing if it is 'Isha or taraweeh: he should intend to follow the imam, and if it is taraweeh, he completes it and then prays 'Isha. These rulings emphasize the flexible yet structured nature of taraweeh as a supererogatory prayer.

Key Terms
الثناء (al-thana'): The opening praise recited at the beginning of prayer, specifically 'Subhanaka Allahumma' etc.
تسبيح الركوع والسجود (tasbih al-ruku' wa al-sujud): The glorification of Allah ('Subhana Rabbiyal-Adheem' and 'Subhana Rabbiyal-A'la') during bowing and prostration.
قضاء (qada'): Making up a missed act of worship after its specified time.
التراويح (al-tarawih): The special night prayers during Ramadan, performed after 'Isha prayer, usually in congregation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on making up missed taraweeh prayers?
A) It is obligatory to make them up.
B) They are not made up; if performed later they become nafl, not taraweeh.
C) They are made up only if missed with a valid excuse.
D) They are made up only in congregation.

Key Takeaway
Taraweeh is a sunna; its associated dhikr is not abandoned for laziness, and missed taraweeh is never made up because qada is only for wajib acts.

Salah — Prayer

The True Qibla: Validity of Prayer Inside and on Top of the Ka'bah
Establishing the qibla definition and its implications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of qibla as the entire buq'ah and its airspace, and apply it to determine the ruling of prayer inside and on top of the Ka'bah.

Core Idea
The qibla is the whole precinct of the Ka'bah, not just its building.

A common question is whether prayer inside the Ka'bah is valid, since one cannot face the building itself when inside. This lesson explains the Hanafi position: the qibla is the entire ground (buq'ah) and airspace. Thus prayer inside and on top is valid, though praying on top is disliked (makruh) due to adab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi definition of qibla
Find where the text explicitly defines qibla as the ground (buq'ah) of the Ka'bah and its airspace up to the sky.
Key phrase: 'القبلة اسم لبقعة الكعبة المحدودة وهوائها إلى عنان السماء'
2
Examine the proofs
The text cites the hadith of Bilal (Prophet prayed inside), the Quranic verse commanding purification, and the practice of Companions praying to the ground when the building was removed.
Hadith is from Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Understand the madhhab dispute
Other schools may consider the building itself as qibla. The Hanafi proof includes the example of praying on Mount Abu Qubays with no building in front yet valid.
The thamarah al-khilaf: inward prayer facing any direction is valid only in Hanafi.
4
Derive the ruling for inside
Since qibla is the ground/air, prayer inside is valid facing any part of the interior.
Support from verse 2:144 'turn your faces toward it'.
5
Derive the ruling for on top
Prayer on top is also valid (same qibla) but makruh tanzihan due to placing oneself above the Ka'bah.
Makruh because of disrespect, not invalidity.
