اعلم أن شروط صحة الصلاة استقبال جزء من بقعة الكعبة أو هو ائها؛ لأن القبلة اسم لبقعة الكعبة المحدودة وهوائها إلى عنان السماء عندنا، كما في ( العناية » ، وليس بناؤها قبلة؛ لأنـه لـو صلى على جبل أبي قبيس لا يكون بين يديه شيء من بناء الكعبة وصحت صلاته، ولذا حين أُزيــل البناء في زمن عبد الله بن الزبير الله صلى الصحابة لله إلى البقعة، وكذا فيما بعده، ولم ينقل عنهم أنهم اتخذوا سترة. وقال تعالى: ﴿وَحَيْثُ مَا كُنتُمْ فَوَلُّوا وُجُوهَكُمْ شَطْرَهُ ﴾ [البقرة : ١٤٤] فكان الشرط البقعة أو هواءها دون البناء، وإن كان البناء المرتفع يسمى كعبة؛ لأنه مأخوذ من الارتفاع والنتوء، ومنـه الكاعب، (صح فرضٌ ونفل) صلاهما (فيها ) أي: في داخلها إلى أي جزء مـنـهـا توجـه المصلي؛ لحديث بلال : ( أنَّه عليه الصلاة والسلام دَخَلَ البَيْتَ وَصَلَّى فِيهِ » ) ، وصلاته وإن كــانـت نـفـلاً فالفرض في معناه، فيما هو من شرائط الجواز دون الأركان، ولأنها صلاة استجمعت شرائطها بوجود استقبال القبلة، لأن استقبال جميعها ليس بشرط، كما لو صلى خارجها، ولقوله تعالى: ﴿ أَن طَهِّرَا بَيْتِي لِلطَّابِفِينَ وَالْعَاكِفِينَ وَالرُّكَّعِ السُّجُودِ [البقرة : ١٢٥] فإن الأمر بالتطهير فيـه ظـاهـر في صحتها فيه، إذ لا معنى لتطهير المكان لأجل الصلاة، وهي لا تجوز في ذلك المكان، وكذا) صــح فــرض ونفل، (فوقها، وإن لم يتخذ المصلي (سُترةً لكنّه مكروه لـه الصلاة فوقها (لإساءة الأدب باستعلائه عليها)، وترك تعظيمها. ومن جعل ظهرَهُ إلى غير وجه إمامه فيها، أو فوقها) بأن كان وجهه إلى ظهر إمامه، أو إلى جنب إمامه، أو ظهره إلى جنب إمامه، أو ظهره إلى ظهر إمامه، أو جنبه إلى وجه إمامه، أو جنبه إلى جنب إمامه، متوجهاً لغير جهته، أو وجهه إلى وجه إمامه، (صح) اقتداؤه في هذه الصور السبع، إلا أنه يكره إن قابل وجهه وجه إمامه، وليس بينهما حائل؛ لما تقدم من كراهته لشبهه بعبادة الصورة، وكل جانب قبلة، والتقدم والتأخر إنما يظهر عند اتحاد الجهة، وهي مختلفة في جوف الكعبة وقوله: (وإن جعل ظهره إلى وجهِ إمامه لا يصح اقتداؤه، تصريح بما علم التزاماً مــن
(۲)
(1) أخرجه البخاري من حديث عبد الله بن عمر في الصلاة، باب الصلاة بين السواري (٥٠٥)، ومسلم في الحج، باب استحباب دخول الكعبة للحاج وغيره للصائم فيها والدعاء في نواحيها كلها ١٣٢٩. (٢) ص (٣٦٩ ).
Chapter: Prayer in the Ka'bah.
Know that the conditions for the validity of prayer is facing a part of the ground of the Ka'bah or its airspace, because the qibla is the name for the limited ground of the Ka'bah and its airspace up to the canopy of the sky according to us, as in al-'Inayah. Its building is not the qibla, because if one prays on Mount Abu Qubays, there is nothing of the building of the Ka'bah before him, yet his prayer is valid. Likewise when the building was removed in the time of Abdullah ibn al-Zubair (may Allah be pleased with them), the Companions prayed facing the ground, and similarly after that, and it is not reported that they took a sutra (screen). And Allah Most High said: {And wherever you [may be], turn your faces toward it} [al-Baqarah: 144], so the condition is the ground or its airspace, not the building, even though the elevated building is called Ka'bah, because it is derived from height and prominence, and from it is 'al-ka'ab' (the young girl's swelling breast). (Valid is fard and nafl) prayers performed (in it) i.e., in its interior, in whatever direction the worshipper faces, because of the hadith of Bilal: 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) entered the House and prayed in it.' And his prayer, though it was nafl, the fard is in its meaning regarding what is from the conditions of permissibility not the pillars, and because it is a prayer that has combined its conditions by the existence of facing the qibla, because facing all of it is not a condition, just as if one prays outside it, and because of His saying: {Purify My House for those who circumambulate and those who stay and those who bow and prostrate} [al-Baqarah: 125], for the command to purify in it is apparent regarding its validity therein, since there is no meaning to purifying a place for prayer while prayer is not permissible in that place. And likewise) valid is fard and nafl (above it, even if the worshipper does not take a screen (sutra), but it is disliked for him to pray above it (due to bad manners of being above it) and abandoning its veneration. And whoever places his back to other than the face of his imam in it, or above it, such that his face is towards the imam's back, or towards the imam's side, or his back towards the imam's side, or his back towards the imam's back, or his side towards the imam's face, or his side towards the imam's side, facing other than his direction, or his face towards the imam's face, (valid) is his following in these seven forms, except that it is disliked if his face faces the imam's face and there is no barrier between them, because of what has preceded of its dislike due to resemblance to worshipping an image, and every side is a qibla, and advancement and delay only appear when the direction is unified, and they differ in the interior of the Ka'bah. And his statement: (And if he places his back towards the face of his imam, his following is not valid) is a clarification of what is known necessarily from...
(2)
(1) Recorded by al-Bukhari from the hadith of Abdullah ibn Umar in the Book of Prayer, Chapter: Prayer between Pillars (505), and Muslim in Hajj, Chapter: Recommendation of Entering the Ka'bah for the Pilgrim and Others for Prayer and Supplication in All Its Corners (1329). (2) p. (369).
Source pages p. 435

Commentary
This chapter from Imdad al-Fattah discusses the validity of prayer inside and on top of the Ka'bah, as well as the rules for following an imam in such settings. The commentator begins by clarifying a key principle: the qibla is not merely the building of the Ka'bah but the entire designated ground (buq'ah) and its airspace up to the sky. This is evident because praying on Mount Abu Qubays, where no part of the Ka'bah's structure is in front of the worshipper, is still valid. This principle is supported by the Quranic verse ordering turning towards the Ka'bah. Therefore, prayer inside the Ka'bah is valid regardless of which part of the interior one faces, as long as one faces some part of the Ka'bah's precinct. The hadith of Bilal confirms that the Prophet himself prayed inside the Ka'bah. Though his prayer was nafl, the same permissibility applies to fard prayers because the conditions for validity (like facing the qibla) are met; the ka'bah's entire interior is qibla. Similarly, praying on top of the Ka'bah is valid, but it is disliked (makruh) because it involves placing oneself above the Ka'bah, showing disrespect. Regarding congregational prayer, the text enumerates seven forms where following an imam inside or on top of the Ka'bah is valid, even if the follower is not directly behind the imam. These include: (1) follower's face towards imam's back, (2) follower's face towards imam's side, (3) follower's back towards imam's side, (4) follower's back towards imam's back, (5) follower's side towards imam's face, (6) follower's side towards imam's side, (7) follower's face towards imam's face. In all seven, the prayer is valid, but the seventh (face to face) is disliked if no barrier exists, as it resembles worshipping an idol. The only invalid case is when the follower's back is towards the imam's face, which makes following impossible.

Key Terms
الكعبة (al-Ka'bah): The sacred house in Mecca; here it refers to both the building and its entire precinct (buq'ah) including airspace.
القبلة (al-qiblah): The direction faced during prayer; in this context, it is the entire area of the Ka'bah's ground and airspace.
البقعة (al-buq'ah): The designated ground of the Ka'bah, the area considered sacred for prayer direction.
الاقتداء (al-iqtida'): Following an imam in congregational prayer; the conditions for validity when inside or atop the Ka'bah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the qibla?
A) The building of the Ka'bah.
B) The entire ground (buq'ah) and airspace of the Ka'bah.
C) The black stone.
D) The entire Masjid al-Haram.

Key Takeaway
Prayer inside and on top of the Ka'bah is valid because the qibla is the entire precinct, not just the structure.

Following an Imam Inside or On Top of the Ka'bah: Seven Valid Positions
Enumeration of permissible and impermissible follower positions inside the Ka'bah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the seven valid forms of iqtida' inside or on top of the Ka'bah and recognize the one invalid form.

Core Idea
Except when the follower's back is to the imam's face, all relative positions are valid for prayer inside the Ka'bah.

Congregational prayer inside the Ka'bah raises a unique challenge: since every direction is qibla, the usual alignment rules are different. This passage from Imdad al-Fattah lists seven valid follower positions and explains why only one arrangement—back to imam's face—invalidates the prayer.

Guided Path
1
List the seven valid forms
From the text, enumerate the seven relative positions where iqtida' is valid: follower's face to imam's back, face to side, back to side, back to back, side to face, side to side, face to face.
The text uses detailed descriptions; capture each.
2
Identify the invalid form
The text explicitly states that if the follower's back is towards the imam's face, the iqtida' is not valid.
This is the eighth possible arrangement.
3
Understand the disliked case
Face to face without barrier is valid but makruh, because it resembles worship of an image.
Makruh tanzihi, not invalid.
4
Relate to the qibla principle
Because every direction inside the Ka'bah is qibla, there is no single 'front' or 'back', so most alignments are acceptable.
Refer back to Lesson 1.

باب الصلاة في الكعبة
اعلم أن شروط صحة الصلاة استقبال جزء من بقعة الكعبة أو هو ائها؛ لأن القبلة اسم لبقعة الكعبة المحدودة وهوائها إلى عنان السماء عندنا، كما في ( العناية » ، وليس بناؤها قبلة؛ لأنـه لـو صلى على جبل أبي قبيس لا يكون بين يديه شيء من بناء الكعبة وصحت صلاته، ولذا حين أُزيــل البناء في زمن عبد الله بن الزبير الله صلى الصحابة لله إلى البقعة، وكذا فيما بعده، ولم ينقل عنهم أنهم اتخذوا سترة. وقال تعالى: ﴿وَحَيْثُ مَا كُنتُمْ فَوَلُّوا وُجُوهَكُمْ شَطْرَهُ ﴾ [البقرة : ١٤٤] فكان الشرط البقعة أو هواءها دون البناء، وإن كان البناء المرتفع يسمى كعبة؛ لأنه مأخوذ من الارتفاع والنتوء، ومنـه الكاعب، (صح فرضٌ ونفل) صلاهما (فيها ) أي: في داخلها إلى أي جزء مـنـهـا توجـه المصلي؛ لحديث بلال : ( أنَّه عليه الصلاة والسلام دَخَلَ البَيْتَ وَصَلَّى فِيهِ » ) ، وصلاته وإن كــانـت نـفـلاً فالفرض في معناه، فيما هو من شرائط الجواز دون الأركان، ولأنها صلاة استجمعت شرائطها بوجود استقبال القبلة، لأن استقبال جميعها ليس بشرط، كما لو صلى خارجها، ولقوله تعالى: ﴿ أَن طَهِّرَا بَيْتِي لِلطَّابِفِينَ وَالْعَاكِفِينَ وَالرُّكَّعِ السُّجُودِ [البقرة : ١٢٥] فإن الأمر بالتطهير فيـه ظـاهـر في صحتها فيه، إذ لا معنى لتطهير المكان لأجل الصلاة، وهي لا تجوز في ذلك المكان، وكذا) صــح فــرض ونفل، (فوقها، وإن لم يتخذ المصلي (سُترةً لكنّه مكروه لـه الصلاة فوقها (لإساءة الأدب باستعلائه عليها)، وترك تعظيمها. ومن جعل ظهرَهُ إلى غير وجه إمامه فيها، أو فوقها) بأن كان وجهه إلى ظهر إمامه، أو إلى جنب إمامه، أو ظهره إلى جنب إمامه، أو ظهره إلى ظهر إمامه، أو جنبه إلى وجه إمامه، أو جنبه إلى جنب إمامه، متوجهاً لغير جهته، أو وجهه إلى وجه إمامه، (صح) اقتداؤه في هذه الصور السبع، إلا أنه يكره إن قابل وجهه وجه إمامه، وليس بينهما حائل؛ لما تقدم من كراهته لشبهه بعبادة الصورة، وكل جانب قبلة، والتقدم والتأخر إنما يظهر عند اتحاد الجهة، وهي مختلفة في جوف الكعبة وقوله: (وإن جعل ظهره إلى وجهِ إمامه لا يصح اقتداؤه، تصريح بما علم التزاماً مــن
(۲)
(1) أخرجه البخاري من حديث عبد الله بن عمر في الصلاة، باب الصلاة بين السواري (٥٠٥)، ومسلم في الحج، باب استحباب دخول الكعبة للحاج وغيره للصائم فيها والدعاء في نواحيها كلها ١٣٢٩. (٢) ص (٣٦٩ ).
Chapter: Prayer in the Ka'bah.
Know that the conditions for the validity of prayer is facing a part of the ground of the Ka'bah or its airspace, because the qibla is the name for the limited ground of the Ka'bah and its airspace up to the canopy of the sky according to us, as in al-'Inayah. Its building is not the qibla, because if one prays on Mount Abu Qubays, there is nothing of the building of the Ka'bah before him, yet his prayer is valid. Likewise when the building was removed in the time of Abdullah ibn al-Zubair (may Allah be pleased with them), the Companions prayed facing the ground, and similarly after that, and it is not reported that they took a sutra (screen). And Allah Most High said: {And wherever you [may be], turn your faces toward it} [al-Baqarah: 144], so the condition is the ground or its airspace, not the building, even though the elevated building is called Ka'bah, because it is derived from height and prominence, and from it is 'al-ka'ab' (the young girl's swelling breast). (Valid is fard and nafl) prayers performed (in it) i.e., in its interior, in whatever direction the worshipper faces, because of the hadith of Bilal: 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) entered the House and prayed in it.' And his prayer, though it was nafl, the fard is in its meaning regarding what is from the conditions of permissibility not the pillars, and because it is a prayer that has combined its conditions by the existence of facing the qibla, because facing all of it is not a condition, just as if one prays outside it, and because of His saying: {Purify My House for those who circumambulate and those who stay and those who bow and prostrate} [al-Baqarah: 125], for the command to purify in it is apparent regarding its validity therein, since there is no meaning to purifying a place for prayer while prayer is not permissible in that place. And likewise) valid is fard and nafl (above it, even if the worshipper does not take a screen (sutra), but it is disliked for him to pray above it (due to bad manners of being above it) and abandoning its veneration. And whoever places his back to other than the face of his imam in it, or above it, such that his face is towards the imam's back, or towards the imam's side, or his back towards the imam's side, or his back towards the imam's back, or his side towards the imam's face, or his side towards the imam's side, facing other than his direction, or his face towards the imam's face, (valid) is his following in these seven forms, except that it is disliked if his face faces the imam's face and there is no barrier between them, because of what has preceded of its dislike due to resemblance to worshipping an image, and every side is a qibla, and advancement and delay only appear when the direction is unified, and they differ in the interior of the Ka'bah. And his statement: (And if he places his back towards the face of his imam, his following is not valid) is a clarification of what is known necessarily from...
(2)
(1) Recorded by al-Bukhari from the hadith of Abdullah ibn Umar in the Book of Prayer, Chapter: Prayer between Pillars (505), and Muslim in Hajj, Chapter: Recommendation of Entering the Ka'bah for the Pilgrim and Others for Prayer and Supplication in All Its Corners (1329). (2) p. (369).
Source pages p. 435

Commentary
This chapter from Imdad al-Fattah discusses the validity of prayer inside and on top of the Ka'bah, as well as the rules for following an imam in such settings. The commentator begins by clarifying a key principle: the qibla is not merely the building of the Ka'bah but the entire designated ground (buq'ah) and its airspace up to the sky. This is evident because praying on Mount Abu Qubays, where no part of the Ka'bah's structure is in front of the worshipper, is still valid. This principle is supported by the Quranic verse ordering turning towards the Ka'bah. Therefore, prayer inside the Ka'bah is valid regardless of which part of the interior one faces, as long as one faces some part of the Ka'bah's precinct. The hadith of Bilal confirms that the Prophet himself prayed inside the Ka'bah. Though his prayer was nafl, the same permissibility applies to fard prayers because the conditions for validity (like facing the qibla) are met; the ka'bah's entire interior is qibla. Similarly, praying on top of the Ka'bah is valid, but it is disliked (makruh) because it involves placing oneself above the Ka'bah, showing disrespect. Regarding congregational prayer, the text enumerates seven forms where following an imam inside or on top of the Ka'bah is valid, even if the follower is not directly behind the imam. These include: (1) follower's face towards imam's back, (2) follower's face towards imam's side, (3) follower's back towards imam's side, (4) follower's back towards imam's back, (5) follower's side towards imam's face, (6) follower's side towards imam's side, (7) follower's face towards imam's face. In all seven, the prayer is valid, but the seventh (face to face) is disliked if no barrier exists, as it resembles worshipping an idol. The only invalid case is when the follower's back is towards the imam's face, which makes following impossible.

Key Terms
الكعبة (al-Ka'bah): The sacred house in Mecca; here it refers to both the building and its entire precinct (buq'ah) including airspace.
القبلة (al-qiblah): The direction faced during prayer; in this context, it is the entire area of the Ka'bah's ground and airspace.
البقعة (al-buq'ah): The designated ground of the Ka'bah, the area considered sacred for prayer direction.
الاقتداء (al-iqtida'): Following an imam in congregational prayer; the conditions for validity when inside or atop the Ka'bah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is the only invalid form of following an imam inside or on top of the Ka'bah?
A) Face to face without barrier.
B) Back to back.
C) Back to imam's face.
D) Side to side.

Key Takeaway
Inside the Ka'bah, as long as the follower's back is not towards the imam's face, the iqtida' is valid in any relative position.

Prayer Inside and On Top of the Kaaba: Ruling and Proofs
Ruling on prayer inside and atop the Kaaba and following the Imam therein

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on prayer inside and on top of the Kaaba, explain the definition of qibla as buq'ah, and identify the valid and invalid orientations for following an imam inside the Kaaba.

Core Idea
The Kaaba's area (buq'ah) is the qibla, not the building; prayer inside and on top is valid but the latter is disliked.

This lesson examines a unique case in Hanafi fiqh: praying inside or on top of the Kaaba. The ruling hinges on the definition of qibla — whether it is the building itself or its entire area and airspace. The Hanafi position is that the qibla is the buq'ah, making such prayers valid, though praying on top is disliked for disrespect. The passage also details the rules of following an imam inside the Kaaba, where orientation matters differently due to the multiple possible directions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the passage rules on two acts: praying inside the Kaaba and praying on top of it. For each, determine the hukm level (valid vs. invalid) and any associated dislike.
The ruling is 'sahih' (valid) for both, but 'makruh tanzihan' for on top.
2
Locate the dalil for the definition of qibla
The passage cites the Quranic verse 'turn your faces toward it' (2:144) and the hadith of Bilal that the Prophet prayed inside. Understand how these proofs establish that the qibla is the area (buq'ah) and airspace, not the building.
Also note the practical example of Mount Abu Qubais and the Companions' practice when the Kaaba was rebuilt.
3
Analyze the conditions for valid iqtida' (following the imam) inside the Kaaba
List the seven orientations where following the imam is valid, and the one where it is invalid (back to imam's face). Understand the reasoning: since every direction is a qibla inside the Kaaba, the usual rule of facing the qibla is modified.
The passage also notes that facing the imam directly is disliked but not invalid, unless there is no barrier.
4
Note the Hanafi unique definition of qibla
The commentary emphasizes that the condition for prayer is facing any part of the buq'ah (area) or its airspace. This is a distinct Hanafi view and explains why prayer inside the Kaaba is valid even if not facing the building itself.
This definition differs from other schools and is supported by istidlal from the Quran and the Companions' practice.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Take a concrete case: a person prays on top of the Kaaba without a sutra. According to the passage, the prayer is valid but makruh. Explain why: the sutra is not required because there is no need to prevent passage, but it is disliked due to showing dominance over the Kaaba.
This highlights the interplay between validity (sahih) and moral recommendation (makruh).

باب الصلاة في الكعبة
اعلم أن شروط صحة الصلاة استقبال جزء من بقعة الكعبة أو هوائها؛ لأن القبلة اسم لبقعة الكعبة المحدودة وهوائها إلى عنان السماء عندنا، كما في ( العناية » ، وليس بناؤها قبلة؛ لأنه لو صلى على جبل أبي قبيس لا يكون بين يديه شيء من بناء الكعبة وصحت صلاته، ولذا حين أُزيــل البناء في زمن عبد الله بن الزبير رضي الله عنه صلى الصحابة رضي الله عنهم إلى البقعة، وكذا فيما بعده، ولم ينقل عنهم أنهم اتخذوا سترة. وقال تعالى: ﴿وَحَيْثُ مَا كُنتُمْ فَوَلُّوا وُجُوهَكُمْ شَطْرَهُ ﴾ [البقرة : ١٤٤] فكان الشرط البقعة أو هواءها دون البناء، وإن كان البناء المرتفع يسمى كعبة؛ لأنه مأخوذ من الارتفاع والنتوء، ومنه الكاعب، (صح فرضٌ ونفل) صلاهما (فيها ) أي: في داخلها إلى أي جزء منها توجه المصلي؛ لحديث بلال : ( أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام دَخَلَ البَيْتَ وَصَلَّى فِيهِ » ) ، وصلاته وإن كانت نفلاً فالفرض في معناه، فيما هو من شرائط الجواز دون الأركان، ولأنها صلاة استجمعت شرائطها بوجود استقبال القبلة، لأن استقبال جميعها ليس بشرط، كما لو صلى خارجها، ولقوله تعالى: ﴿ أَن طَهِّرَا بَيْتِي لِلطَّابِفِينَ وَالْعَاكِفِينَ وَالرُّكَّعِ السُّجُودِ [البقرة : ١٢٥] فإن الأمر بالتطهير فيه ظاهر في صحتها فيه، إذ لا معنى لتطهير المكان لأجل الصلاة، وهي لا تجوز في ذلك المكان، وكذا) صح فرض ونفل، (فوقها، وإن لم يتخذ المصلي (سُترةً لكنّه مكروه لـه الصلاة فوقها (لإساءة الأدب باستعلائه عليها)، وترك تعظيمها. ومن جعل ظهرَهُ إلى غير وجه إمامه فيها، أو فوقها) بأن كان وجهه إلى ظهر إمامه، أو إلى جنب إمامه، أو ظهره إلى جنب إمامه، أو ظهره إلى ظهر إمامه، أو جنبه إلى وجه إمامه، أو جنبه إلى جنب إمامه، متوجهاً لغير جهته، أو وجهه إلى وجه إمامه، (صح) اقتداؤه في هذه الصور السبع، إلا أنه يكره إن قابل وجهه وجه إمامه، وليس بينهما حائل؛ لما تقدم من كراهته لشبهه بعبادة الصورة، وكل جانب قبلة، والتقدم والتأخر إنما يظهر عند اتحاد الجهة، وهي مختلفة في جوف الكعبة وقوله: (وإن جعل ظهره إلى وجهِ إمامه لا يصح اقتداؤه، تصريح بما علم التزاماً من السابق؛ لإيضاح الحكم.
Chapter: Prayer in the Kaaba. The performance of obligatory and supererogatory prayers inside it is valid, and likewise on top of it, even if one does not take a sutra. But it is disliked (makruh) due to bad manners in showing dominance over it. Whoever makes his back to other than the face of his imam inside it or on top of it, his following is valid, but if he makes his back to the face of his imam, it is not valid. Chapter: Prayer in the Kaaba. Know that the condition for the validity of prayer is facing a part of the area of the Kaaba or its airspace, because 'qibla' is the name of the defined area of the Kaaba and its airspace up to the sky according to us, as in al-'Inaya. Its building is not the qibla, because if one prays on Mount Abu Qubais, there is nothing of the building of the Kaaba in front of him, yet his prayer is valid. Hence when the building was removed in the time of 'Abdullah ibn al-Zubayr (may Allah be pleased with him), the Companions prayed facing the area, and likewise after that, and it is not reported that they took a sutra. Allah Almighty said: 'And wherever you are, turn your faces toward it' (al-Baqarah 2:144). Thus the condition is the area or its airspace, not the building, although the elevated building is called Ka'ba because it is derived from height and protrusion, and from it is al-ka'ib (a girl whose breast begins to swell). (The performance of obligatory and supererogatory prayers) both of them are valid (inside it) i.e., inside its interior, facing any part of it the worshipper turns to, due to the hadith of Bilal that the Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him) entered the House and prayed in it. And even if his prayer was supererogatory, an obligatory prayer is similar to it in terms of what is part of conditions of permissibility, not the pillars, and because it is a prayer that fulfills its conditions by the existence of facing the qibla, because facing all of it is not a condition, as if he prayed outside it, and due to the saying of Allah Almighty: 'Purify My House for those who circumambulate it and those who stay there and those who bow and prostrate' (al-Baqarah 2:125). For the command to purify in it is evident in the validity of prayer therein, since there is no meaning to purifying a place for prayer if prayer is not permissible in that place. Likewise, (the performance of obligatory and supererogatory prayers is valid) on top of it, even if the worshipper does not take a sutra, but it is disliked for him to pray on top of it due to bad manners in showing dominance over it and abandoning its reverence. And whoever makes his back to other than the face of his imam inside it or on top of it, such that his face is to the back of his imam, or to the side of his imam, or his back to the side of his imam, or his back to the back of his imam, or his side to the face of his imam, or his side to the side of his imam, facing other than his direction, or his face to the face of his imam, his following is valid in these seven forms, except that it is disliked if he faces the face of his imam and there is no barrier between them, due to what was previously mentioned of its dislike due to resemblance to worship of images. And every side is a qibla, and precedence and lateness only appear when the direction is unified, and they differ in the interior of the Kaaba. And his saying: 'And if he makes his back to the face of his imam, his following is not valid' is a clarification of what is known implicitly from what preceded to explain the ruling.
Source pages p. 435

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from Nur al-Idah expanded in Imdad al-Fattah. It begins by stating the basic ruling: obligatory (fard) and supererogatory (nafl) prayers are valid inside the Kaaba and on top of it, even without a sutra (a barrier in front). However, praying on top is makruh tanzihan (disliked) due to disrespect. Then it discusses following an imam inside or on top: if the follower makes his back to any direction other than the imam's face, the following is valid; but if his back is directly to the imam's face, it is invalid. The commentary then explains the Hanafi definition of qibla: it is the entire area (buq'ah) of the Kaaba and its airspace, not just the building. Evidence: the hadith of Bilal that the Prophet prayed inside, and the verse commanding to turn towards 'shathrahu' (the direction of the Kaaba), which Hanafis interpret as the area. The verse about purifying the House implies prayer is valid inside. The seven cases of valid following relative to the imam are enumerated, with the exception that facing the imam directly is disliked (not invalid) as it resembles image worship. The invalidity only occurs when the follower's back is to the imam's face, because that constitutes the follower being ahead of the imam in direction, which is prohibited.

Key Terms
كعبة (ka'bah): The physical building in Mecca, but the qibla is its entire area (buq'ah) and airspace.
سُترة (sutrah): An object placed in front of a praying person to prevent passage, not required inside the Kaaba.
اقتداء (iqtida'): Following the imam in prayer; the rules of validity depend on the relative direction of the follower and imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a valid orientation for following an imam inside the Kaaba according to the Hanafi madhhab?
A) The follower's face is to the imam's back.
B) The follower's back is to the imam's face.
C) The follower's side is to the imam's side.
D) The follower's face is to the imam's side.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi madhhab holds that prayer inside the Kaaba is valid because the qibla is the buq'ah (area), and following an imam inside is valid in all orientations except when the follower's back is directly opposite the imam's face.

Following an Imam Inside the Kaaba from Outside
Conditions for following imam inside Kaaba and circle scenario.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for valid following (iqtida') of an imam inside the Kaaba and identify the exception when followers are around the Kaaba.

Core Idea
Following an imam inside the Kaaba is valid if you can see him; being closer to the Kaaba only invalidates if you face the same direction.

The Kaaba presents unique spatial challenges for congregational prayer. This passage clarifies two scenarios: when the imam prays inside the Kaaba and the followers are outside, and when followers form a circle around the Kaaba with the imam outside. Understanding these rulings helps you distinguish between valid and invalid configurations based on visibility and direction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State the act: a person outside the Kaaba following an imam inside. The ruling: valid (sahih) if the door is open.
The door condition ensures the follower can see the imam's movements.
2
Analyze the exception for the circle scenario
When followers encircle the Kaaba and the imam is outside, following is valid for all except one who is closer to the Kaaba than the imam in the imam's direction.
Closeness alone does not invalidate; direction matters. If the follower's direction differs, precedence is not an issue.
3
Understand the reasoning
The text compares the Kaaba to a mihrab: standing inside it is like standing in a mihrab. The condition of the door being open is for seeing the imam; if hearing through relay suffices, the door may be closed.
This is a qiyas reasoning: the Kaaba is like a mosque.
4
Apply the rule to a practical case
Imagine a crowd around the Kaaba all facing it. The imam is near one side. A follower on the opposite side is closer to the Kaaba than the imam but faces the Kaaba the same way? Actually if all face the Kaaba, they all face the same direction, so the follower closer to the Kaaba than the imam would be ahead. But if the follower faces a different direction (e.g., towards the Yemeni corner while imam faces a specific direction), then closeness does not matter.
The key is unity of direction (jihah).
5
Note the epistemological weight
The ruling is from later Hanafi works (al-Tabyin, al-Ikhtiyar) but consistent with Zahir al-Riwayah. It is the mufta bihi position.
The authority_weight is fatawa mutakhkhirin.

Source Text

وصح الاقتداء خارجها بإمام فيها؛ والباب مفتوح. وإن تحلّقوا حولها، والإمامُ خارجها صح؛ إلا لِمَنْ كان أقرب إليها في جهة إمامه. (وصح الاقتداء) لمن كان (خارجها بإمـام فـيـهـا ) أي: في جوفها، سواء كان معه جماعة فيها أو لم يكن (وَ) هذا الباب مفتوح) لأنه كقيامه في المحراب في غيرها من المساجد، كما في ( التبيين»، و « الاختيار » ، ولعل اشتراط فتح الباب ليعلم انتقال الإمام بالنظر إليه، فلو سمع انتقالاته بالتبليغ والباب مغلق، لا مانع من صحة الاقتداء، لعدم المانع منه، كما قدمناه (۱) في شروط صحة الاقتداء، وإن تحلّقوا حولها، والإمام) ( لِمَنْ كان أقرب إليـهـا ) مـن إمامه وهـو ( في جهة إمامه)؛ لتقدمه على إمامه، وأما من هو أقرب إليها من إمامه وليس هو في جهته، فاقتداؤه صحيح؛ لأن التقدم والتأخر لا يظهر إلا عند اتحاد الجانب، المتوجه إليه كل منهما.
And the following (of a person) outside the Kaaba with an imam inside it is valid, while the door is open. And if they gather around it, and the imam is outside it, it is valid, except for one who is closer to it in the direction of his imam. (And the following is valid) for one who is (outside it with an imam inside it) i.e., in its interior, whether there is a congregation with him inside or not, (and) while the door is open, because it is like him standing in the mihrab in other mosques, as in al-Tabyin and al-Ikhtiyar. Perhaps the condition of the door being open is so that he can know the movements of the imam by looking at him. If he hears his movements through transmission and the door is closed, there is no impediment to the validity of the following, as we previously mentioned in the conditions of the validity of following. And if they gather around it, and the imam is outside, (it is valid) except for one who is closer to it than his imam while he is in the direction of his imam, because he is ahead of his imam. As for one who is closer to it than his imam but is not in his direction, his following is valid, because precedence and lateness only appear when the side they are both facing is unified.
Source pages p. 436

Commentary
This passage continues the ruling on following an imam in relation to the Kaaba. It addresses the case where the imam is inside the Kaaba and the followers are outside. The ruling: such following is valid provided the door is open, so the followers can see the imam's movements. If the door is closed but the followers hear the imam's cues (tabligh), it is still valid, as the condition of seeing is not absolute. Then it discusses a scenario where the people form a circle around the Kaaba (presumably all facing it) and the imam is outside the Kaaba. In that case, the following is valid for all except one who is closer to the Kaaba than the imam in the direction the imam is facing, because that would put him ahead of the imam in direction. The reasoning is that precedence (taqaddum) only matters when the direction (jiha) is the same; if their directions differ, closeness does not affect validity. The text draws from earlier discussions on the conditions of iqtida'.

Key Terms
اقتداء (iqtida'): Following the imam in congregational prayer; the conditions discussed here relate to spatial orientation relative to the Kaaba.
جِهَة (jihah): The direction one is facing in prayer; here it determines whether a follower is ahead of the imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi madhhab, if a group of people forms a circle around the Kaaba and the imam is outside the Kaaba, whose following is invalid?
A) Anyone who is closer to the Kaaba than the imam.
B) Anyone who is closer to the Kaaba than the imam and facing the same direction as the imam.
C) Anyone who is not facing the Kaaba.
D) All of their following is invalid.

Key Takeaway
Following an imam inside the Kaaba is valid with visibility; when around the Kaaba, only those closer in the same direction are invalid.

'Azima and Rukhsa: The Classification of Qasr
Defines 'azima and rukhsa and classifies qasr as isqat rukhsa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the difference between 'azima and rukhsa, distinguish between tarkhiṣ and isqāṭ rukhṣa, and classify qaṣr as an isqāṭ rukhṣa with justification.

Core Idea
Qasr is not optional; it is a complete dropping of the full prayer, making completion sinful.

This passage opens the chapter on the traveler's prayer by introducing two foundational categories of shar'i rulings: 'azima (original ruling) and rukhsa (concession). It then delves into the subtypes of rukhsa and applies a criterion to determine when a rukhsa grants choice and when it drops the original ruling entirely. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying the rulings of travel.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
Notice that the text divides all shar'i rulings into 'azima and rukhsa. 'Azima is the original ruling, rukhsa is a concession due to an excuse.
This terminology is foundational in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Distinguish the types of rukhsa
The text mentions two types: rukhsa tarkhiṣ (relief, with choice) and rukhsa isqāṭ (dropping, no choice).
Examples: breaking fast (tarkhiṣ) vs. being forced to drink wine (isqāṭ).
3
Understand the criterion for choice
For a rukhsa to be a true permission (with choice), the 'azima must contain either superior reward or some other ease not found in the rukhsa.
If the 'azima offers no extra reward or ease, the rukhsa becomes an isqāṭ.
4
Apply to qaṣr
The text argues that completing the prayer in travel offers no superior reward (reward is based on fulfilling obligation, not number of rak'at) and no other ease. Therefore, qaṣr is an isqāṭ rukhsa.
Performing the full prayer would be sinful because the 'azima has dropped.
5
Conclude the ruling
Thus, the traveler must shorten the four-rak'ah prayers; doing otherwise is a sin.
This is the established Hanafi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صلاة المسافر من باب إضافة الشيء إلى شرطه، ويقال: إلى محله، أو الفعل إلى فاعله. وأصل المفاعلة أن تكون بين اثنين، وقد تستعمل في واحد أيضاً. والمسافر من هذا القبيل، ولأن المسافرة من السفر وهو الكشف وقد حصل بين اثنين هنا، فإن المسافر ينكشف للطريق وهي تنكشف له؛ كذا في مجمع الروايات». واعلم أن المشروعات على نوعين عزيمة ورخصة، فالعزيمة: على ما تقرر على الأمر الأول، والرخصة: ما تغير من عسر إلى يسر بواسطة عذر، ثم الرخصة على ضربين: رخصة ترفيه، مثل الفطر وإجراء كلمة الكفر، ورخصة إسقاط أي سقط الحكم أصلا، مثل الكره على شرب الخمر نعوذ بالله - ومن هذا القبيل قصر الصلاة. أو نقول الرخصة على ضربين حقيقية وهو على نوعين: إما أن يكون السبب موجوداً والحكم كذلك، مثل الإكراه على إجراء كلمة الكفر ونحوه، أو السبب موجوداً والحكم غير موجود، مثل الفطر في رمضان. ومجاز وهو: إما أن يكون السبب معدوماً والحكم كذلك، مثل وضع الإصر والأغلال عنا، أو يكون السبب في الجملة موجوداً وليس في موضع العذر بموجود، كالسلم وقصر الصلاة. كذا في « المستصفى». وفي « مجمع الروايات » : قال في «التحقيق» وفي «الشريعة» : العزيمة : اسم لما هو أصل من الأحكام، والمراد به ما ثبت ابتداءً بإثبات الشرع. والرخصة: اسم لما بني عليه أعذار العباد، كالإذن بإجراء كلمة الكفر على اللسان عند الإكراه، وإباحة الفطر في رمضان بعذر السفر والمرض. وإنما جعلناها أي: هذه الرخصة أي قصر الصلاة في السفر إسقاطاً للعزيمة استدلالاً بمعنى الرخصة. أن الرخصة الحقيقية إذا ثبتت في شيء ثبت للعبد الخيار بين الإقدام على الرخصة، وبين الإتيان بالعزيمة، لأن الرخصة وإن تضمنت يسراً، فالعزيمة إما أن تضمنت فضل ثواب، كتضمن العزيمة في الإكراه على الكفر ثواب الشهادة، أو تضمنت يسراً آخر ليس ذلك في الرخصة، كتضمن الصوم في السفر موافقة المسلمين. فإذا لم يكن فيها فضل ثواب ولا نوع يسر سقطت أي: العزيمة لحصول المقصود بالرخصة وتعين اليسر فيها. وفيما نحن فيه تعين اليسر في قصر الصلاة، وهو ظاهر، ولا يتضمن الإكمال فضل ثواب؛ لأن تمام الثواب في فعل العبد جميع ما عليه، لا في أعداد الركعات، والمسافر قد أتى بجميع ما عليه كالمقيم، فكان كالجمعة أو الفجر . مع الظهر، فإنه الأفضل لظهر المقيم على فجره، ولا جمعة الحُرِّ على ظهر العبد. وإذا كان ذلك وجب القـول بسقوط الإكمال أصلاً انتهى. أي: فيأثم العامل بالعزيمة؛ لأنه حكم رخصة الإسقاط، وهو
Chapter on the Traveler's Prayer. It is a chapter of adding something to its condition, or it is said: to its place, or the action to its doer. The basis of mutual interaction is between two, but it is also used for one. And the traveler is of this type, because traveling (safar) is uncovering, which occurs between two here: the traveler uncovers the road and the road uncovers him. Thus in Majma' al-Riwayat. Know that legislated matters are of two types: 'azima and rukhsa. 'Azima is what is established on the original command. Rukhsa is what changes from difficulty to ease due to an excuse. Then rukhsa is of two types: rukhsa for relief, such as breaking fast and uttering words of disbelief, and rukhsa of dropping, i.e., the ruling drops entirely, such as being forced to drink wine (may Allah protect us) - and from this category is the shortening of prayer. Or we say: rukhsa is of two types: real rukhsa, which is of two kinds: either the cause exists and the ruling also exists, like coercion to utter words of disbelief and the like, or the cause exists and the ruling does not exist, like breaking fast in Ramadan. And metaphorical rukhsa: either the cause is absent and the ruling is also absent, like the removal of burdens and chains from us, or the cause exists in general but is not in a place of excuse, such as peace and shortening of prayer. Thus in al-Mustasfa. And in Majma' al-Riwayat: it is said in al-Tahqiq and al-Shari'a: 'Azima is a name for what is original among rulings, meaning what is established initially by the proof of the Shari'a. Rukhsa is a name for what is built upon the excuses of servants, such as permission to utter words of disbelief on the tongue under coercion, and permission to break fast in Ramadan due to travel or illness. And we have made this rukhsa (i.e., shortening of prayer in travel) a dropping of the 'azima by deducing from the meaning of rukhsa. For when a real rukhsa is established for something, the servant has the choice between performing the rukhsa and performing the 'azima, because although the rukhsa contains ease, the 'azima either contains superior reward, as the 'azima in coercion to disbelief includes the reward of martyrdom, or contains another ease not found in the rukhsa, like fasting in travel includes conformity with Muslims. So when there is no superior reward nor any type of ease, the 'azima drops because the purpose is achieved by the rukhsa and ease is determined. In our case, ease is determined in shortening prayer, which is apparent, and completing does not contain superior reward because the complete reward is in the servant doing all that is upon him, not in the number of rak'ahs, and the traveler has done all that is upon him like the resident. So it is like Jumu'a or Fajr with Zuhr: the Zuhr of the resident is better than his Fajr, and there is no Jumu'a for the free man over the slave's Zuhr. When this is the case, it becomes necessary to say that completion drops entirely. End. Meaning: the one acting according to the 'azima sins, because it is the ruling of a rukhsa of dropping, and it is
Source pages p. 437

Commentary
This passage is a definition-ruling that opens the chapter on the traveler's prayer. It first explains the etymology of 'musafir' as one who 'unveils' the road. Then it introduces a key fiqh distinction: 'azima (original ruling) and rukhsa (concession). Rukhsa is divided into two types: tarkhis (permission, with choice) and isqat (dropping, no choice). The author argues that qasr (shortening prayer in travel) is an isqat rukhsa, meaning the full prayer is not merely optional but dropped entirely. The reasoning is that a real rukhsa gives a choice only if the 'azima offers superior reward or some other ease. In the case of qasr, completing the prayer offers no extra reward (since reward is based on fulfilling what is obligated, not number of rak'ats), and no other ease. Therefore, the 'azima drops completely, and performing the full prayer would be sinful. The passage uses analogies: like how Jumu'a is better than Zuhr for a resident, but a traveler has no Jumu'a obligation, similarly qasr is the only valid option.

Key Terms
عزيمة ('azima): The original ruling established by the Shari'a without concession.
رخصة (rukhsa): A concession that changes a difficult ruling to ease due to an excuse.
قصر (qasr): Shortening the four-rak'ah prayers to two rak'ahs during travel.
إسقاط (isqat): Dropping or removal of the original ruling entirely.
ترخيص (tarkhiṣ): A concession that permits an action that was originally prohibited or relaxes a requirement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is qasr considered an 'isqat' rukhsa rather than a 'tarkhis' rukhsa?
A) Because the traveler has the choice to pray full or short
B) Because completing the prayer offers no superior reward or extra ease
C) Because the cause for rukhsa exists and the ruling also exists
D) Because the traveler is not required to pray at all

Key Takeaway
Qaṣr is an isqāṭ rukhṣa: the full prayer drops entirely, and the traveler who completes it sins.

Minimum Travel Distance and Ruling on Shortening Prayers
Defines minimum travel distance and specifies which prayers are shortened.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of the minimum travel distance and explain why only the four-rak'at fard prayers are shortened during travel.

Core Idea
Travel that changes rulings is three days moderate pace; only four-rak'at fard prayers are shortened to two.

This lesson examines the Hanafi definition of travel (safar) that triggers concessions like shortening prayers. The minimum distance is three days of moderate pace, derived from the hadith of wiping over khuffs. We will also explore which prayers are shortened and the debates about supererogatory prayers during travel.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of travel
Read the passage to find the explicit definition: three days' moderate pace from the shortest days of the year, including rest stops.
This is the foundational ruling.
2
Analyze the dalil from the wiping hadith
Examine the hadith: 'The resident wipes one day and night, the traveler three days and nights.' Focus on the word 'al-musafir' and the claim that it indicates generality (istighraq).
The lam is for generalization, so every traveler is entitled to three days.
3
Apply the generalization argument
Understand that if the minimum travel were less than three days, some travelers could not complete the three-day concession, so the minimum must be three days.
This is a qiyas argument supported by ijma that no one says more than three days.
4
Determine which prayers are shortened
Identify that only the four-rak'at fard prayers (Zuhr, Asr, Isha) are shortened to two. Maghrib, Fajr, and Jumu'ah are not shortened, based on practice and hadith.
The proof includes reports from Aisha and Umar that prayer was originally two rak'ahs.
5
Discuss the sunan prayers debate
Review the intra-Hanafi differences: whether to perform sunan during travel depends on safety and stability (al-Tajnis). The mufta bihi is to perform them when safe.
Witr is never left and never shortened.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

وحضراً فاتبعناه؛ ولما روى أبو داود في سننه، بإسناده إلى عائشة الله أنها قالت: «فُرِضَتِ الصَّلاةُ رَكْعَتِينَ رَكْعَتِينَ فِي الحَضَرِ والسَّفَر، فأقرَّتْ صَلاةُ السَّفَر، وزِيدَتْ صَلاةُ الحَضَرَ » ). كذا في « الديــري»؛ ولما روي عنـها : « أنَّ الصَّلاةَ فُرِضَتْ فِي الأَصْلِ رَكْعَتِينِ، فَلَمَّا قَدِمَ النَّبي صلى الله عليه وسلم المَدِينَةَ ضَمَّ إِلى كُلِّ صَلَاةٍ مِثْلَهَا، غَيْرَ الْمَغْرِبِ فإِنَّهَا وِتْرُ النَّهَارِ » ). وفي ( مجمع الروايات : قال في شرح الغزنوي»: قالت عائشة: « فُرِضَتِ الصَّلَاةُ رَكْعَتِينِ رَكْعَتِينِ، فَزِيْدَتْ فِي الحَضَرِ، وَأَقِرَّتْ فِي السَّفَرِ، إِلَّا المَغْرِبِ فَإِنَّهَا وِتْرُ النَّهَارِ، وَالجُمُعَةُ لِمَكَانِهَا مِنَ الخُطْبَةِ وَالصُّبْحُ لِطُولِ قِرَاءَتِهَا ). وعن عمر له أنه قال: « صَلاةُ الجُمُعَةِ رَكْعَتَانِ، وَصَلاةُ الفَجْرِ رَكْعَتَانِ، وَصَلاةُ السَّفَرِ رَكْعَتَانِ، تَامٌ غَيْرَ قَصْرٍ عَلَى لِسَانِ نَبِيِّكُمْ ).
The minimum travel that changes rulings: a journey of three days from the shortest days of the year, with moderate pace, including rest stops. The moderate pace is the pace of camels and walking on foot, on land, and in the mountains whatever is suitable. The duration for wiping [over khuffs] is measured by travel as stated in al-Durar wa al-Gharar. Travel linguistically means covering distance, as in al-ʿInayah and others. In Majmaʿ al-Riwayat: travel linguistically means prolonged departure. In sacred law it has a limit clarified by his statement: (The minimum) duration (of travel that changes) rulings, which are the obligation to shorten prayer, permission to break fast, extension of wiping [over khuffs] to three days, dropping of obligation of Jumuʿah, the two Eids, sacrifice, prohibition of a free woman traveling without a mahram, and others, (a journey of three days) meaning intending a place only reached by walking three days, (from the shortest days of the year) as stated in al-Jawharah and al-Burhan, and we indicated its estimation by days to show it is not estimated by farsakhs, which is the correct view, due to his statement: 'The resident wipes one day and night, and the traveler three days and nights' – adherence to it necessitates that whoever is truly a traveler is legislated to wipe three days, since the lam in 'al-musafir' (the traveler) is for generalization, as on the resident side, and this is only conceivable if the minimum travel duration is three days, because if it were less he could not complete his duration due to his travel ending, thus necessitating its estimation as such, otherwise some travelers would be excluded from this concession, and increasing it is unanimously rejected, so the need to establish three as the minimum travel duration; and because the concession was certainly non-existent, so it is only established with certainty of what is legally a travel, which is what we specified, since no one said more than that, as in al-Tabyeen, al-Burhan, and al-Fath. That travel is considered with moderate pace during the day, for night is not for travel but rest, and travel during the day (with rest stops), because the traveler must stop to eat, drink, and pray, and most of the day has the ruling of the whole. If the traveler starts early on the first day, travels until noon reaching the stage, stops for rest and stays overnight, then starts early on the second day and travels past noon and stops, then starts early on the third and walks until noon reaching the destination, Shams al-Aimma al-Sarakhsi said: the correct is that he becomes a traveler at the intention, as in al-Jawharah and al-Burhan. (And) moderate travel: pace of camels and walking on foot, considered (on land), and considered in mountains according to suitable pace, because it involves ascent, descent, narrowness and roughness, so walking of camels and feet there is less than on plains. So if by such travel he covers a not distant distance and stops after noon, it is counted on the pattern we mentioned: if he started early and reached at noon and stopped, it was a day. We only considered moderate travel because its fastest is the mail relay, its slowest is the oxcart, and camel and foot travel is moderate, and the best of matters is their middle. (And at sea) moderate wind is considered, according to the fatwa position. If he travels most of the day by it, it is like the whole day even if the distance is less than on land. Once you know the duration of travel and the pace, (then he shortens the obligatory prayer, and there is no shortening of the supererogatory prayers. Then it was said: it is better to leave them seeking concession, and it was said: performing them as devotion. Al-Hinduwani said: performing when stopping, leaving while traveling. It was said: he prays the sunnah of Fajr especially, and said: also the sunnah of Maghrib. In al-Tajnis: the chosen position is that if in safety and stability he performs them, i.e., the supererogatory, because they are legislated as completions, and the traveler needs them, and if in fear he does not perform them because it is left due to an excuse. End. From this you know that Witr is not left, just as it is not shortened. He restricted the obligatory to the four-rakʿah because there is no shortening of the two-rakʿah and three-rakʿah obligatory, due to his statement: 'Pray as you have seen me praying.' He prayed as we mentioned, travel and residence, so we follow. And because Abu Dawud narrated in his Sunan with his chain to ʿAishah that she said: 'Prayer was prescribed two rakʿahs two rakʿahs in residence and travel; the travel prayer was confirmed and the residence prayer was increased.' As quoted in al-Dabri. And because it is narrated from her: 'Prayer was originally prescribed two rakʿahs; when the Prophet arrived in Medina, he added to each prayer another like it except Maghrib, for it is the odd of the day.' In Majmaʿ al-Riwayat, it says in Sharh al-Ghaznawi: ʿAishah said: 'Prayer was prescribed two rakʿahs, then increased in residence, and confirmed in travel, except Maghrib for it is the odd of the day, and Jumuʿah due to its position of the sermon, and Fajr due to its long recitation.' And from ʿUmar that he said: 'Jumuʿah prayer is two rakʿahs, Fajr prayer is two rakʿahs, travel prayer is two rakʿahs, complete not shortened, according to the tongue of your Prophet.'
Source pages p. 438

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah Sharh Nur al-Idah is a ruling with proof on the definition of travel that changes Islamic rulings and which prayers are shortened. The text begins by establishing that the minimum travel distance is three days' journey, calculated from the shortest days of the year, with moderate pace including rest stops. The moderate pace is defined as the pace of camels and walking on foot on land, with appropriate adjustments for mountainous terrain and sea (where moderate wind is considered). The author supports this definition by citing the hadith of wiping over khuffs: the resident wipes one day and night, the traveler three days and nights. He argues that since every traveler is entitled to the three-day concession, the minimum travel must be three days; otherwise some travelers would not be able to complete the concession. He also notes that the duration is measured by days, not farsakhs, which is the correct position. The text then explains that once travel is established, shortening of the obligatory four-rak'at prayers becomes permissible, while supererogatory prayers are not shortened. There is a discussion among Hanafi scholars about whether to pray sunan during travel: some say it is better to leave them (as a concession), others say perform them (as devotion). Al-Hinduwani distinguishes between stopping (pray them) and traveling (leave). The preferred view in al-Tajnis is that if safe and settled, one prays the sunan; if in fear, one does not. Witr is not to be left and is not shortened. The limitation to four-rak'at prayers is supported by the hadith 'Pray as you have seen me praying' and by the reports from ʿAishah and ʿUmar that prayer was originally prescribed as two rak'ahs, then increased in residence but confirmed in travel, except Maghrib (three) and Fajr (two) and Jumu'ah (two). Thus, only the four-rak'at fard prayers (Zuhr, Asr, Isha) are shortened to two rak'ahs in travel.

Key Terms
سفر (safar): Travel; legally defined as a journey of three days' moderate pace from the shortest days of the year, which changes certain rulings.
قصر الصلاة (qasr al-salah): Shortening the four-rak'at obligatory prayers to two rak'ahs while traveling.
سير وسط (sayr wasaṭ): Moderate pace, defined as the pace of camels and walking on foot, not too fast (mail relay) nor too slow (oxcart).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as explained in the passage, which of the following prayers is shortened during travel?
A) Fajr prayer
B) Maghrib prayer
C) Zuhr prayer
D) Jumu'ah prayer

Key Takeaway
The minimum travel that changes rulings is three days moderate pace; only the four-rak'at fard prayers are shortened, confirming the practice of the Prophet.

Ruling on Shortening Prayer at Sea and the Criterion of Moderate Wind
Defining moderate wind as criterion for counting travel days at sea

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi criterion of moderate wind (iʻtidāl al-rīḥ) to determine whether a day of sea travel counts for shortening prayer, and explain the qiyās (analogy) with land travel pace.

Core Idea
At sea, moderate wind replaces normal walking pace to count travel days for shortening prayer.

When traveling by sea, the Hanafi school establishes a clear criterion to determine whether a day counts for shortening prayer. Just as on land the normal walking pace (sīr wasaṭ) is used, at sea the standard is moderate wind (iʻtidāl al-rīḥ). This lesson unpacks the rule and its underlying analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal category
The act is shortening the four-rak‘ah obligatory prayer (qaṣr). This is a dispensation (rukhṣa) for travelers. Determine what constitutes a 'travel day' for this purpose.
2
Understand the land criterion
On land, travel days are counted based on the normal walking pace (sīr wasaṭ), which is neither too fast nor too slow. This is the baseline.
The author explains that extremes (barīd and carriage) are not used.
3
Apply the analogy to sea travel
At sea, the equivalent of normal walking pace is moderate wind (iʻtidāl al-rīḥ). This is the relied-upon position (muftā bihī). The analogy (qiyās) is that both allow steady progress.
The text states: 'In the sea, moderate wind is considered according to the fatwa.'
4
Apply the rule
If a traveler sails with moderate wind for most of the day, that day is counted as a full travel day, even if the distance covered is less than on land.
The key phrase: 'if he travels most of the day with it, it is as if the whole day.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي البحر اعتدال الرّيح. فيقصُرُ الفرض الرباعي . الإبل والأقدام فيه دون سيرهما في السهل، فإذا قطع بذلك السير مسافة ليست ببعيدة، ونـزل بـعـد الزوال، احتسب به على نحو ما قدمناه لو بكر وسار إلى الزوال فنزل كان يوماً، وإنما اعتبرنا السير الوسط؛ لأن أعجله سير البريد، وأبطأه سير العجلة، وسير الإبل والأقدام وسط، وخـيـر الأمـور أوساطها، (وَفي البَحْرِ) يعتبر (اعتدال الريح) على المفتى به، فإذا سار أكثر اليـوم بـه كـان كـكـلـه وإن كانت المسافة دون ما في السهل
And in the sea, moderate wind. So the four-rak'ah obligatory prayer is shortened. Camels and walking are in it less than their pace on land. So if one covers with that pace a distance not far, and alights after midday, it is counted like what we previously mentioned: if he set out early and traveled until midday and alighted, it counts as one day. We only consider the middle pace because its fastest is the pace of the post (barīd) and its slowest is the pace of the carriage (al-ʻajalah), and the pace of camels and walking is middle, and the best of affairs is the middle. And in the sea, moderate wind is considered according to the fatwa. So if he travels most of the day with it, it is as if the whole day, even if the distance is less than on land.
Source pages p. 439

Commentary
This passage specifies the condition for counting travel days at sea. Just as on land the normal walking pace (sīr wasaṭ) is used to calculate travel time, at sea the standard is moderate wind (iʻtidāl al-rīḥ). If a traveler sails with moderate wind for most of the day, that day counts as a travel day, even if the actual distance covered is less than what would be covered on land in a day. This is the relied-upon position (muftā bihī). The author explains that the moderate pace is chosen because extremes hinder accurate measurement. The mention of camels and walking refers to land travel, establishing the analogy.

Key Terms
سير الوسط (sīr wasaṭ): The average pace of a traveler on land, neither fast nor slow, used as a standard for calculating travel days.
اعتدال الريح (iʻtidāl al-rīḥ): Moderate wind that allows steady sailing, considered equivalent to the normal walking pace on land for sea travel.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the standard for counting a travel day at sea according to this passage?
A) Sailing at top speed
B) Sailing with moderate wind for most of the day
C) Covering the same distance as on land
D) Anchoring at midday

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a travel day at sea is counted when one sails with moderate wind for most of the day, analogous to the normal walking pace on land.

Performing Sunnah Prayers During Travel – Hanafi Opinions
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sunnah prayers in travel

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi intra-madhhab dispute on performing sunnah prayers during travel and identify the mufta bihi position based on safety and settlement.

Core Idea
When safe, pray the sunnahs; when fearful, leave them – the traveller's sunnah depends on his state.

You know that only obligatory prayers are shortened in travel. But what about the sunnah prayers? Hanafi scholars debated whether to perform or leave them. This passage from Imdād al-Fattāh presents several views and settles on a practical criterion: safety and settlement. Let's unpack these opinions.

Guided Path
1
State the issue
The question: should a traveller perform the sunnah prayers (rawātib) or leave them? The passage first clarifies that sunnah prayers are not shortened like obligatory ones.
Shortening applies only to fard prayers.
2
List the opinions
Multiple views are recorded: leaving as a concession (tarkhas), performing as an act of nearness (taqarrub), performing while halted but not while traveling (al-Hindūwānī), performing only the sunnah of Fajr, or also Maghrib.
Each view has a rationale: tarkhas emphasizes ease, taqarrub emphasizes reward.
3
Identify the relied-upon view
Al-Tajnīs says the chosen (mukhtār) is: if in safety and settlement (amanah wa qarar), perform the sunnahs; if in fear, leave them with an excuse.
This balances the traveller's need for both spiritual benefit and practical ease.
4
Note the exception: Witr
Witr is wajib in the Hanafi school, so it is never left or shortened. The passage explicitly states: 'and from this you know that Witr is not left, just as it is not shortened.'
Witr has a higher status than sunnah rawātib.
5
Understand the rationale
Sunnahs are complements (mukammilāt); the traveller is in need of them when settled because they complete the obligatory prayer. When fearful, the excuse overrides the recommendation.
This mirrors the principle of removing hardship (raf' al-haraj).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا علمت مدة السفر والسير (فيقصُرُ الفرض العلمي فلا قصر في السنن، ثم قيل: الأفضل تركها ترخصاً، وقيل: الفعل تقرُّباً، وقال « الهندواني » : الفعل حـال النزول، والترك حال السير، وقيل: يصلي سنة الفجر خاصة ، وقيل : سنة المغرب أيضاً. وفي التجنيس : المختار أنه إن كان حال أمنَةٍ وقرارٍ يأتي بها، أي: السنن؛ لأنـهـا شـرعـت مكملات، والمسافر إليه محتاج، وإن كان حال خوف لا يأتي بها لأنه ترك بعذر. انتهى. وبذا علمت أن الوتر لا يترك، كما لا يقصر
And when you know the duration of travel and travel pace, then the obligatory prayer is shortened; there is no shortening in the sunnah prayers. Then it was said: it is better to leave them as a concession; and it was said: performing them is drawing closer. Al-Hindūwānī said: performing them while halting, and leaving them while traveling. And it was said: he prays the sunnah of Fajr specifically, and it was said: also the sunnah of Maghrib. And in al-Tajnīs: the chosen view is that if he is in a state of safety and settlement, he performs them, meaning the sunnahs, because they were legislated as complements and the traveler is in need of them; and if in a state of fear, he does not perform them because he leaves them with an excuse. End. And from this you know that Witr is not left, just as it is not shortened.
Source pages p. 439

Commentary
This passage addresses the debated issue of whether a traveler should perform the sunnah prayers. After establishing that only obligatory prayers are shortened, it presents several opinions: some say it is better to leave them as a concession, others say performing them is an act of worship. Al-Hindūwānī distinguishes between halting (perform) and traveling (leave). Others restrict it to the sunnah of Fajr, or also Maghrib. The relied-upon view cited from al-Tajnīs is that if one is safe and settled, he should pray the sunnahs because they are complementary and beneficial; if in fear, he may leave them due to the excuse. The passage also notes that Witr prayer is not left, just as it is not shortened.

Key Terms
السنن (al-sunan): The non-obligatory prayers (rawātib) associated with the five daily prayers.
الوتر (al-witr): The odd-numbered prayer that is wājib according to Hanafis; it is not shortened or left during travel.
ترخص (tarkhas): Taking a concession; here, leaving the sunnah as a concession of travel.
تقرب (taqarrub): Drawing closer to Allah through worship; performing the sunnah as an act of devotion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view (al-mukhtār) in this passage, when should a traveler pray sunnah prayers?
A) Always, without exception.
B) Never, because travel is a concession.
C) When in a state of safety and settlement.
D) Only when traveling by land, not by sea.

Key Takeaway
The traveller's sunnah practice depends on safety and settlement; when safe, he should perform them, when in fear, he may leave them, and Witr is always observed.

Salah — Prayer

Proof That Only Four-Rakʿah Prayers Are Shortened
Hadith evidence for qaṣr eligibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the obligatory prayers eligible for qaṣr in travel and cite the primary hadith evidence for the Hanafi position.

Core Idea
Only four-rakʿah fard prayers are shortened in travel – two- and three-rakʿah prayers remain unchanged.

This lesson explores the textual proof that only the four-rakʿah obligatory prayers (Ẓuhr, ʿAṣr, ʿIshāʾ) are shortened during travel. The Hanafi school relies on authentic hadith from ʿĀʾishah and ʿUmar which show that prayer was originally prescribed as two rakʿahs, and the increase in residence was limited to specific prayers. Understanding this evidence is crucial for correct practice and for appreciating the school's methodological consistency.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
First, determine which prayers are subject to qaṣr according to the Hanafi school: only four-rakʿah fard prayers (Ẓuhr, ʿAṣr, ʿIshāʾ). Note that three-rakʿah (Maghrib) and two-rakʿah (Fajr, Friday) are not shortened.
The ruling is that qaṣr is wājib for these prayers during travel.
2
Locate the primary dalīl
Find the main proof: the hadith of ʿĀʾishah narrated by Abū Dāwūd: 'Prayer was prescribed as two rakʿahs in residence and travel; the prayer of travel was confirmed, and the prayer of residence was increased.' This is the core textual evidence.
Also note the chain and authenticity (zannī al-thubūt).
3
Understand the wajh al-dalālah
Explain how the hadith proves the ruling. The phrase 'the prayer of travel was confirmed' means travel prayer remained two rakʿahs. Only prayers that were increased in residence (the four-rakʿah ones) can be reduced back to two. Two-rakʿah prayers (Fajr, Friday) and three-rakʿah (Maghrib) were never increased, so they are not shortened.
Maghrib is excluded because it is the 'witr of the day', and Fajr due to long recitation, Friday due to the sermon.
4
Analyse the exceptions
Review the explicit exceptions from the hadith: Maghrib (three rakʿahs), Fajr (two rakʿahs with long recitation), and Friday (two rakʿahs due to sermon). These are not shortened even if one is travelling.
These exceptions are based on the same hadith corpus and are accepted by all major schools.
5
Compare with other schools
Recognise that the Shāfiʿī school shortens all four-rakʿah prayers (including Ẓuhr, ʿAṣr, ʿIshāʾ) but does not shorten Fajr, Maghrib, or Friday. The difference is that Shāfiʿīs consider qaṣr as a concession, while Hanafis consider it a duty (wājib). The evidence is the same but interpreted differently.
The Hanafi position is consistent with the Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah and the practice of the early community.

And he restricted the obligatory prayer by his saying: 'the four-rakʿah' because there is no shortening in the two- and three-rakʿah obligatory prayers, due to his saying: 'Pray as you have seen me praying.' And he prayed as we mentioned, traveling and resident, so we followed him. And because Abu Dawud narrated in his Sunan with his chain to ʻĀʼishah (may Allah be pleased with her) that she said: 'Prayer was prescribed as two rakʿahs, two rakʿahs, in residence and travel; the prayer of travel was confirmed, and the prayer of residence was increased.' That is in al-Dayrī. And because it was narrated from her: 'Prayer was originally prescribed as two rakʿahs; when the Prophet (peace be upon him) arrived in Madinah, he added the like of it to each prayer except Maghrib, for it is the odd of the day.' And in Majmaʻ al-Riwāyāt, it is said in Sharḥ al-Ghaznawī: ʻĀʼishah said: 'Prayer was prescribed as two rakʿahs, two rakʿahs; then it was increased in residence, and confirmed in travel, except Maghrib for it is the odd of the day, and Friday because of its place from the sermon, and Subh because of the length of its recitation.' And from ʻUmar (may Allah be pleased with him) that he said: 'Friday prayer is two rakʿahs, Fajr prayer is two rakʿahs, and travel prayer is two rakʿahs, complete not shortened, upon the tongue of your Prophet.' And prayer before the Night Journey was two prayers: a prayer before sunset and a prayer before sunrise, and this is witnessed by the statement of Allah Most High: 'And exalt [Allah] with praise of your Lord before the rising of the sun and before its setting.' Based on this, it is possible that the saying of ʻĀʼishah 'it was increased in residence' means that it was increased when it was completed to five, so the increase was in the number of rakʿahs and in the number of prayers; and her saying 'prayer was prescribed as two rakʿahs' refers to before the Night Journey. This was said by a group of the Salaf, among them Ibn ʻAbbās. And it is possible that the meaning of her saying 'prayer was prescribed' is that on the night of the Night Journey when the five were prescribed, they were prescribed as two rakʿahs, then increased in residence afterward. This is narrated from some narrators of the hadith from ʻĀʼishah, al-Ḥasan and al-Shaʻbī, that the increase in residence prayer was after the Hijrah by about a year. Abu ... mentioned it. End.
Source pages p. 439

Commentary
This passage provides the textual evidence for why only four-rakʿah prayers are shortened during travel. The Prophet's command to pray as he did indicates that two-rakʿah and three-rakʿah prayers remain as they are. The hadith of ʻĀʼishah and ʻUmar confirm that prayer was originally two rakʿahs; in travel it remained two, while in residence it was increased. The exception of Maghrib (three rakʿahs, the 'odd of the day'), Fajr (two rakʿahs with long recitation), and Friday (two rakʿahs due to sermon) explains why they are not shortened. The passage also explores different interpretations of ʻĀʼishah's hadith concerning whether the two-rakʿah prescription was before the Night Journey or at that time. The Hanafi position is clear: shortening applies only to four-rakʿah obligatory prayers.

Key Terms
الفرض الرباعي (al-farḍ al-rubāʿī): The obligatory prayers consisting of four rakʿahs: Ẓuhr, ʿAṣr, and ʿIshāʾ (excluding Friday which is two).
الوتر (al-witr): Here used to indicate Maghrib as the odd-numbered prayer of the day.
القصر (al-qaṣr): Shortening of the four-rakʿah obligatory prayers to two rakʿahs during travel.

C) Because it is a sunnah prayer, not fard
D) Both A and B are correct

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling that only four-rakʿah fard prayers are shortened in travel is firmly rooted in explicit hadith and the practice of the early community.

Conditions for Qasr: Leaving Residence and Fina
Specifying conditions for traveler status in qaṣr rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the spatial conditions required for a traveler to shorten prayer and explain why even sinful travel qualifies for the concession.

Core Idea
A traveler must physically leave the built-up area and its attached courtyard; sinful travel does not forfeit the concession.

This passage from Imdād al-Fattāḥ specifies the precise spatial conditions that must be met for a person to be legally considered a traveler (musāfir) entitled to shortening prayer. It not only affirms that the concession applies to all journeys regardless of sin, but also defines the boundaries of 'residence' to include the attached courtyard (fināʼ) and the surrounding suburbs (rabḍ). Understanding these conditions is crucial to correctly applying the qaṣr ruling in daily life.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the act under discussion is shortening the prayer (qaṣr) for a traveler. The ruling is that qaṣr becomes wājib (obligatory) once the conditions are met, not merely permissible.
The Ḥanafī school considers qaṣr wājib, unlike some other schools.
2
Locate the dalīl (proof)
The passage cites Quran 4:101, 2:184, and a hadith on wiping over socks. All use general expressions about travel without restricting to permissible journeys.
The proofs are from the Quran and Sunnah; their absolute wording is key.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalālah (indication)
The phrase 'when you travel upon the earth' is general (ʿāmm). In Ḥanafī uṣūl, a general command is applied to all its instances unless there is a specific exclusion. Here, no exclusion is made for sinful travel, so the concession applies universally.
The Ḥanafī principle: al-ʿāmm yufīdu al-wujūb wa lā yukhaṣṣṣu illā bi-dalīl.
4
Note the spatial conditions
The traveler must have physically left the houses of his residence (buyūt muqāmihī), including tents, and also the attached courtyard (fināʼ). Additionally, if the residence is in a city, he must pass through the suburbs (rabḍ) as they are considered part of the city.
Merely intending to leave is insufficient; actual departure is required.
5
Evaluate the ikhtilāf (dispute) on sinful travel
Other schools may restrict the concession to permissible travel. The Ḥanafīs argue that the absolute texts do not differentiate, and the sin is a separate issue that does not invalidate the ruling.
The thamarah al-khilāf: a runaway slave may shorten prayer only in the Ḥanafī school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعندنا يقصر (مَنْ) نوى (السفر) أي: قصد تلك المسافة ( ولو كان عاصيـاً بـسـفـره كـآبق من سيده، وناشز، وقاطع طريق؛ لأن نصوص الرخصة مطلقة، قال تعالى: ﴿ وَإِذَا ضَرَبْتُمْ فِي الْأَرْضِ فَلَيْسَ عَلَيْكُمْ جُنَاحٌ أَن نَقصُرُوا مِنَ الصَّلَوَة ﴾ [النساء : ۱۰۱]، وقال في الصوم: ﴿ فَمَن كَانَ مِنكُم مَّرِيضًا أَوْ عَلَى سَفَرٍ ﴾ [البقرة: ١٨٤]، وقال : ( يَمْسَحُ المُسَافِرُ ثَلاثَةَ أَيَّامٍ ولَيَالِيهَا ). فوجب إعمال إطلاقها، والقُبْحُ المُجَاور، لا ينفي الأحكام كالبيع وقت المند، والصلاة في الأرض المخصوبة ولا يكون مسافراً مع قصده تلك المسافة إلا ( إذا جاوز بيوت مُقَامِهِ)، ولو بيوت الأخبية وإن كانت متفرقة، إذا فـارق عما قرب من خيمته، وإن نزلوا على ماء أو محتطب، يعتبر مفارقة الماء والمحتطب، كذا في «مجمع الروايات»، ولعله ما لم يكن محتطباً واسعاً جداً. ثم المعتبر المجاوزة من الجانب الذي خرج منه، ولو حاذاه في أحد جانبيه فقط لا يضر، كما في قاضي خان وغيره. (و) يشترط أن يكـون قـد (جَاوَزَ أيضاً ما اتصل به أي بمقامه (منْ فِنَائِهِ)، كما يشترط مجاوزة ربضه، وهو مـا حـول المدينة من بيوت ومساكن فإنه في حكم المصر، وكذا القرى المتصلة بربض المصر، يشترط مجاوزتها في
And according to us, (whoever) intends (travel), i.e., aims for that distance, shortens (even if he is a sinner in his travel, like a runaway from his master, a nāshiz (disobedient wife), or a highway robber, because the texts of concession are absolute. Allah said: 'And when you travel upon the earth, there is no blame upon you for shortening the prayer' [al-Nisāʼ 4:101], and regarding fasting: 'So whoever among you is ill or on a journey' [al-Baqarah 2:184], and he said: 'The traveler may wipe for three days and nights.' So it is necessary to apply their absoluteness. The accompanying evil does not negate rulings, like selling at the time of the call (to Friday prayer) and prayer on usurped land. And he is not considered a traveler with his intention of that distance unless (he has passed the houses of his residence), even if it is a tent (khibāʼ), even if they are scattered, when he departs from what is close to his tent. And if they alight at water or a place of firewood, leaving the water and the firewood is considered. Thus in Majmaʻ al-Riwāyāt, unless the firewood area is very vast. Then what is considered is passing from the side from which he departed; if he is parallel to it on one side only, it does not harm, as in Qāḍī Khān and others. And it is also necessary that he has passed what is attached to his residence from its courtyard (fināʼ), just as passing its surrounding suburbs (rabḍ) is required, which is what is around the city of houses and dwellings, for it is like the city. Similarly, villages attached to the suburb of the city, it is required to pass them
Source pages p. 440

Commentary
This passage establishes the conditions under which a person is legally considered a traveler (musāfir) for the purpose of shortening prayer. First, it affirms that even sinful journeys (like a runaway slave, a rebellious wife, or a highway robber) still entitle one to the concessions, because the Quranic and hadith texts are unconditional; the sin attached to the journey does not invalidate the rulings. Then it states the key spatial condition: one must have left the houses of his residence (buyūt muqāmihī), including tents and scattered dwellings, as well as the attached courtyard (fināʼ). The suburb (rabḍ) of a city is also considered part of the city, so one must pass beyond it. The passage also clarifies that passing from the direction of departure is sufficient; being parallel on one side does not harm. These conditions ensure that qaṣr is only applied when one has truly left the area of residence.

Key Terms
فناء (fināʼ): The open courtyard or surrounding area attached to a residence; considered part of the residence for travel rulings.
ربض (rabḍ): The suburbs or outskirts of a city, including houses and dwellings adjacent to the city proper.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) A distance of one day's travel

Key Takeaway
Spatial departure from residence and its environs is the essential condition for being a traveler; sinful travel does not affect the concession.
