Ruling on Qasr for the Disobedient Traveler
Establishes that even a disobedient traveler may shorten prayer based on absolute texts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that even a disobedient traveler shortens prayer and explain the proof from the absolute texts of the Quran and Sunnah.

Core Idea
The texts of license are absolute—even a sinful traveler shortens prayer.

This passage presents the Hanafi ruling that all travelers, regardless of the lawfulness of their journey, are entitled to the concession of shortening prayer. The commentator cites unconditional Quranic verses and a hadith to support this, and addresses a potential objection by noting that associated evil does not negate the ruling. Understanding this principle is key to applying travel concessions correctly within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The text states that anyone who intends travel (for the required distance) shortens prayer, even if they are disobedient in that travel, such as a runaway slave, a rebellious wife, or a highway robber. The ruling is unconditional regarding the traveler's piety.
The term 'عاصياً بسفره' covers any travel that is sinful in itself or in its purpose.
2
Examine the proof texts
The Quran verse (4:101) uses the general phrase 'when you travel in the land' without qualification. Similarly, the verse on fasting (2:184) and the hadith on wiping (3 days) are unconditional. The Hanafi school argues that these texts must be applied in their absolute sense unless there is clear evidence for restriction.
The principle: al-mutlaq yajri 'ala itlaqihi (the absolute is left upon its absoluteness).
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to the objection
The commentator preempts a potential objection: how can a sinner benefit from a license? He gives two examples: (1) selling during Friday prayer is sinful but the sale contract is valid; (2) praying on usurped land is sinful but the prayer is valid. Both illustrate that the presence of sin does not negate the underlying ruling.
The reasoning is that the legal cause (sabab) for the concession is travel itself, not the morality of the journey.
4
Place the dispute in context
This is a mukhtalaf fih issue. Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) restrict concessions to legitimate travel. The Hanafi position relies on the absolute wording and the principle that 'associated evil' does not nullify the ruling.
The thamarah al-khilaf: a Hanafi mufti would allow qasr for a sinful traveler, while a Shafi'i mufti would not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعندنا يقصر (مَنْ) نوى (السفر) أي: قصد تلك المسافة ( ولو كان عاصيــاً بـسـفـره كـآبق من سيده، وناشز (۱)، وقاطع طريق؛ لأن نصوص الرخصة مطلقة، قال تعالى: ﴿ وَإِذَا ضَرَبْتُمْ فِي الْأَرْضِ فَلَيْسَ عَلَيْكُمْ جُنَاحٌ أَن نَقصُرُوا مِنَ الصَّلَوَة [النساء : ١٠١]، وقال في الصوم: فَمَن كَانَ مِنكُم مَّرِيضًا أَوْ عَلَى سَفَي [البقرة: ١٨٤]، وقال : ( يَمْسَحُ المُسَافِرُ ثَلاثَةَ أَيَّامٍ ولَيَالِيهَا » (۳). فوجب إعمال إطلاقها، والقُبْحُ المُجَاور، لا ينفي الأحكام كالبيع وقت المند) ، والصلاة في الأرض المخصوبة
And according to us, he who intends travel—i.e., aims for that distance—shortens (prayer), even if he is disobedient in his travel, like a runaway from his master, a nashiz (rebellious wife), and a highway robber; because the texts of the license are absolute. Allah Most High says: 'And when you travel in the land, there is no blame upon you for shortening the prayer' [an-Nisa: 101]. And He says regarding fasting: 'So whoever among you is ill or on a journey' [al-Baqarah: 184]. And the Prophet (PBUH) said: 'The traveler may wipe (over khuffayn) for three days and nights.' Thus it is necessary to apply their absoluteness. And associated evil does not negate rulings, like selling at the time of the Friday call, and praying on usurped land.
Source pages p. 440

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It establishes that the license to shorten prayer (qasr) applies to all travelers, even those who are disobedient in their travel, such as a runaway slave, a rebellious wife (nashiz), or a highway robber. The reasoning is that the primary texts (Quran and Hadith) are absolute and unconditional in their wording. The Quranic verse in Surah an-Nisa does not specify 'righteous' travelers; it is general. Similarly, the verse on fasting and the hadith on wiping over khuffayn do not exclude sinners. The commentator then uses two analogies to show that an associated evil does not negate the underlying ruling: selling at the time of the Friday call is prohibited but the sale contract itself remains valid; praying on usurped land is sin but the prayer is valid. Thus, the sinfulness of the travel does not prevent the application of the travel concessions.

Key Terms
ناشز (nāshiz): A woman who leaves her husband's home without legitimate reason, considered disobedient.
آبق (ābiq): A slave who runs away from his master.
قاطع طريق (qāti' al-ṭarīq): A highway robber or bandit who waylays travelers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Yes, because the texts of the license are absolute and do not exclude sinners.
C) Only if he repents before starting the journey.
D) No, because he is not a legitimate traveler.

Key Takeaway
Even a disobedient traveler shortens prayer because the texts of license are absolute and sin does not negate legal rulings.

Conditions for Becoming a Traveler: Leaving Residence, Fina', and Rabad
Conditions for traveler status for qasr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three spatial conditions for being considered a traveler (houses, fina', rabad) and the three personal conditions (independence, puberty, minimum duration) and define fina' and rabad.

Core Idea
You are not a traveler until you leave your houses, the service area (fina'), and the suburbs (rabad).

In Hanafi fiqh, shortening prayer (qasr) depends on being a valid traveler. This lesson unpacks the precise spatial and personal requirements. The source text from Imdad al-Fattah clarifies what must be left behind and who qualifies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act under discussion is traveling for the purpose of shortening prayer (qasr). The ruling for qasr is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah muakkadah) for a valid traveler.
2
List the spatial conditions
The text requires passing beyond three zones: the houses of residence (including tents), the fina' (service area like horse tracks and burial grounds), and the rabad (suburbs attached to the city). Each must be left behind.
If the fina' is separated by a farm or a bowshot, it need not be passed.
3
Define fina' and rabad
Fina' is the open space prepared for public utilities like exercising horses and burying the dead. Rabad refers to the suburbs with houses and dwellings that are treated as part of the city.
4
List the personal conditions
Three conditions for a valid travel intention: independence (not a dependent follower), puberty (child's travel does not count), and a minimum travel duration of three days.
Examples of followers: woman with husband, slave with master, soldier with commander.
5
Apply to scenarios
Consider a person who leaves his house but stops in the fina' to load luggage. He has not yet left the fina', so he is not a traveler. Similarly, one who leaves the fina' but remains within the rabad is still a resident.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يكون مسافراً مع قصده تلك المسافة إلا إذا جاوز بيوت مُقَامِهِ، ولو بيوت الأخبية وإن كانت متفرقة، إذا فـارق عما قرب من خيمته، وإن نزلوا على ماء أو محتطب، يعتبر مفارقة الماء والمحتطب، كذا في «مجمع الروايات»، ولعله ما لم يكن محتطباً واسعاً جداً. ثم المعتبر المجاوزة من الجانب الذي خرج منه، ولو حاذاه اه في أحد جانبيه فقط لا يضر، كما في قاضي خان وغيره. (و) يشترط أن يكــون قـد (جَاوَزَ أيضاً ما اتصل به أي بمقامه (منْ فِنَائِهِ)، كما يشترط مجاوزة ربضه، وهو مـا حــول المدينة من بيوت ومساكن فإنه في حكم المصر، وكذا القرى المتصلة بربض المصر، يشترط مجاوزتها في الصحيح ) ، ( وإن انفصل الفناء بمزرعة، أوْ قَدْرَ غَلْوَةٍ لا يُشترط مجاوزتُهُ، والفِنَاءُ: المكانُ المُعَدُّ لمصالح البلد، كرَكْضِ الدواب ، ودفن الموتى. ويشترط لصحة تيّةِ السفر ثلاثة أشياء: الاستقلال بالحكم والبلوغ، وعدم نقصان مُدَةِ السَّفَرِ عَنْ ثلاثةِ أَيَّامٍ، فَلا يَقْصُرُ مَنْ لم يجاوز عُمرانَ مُقَامِهِ، أو جاوز، وكان صبياً، أو تابعاً لم يَنْوِ متبوعه السفر، كالمرأة مع زوجها، والعبدِ مع مولاه، والجندي معَ أميرِهِ..
And one is not a traveler with his intention of that distance unless he passes beyond the houses of his residence, even if they are tents, though they be scattered, when he separates from what is near his tent. And if they camp at water or a wood-gathering area, separation from the water and the wood is considered, as in 'Majma' al-Riwayat'. And perhaps unless the wood-gathering area is very vast. Then the consideration is passage from the side from which he exited; even if he is parallel to it on only one side, it does not harm, as in Qadi Khan and others. And it is also a condition that he has passed beyond what is attached to his residence of its fina', just as passing beyond its rabad (suburb) is a condition. The rabad is what is around the city of houses and dwellings, for it is like the city itself. Similarly, villages connected to the rabad of the city: it is required to pass beyond them according to the correct view. And if the fina' is separated by a farm or a bowshot's distance, passing beyond it is not required. The fina': the place prepared for the utilities of the town, such as exercising horses and burying the dead. And for the validity of the intention of travel, three things are required: independence in judgment, puberty, and that the duration of travel is not less than three days. So one does not shorten (prayer) who has not passed beyond the built-up area of his residence, or who has passed but was a child, or a follower whose followed one did not intend travel, like a woman with her husband, a slave with his master, and a soldier with his commander.
Source pages p. 440

Commentary
This passage defines the conditions for being considered a traveler for the purpose of shortening prayer. First, one must physically leave the houses of his residence, including tent dwellings. If living at a water source or wood-gathering area, leaving that area is required. The direction of exit matters: crossing only the side from which one departs, not entire city. Second, one must also leave the fina' (the surrounding service area used for utilities like horse exercise and burial) and the rabad (suburbs attached to the city). However, if the fina' is separated by farmland or a bowshot's distance (approx 400 steps), it does not need to be crossed. Then the passage lists three conditions for a valid intention to travel: independence (the traveler must make his own decision), puberty (child's travel does not count), and a minimum travel duration of three days. Examples of followers are given: a woman following her husband, a slave following his master, a soldier following his commander. Such followers do not count as travelers unless their leader intends travel.

Key Terms
فِنَاء (fināʾ): The open space around a town prepared for public utilities like exercising horses and burying the dead.
رَبَض (rabaḍ): The suburbs attached to a city, including houses and dwellings, treated as part of the city.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what must a person pass beyond to be considered a traveler for qasr?
A) Only the houses of the town.
B) The houses, the fina', and the rabad (suburbs).
C) Only the fina' and rabad, not necessarily the houses.
D) Only the boundary of the town's mosque.

Key Takeaway
Leaving the built-up area alone is insufficient; you must also depart the fina' (service area) and rabad (suburbs) to be considered a traveler for qasr.

Three Conditions for Valid Intention of Travel
Lists three prerequisites for valid travel intention affecting qasr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions for a valid travel intention that permits qasr and apply them to determine who qualifies to shorten prayer.

Core Idea
A valid travel intention requires independence, puberty, and a minimum of three days.

Not every person who leaves their home automatically qualifies to shorten their prayer. The Hanafi school specifies three precise conditions that must be met for the intention of travel to be valid for the purpose of qasr. This lesson unpacks each condition and illustrates them with examples of dependent followers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three conditions
Read the Arabic text carefully and list the three prerequisites mentioned for a valid travel intention.
The text begins with 'ويشترط لصحة نية السفر ثلاثة أشياء'.
2
Understand independence (الاستقلال بالحكم)
This means the traveler must be making their own decision, not merely following another. The text gives examples of followers: wife with husband, slave with master, soldier with commander.
A dependent follower's intention is not valid unless the leader also intends travel.
3
Understand puberty (البلوغ)
The traveler must have reached puberty. A child's travel does not count for the concession of qasr.
Puberty is a general condition for legal obligations in Islam.
4
Understand minimum duration (ثلاثة أيام)
The intended journey must be at least three days (approx. 48 miles or 80 km) in the Hanafi school.
Other schools use different distances, e.g., 16 farsakh (approx. 48 km) in the Shafi'i school.
5
Apply the conditions to examples
For each follower type: if the leader does not intend travel, the follower remains a resident and must pray full prayers.
If the leader intends travel, the follower may shorten, but the condition of independence is still technically lacking; the ruling is permissibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويشترط لصحة نية السفر ثلاثة أشياء: الاستقلال بالحكم والبلوغ، وعدم نقصان مدة السفر عن ثلاثة أيام. فلا يقصر من لم يجاوز عمران مقامه، أو جاوز، وكان صبياً، أو تابعاً لم يَنْوِ متبوعه السفر، كالمرأة مع زوجها، والعبد مع مولاه، والجندي مع أميره.
And for the validity of the intention of travel, three things are required: independence in judgment, puberty, and that the duration of travel is not less than three days. So one does not shorten (prayer) who has not passed beyond the built-up area of his residence, or who has passed but was a child, or a follower whose followed one did not intend travel, like a woman with her husband, a slave with his master, and a soldier with his commander.
Source pages p. 441

Commentary
This passage states the three conditions for a valid intention to travel for the purpose of shortening prayer. First, the traveler must be independent in his decision (mustahill bi al-hukm), meaning he is not a mere follower of someone else's decision. Second, he must have reached puberty (bulugh), because a child's travel is not considered legally significant for this concession. Third, the planned journey must be at least three days in duration (according to the Hanafi school, approximately 48 miles or 80 km). If any of these conditions are missing, one does not qualify to shorten prayer. Examples of those who are dependent followers: a woman traveling with her husband whose intention she follows, a slave with his master, and a soldier with his commander. In such cases, if the leader does not intend travel, the follower does not become a traveler.

Key Terms
الاستقلال بالحكم (al-istiqlāl bi al-ḥukm): The traveler makes his own decision independent of another's authority.
تابع (tābi‘): A person who travels in submission to another's authority, like a wife with her husband or a slave with his master.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The traveler must be independent (not a follower).
B) The traveler must have reached puberty.
C) The travel must be at least three days in duration.
D) The travel must be for a permissible purpose.

Key Takeaway
A valid travel intention for qasr requires the traveler to be independent, adult, and planning a journey of at least three days.

Definition of Fina' and Ruling on Crossing It for Qasr
Defines the outskirts (fina') and its role in determining travel distance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the Hanafi term 'al-fina'' and state when crossing it is not required for shortening prayer.

Core Idea
The fina' is the town's outskirts for utilities; if separated from the built-up area, crossing it is not required for qasr.

This passage clarifies a key term in travel fiqh: 'al-fina'' (the outskirts). The Hanafi school distinguishes between the built-up area (umran) and the fina' used for grazing, burial, etc. The ruling on whether a traveler must cross the fina' depends on whether it is directly attached to the town or separated by a farm or a bowshot distance.

Guided Path
1
Define al-fina'
Identify the term and its definition: the area prepared for the town's needs (grazing, burial, etc.).
The fina' is not part of the built-up town (umran).
2
Identify the condition for exemption
Note the condition: if the fina' is separated from the built-up area by a farm or a bowshot (about 400 steps), then crossing it is not required.
The text uses 'glawah' (bowshot) as a measure.
3
State the ruling
When the fina' is separated, the traveler only needs to cross the built-up area to qualify for qasr.
This is the correct view in the madhhab.
4
Understand the dalil
The Prophet (PBUH) shortened prayer at Dhul-Hulayfah and said, 'If we pass this hut, we will shorten.' This indicates that crossing the built-up boundary, not the fina', is the trigger.
The hadith shows that the built-up area (represented by the hut) is the marker.
5
Apply to a scenario
Consider a traveler leaving a city with an attached fina' versus one where the fina' is separated by a farm. The ruling changes accordingly.
Practice with a concrete example: if the city's houses end at a wall, and beyond that is a grazing field (fina') separated by a bowshot, the traveler only needs to cross the houses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن انفصلَ الفِناء بمزرعة، أوْ قَدْرَ غَلْوَةٍ لا يُشترط مجاوزتُهُ، والفِنَاءُ: المكانُ المُعَدُّ لمصالح البلد، كرَكْضِ الدواب ، ودفن الموتى. (1) الصحيح ) ، ( وإن انفصل الفناء بمزرعة، أوْ قَدْرَ عَلْوَةٍ وتقدم ) أنها أربع مئة خطوة ( لا يُشترط مجاوزته) أي: الفناء، وكذا لو اتصلت القرية بالفناء لا بالربض لا يشترط مجاوزتها، بل مجاوزة الفناء، كذا في «قاضي خان». ( والفناء: المكانُ المُعَدُّ لمصالح البلد، كرَكْضِ الدَّواتِ، ودَفْنِ الموتى) وإلقاء التراب، ولا يعتبر البساتين من عمران المدينة وإن كانت متصلة ببنائها؛ لأنَّ البساتين ليست من البلدة، ولو سكنها أهل البلدة في جميع السنة أو بعضها، ولا يعتبر سكني الحفظة) والأكـــرة (۳) اتفاقاً، وإنما شرط رطنا المجاوزة؛ لأنه عليه الصلاة والسلام «قصر العصر بذي الحليفة». وقال عليه: « لو جاوزنا هذا الخص لقصرنا » )
And if the fina' is separated by a farm or the distance of a bowshot, it is not required to cross it. And the fina': the place prepared for the needs of the town, like running horses and burying the dead. (1) The correct view: And if the fina' is separated by a farm or the distance of a bowshot, and it has been stated that it is four hundred steps, it is not required to cross it, i.e., the fina'. Likewise, if the village is connected to the fina' but not to the ribat (outskirts), it is not required to cross it, rather crossing the fina' is sufficient, as in Qadi Khan. And the fina': the place prepared for the needs of the town, like running horses and burying the dead, and throwing dirt. And orchards are not considered part of the built-up area of the city even if they are connected to its buildings, because orchards are not part of the town, even if the townspeople live in them all or part of the year. And the residence of guards and farmers is not considered, by agreement. And the reason for requiring the crossing of the homeland is because the Prophet (peace be upon him) shortened the Asr prayer at Dhul-Hulayfah, and he said: 'If we pass this hut, we will shorten.'
Source pages p. 441

Commentary
This is a definitional ruling (definition_ruling) that clarifies the term 'fina'' (the outskirts or periphery of a town) and the legal requirement for a traveler to cross it to qualify for shortening prayer (qasr). The passage explains that if the fina' is separated from the built-up area by a farm or a distance of about four hundred steps (a bowshot), it is not necessary to actually cross the fina' itself; rather, crossing the built-up area is sufficient. This is because the fina' is not part of the town proper but is a designated area for the town's needs, such as grazing animals and burial. Orchards and agricultural fields, even if physically connected to the town, are not considered part of the built-up area (umran), and their residence does not count. The ruling is based on the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) who shortened his prayer at Dhul-Hulayfah, a place outside Medina, and his statement about passing a hut, indicating that crossing the boundary of the built-up area triggers the concession of qasr.

Key Terms
الفناء (al-fina'): The area prepared for the needs of the town, such as grazing animals and burying the dead; the outskirts.
الغلوة (al-ghalwah): A bowshot; approximately four hundred steps.
العمران (al-umran): The built-up area of a town or city, not including fields or orchards.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is required to cross the fina' to be considered a traveler.
B) It is not required to cross the fina'; crossing the built-up area suffices.
C) One must cross both the built-up area and the fina'.
D) The fina' is considered part of the town, so no crossing is needed.

Key Takeaway
The fina' is a utility area separate from the built-up town; crossing it is only required if it is directly attached, otherwise crossing the built-up area alone qualifies for qasr.

Three Conditions for Valid Intention of Travel for Qasr
Lists three conditions for valid travel intention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions for a valid intention of travel (qasr) and identify whether a given traveler qualifies based on the criteria of independence, puberty, and journey duration.

Core Idea
Three conditions: independence, puberty, and a three-day journey — missing any invalidates qasr.

The permissibility of shortening prayers (qasr) during travel hinges on a valid intention of travel. The Hanafi school specifies three precise conditions for this intention. This passage from Nur al-Idah enumerates them and clarifies who qualifies and who does not, focusing on the key concepts of independence (istiqlal) and being a follower (tabi'). Understanding these conditions is essential for correctly applying qasr rulings in daily life.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three conditions
Read the text carefully and list the three conditions for a valid intention of travel as stated: independence in judgment (al-istiqlal bi al-hukm), puberty (al-bulugh), and that the travel duration is not less than three days.
These are prerequisites for qasr to be permissible.
2
Understand the independence condition
The text explains that a person must have independent authority (istiqlal) over their travel decision. Those who are dependent — such as a wife, slave, soldier, employee, student, or captive — cannot validly intend travel on their own; they follow the intention of their leader (mattabuc).
Exception: if the leader has not intended travel, the follower is not considered a traveler even if they physically travel.
3
Analyze the puberty condition
A minor (sabi) cannot validly intend travel even if he crosses the built-up area. Puberty is a shart taklif (condition of legal responsibility) for the intention to count.
This aligns with general Hanafi rules of taklif.
4
Apply the three-day minimum duration
The journey must be planned to last at least three days (72 hours). If the intended travel is shorter, qasr is not allowed. The text also notes that the follower's intention is considered only if they know the leader's intention, and this is the most sound view (al-ashah).
The three days are based on the Hanafi fiqh definition of a 'travel' (safar) that permits concessions.
5
Distinguish who qualifies and who does not
Go through the examples: a woman whose husband has paid her prompt dowry is a follower; if the dowry is unpaid, she is not a follower (per Abu Hanifa). Slaves (except mukatab) are followers. A soldier who receives provisions from his commander is a follower. An employee, student, coerced traveler, captive, and a blind person led by a volunteer are also followers. For all followers, qasr is only valid if the leader intended travel and the follower knows it.
Note the specific exception for women with unpaid dowry: they are not obliged to follow and thus their intention is independent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويشترط لصحة نيّة السفر ثلاثة أشياء: الاستقلال بالحكم والبلوغ، وعدم نقصان مُدّة السفر عن ثلاثة أيام، فلا يقصر من لم يجاوز عمران مقامه، أو جاوز وكان صبياً، أو تابعاً لم ينو متبوعه السفر، كالمرأة مع زوجها، والعبد مع مولاه، والجندي مع أميره.. (1) الصحيح ) ، ( ويشترط لصحة نيّة السفر ثلاثة أشياء: الاستقلال بالحُكْمِ، وَ) الثاني: (البلوغ. و) الثالث: (عدمُ نُقصانِ مُدّةِ السفر عن ثلاثةِ أَيَّامٍ. فلا يَقْصُرُ مَنْ لم يجاوز عمرانَ مُقَامِهِ، أَوْ جاوز) العمران ناوياً، (وَ) لكن كان صبيَّاً، أو تابعاً لم يَنْو متبوعه السفر)، والتابع (كالمرأة مع زوجها ) وقد أوفاها مهرها المعجل، وإن لم يوفها لم تكن تبعاً له ولـــو دخــل بـهـا؛ لأنه يجوز لها منعه من الوطء والإخراج؛ للمهر عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله ( والـعـبـد) غـيـر المكاتب، فيشمل المدبر " وأم الولد مع مولاه، والجندي مع أميره) إذا كان يرتزق من الأمير، والأجير مع المستأجر، والتلميذ مع أستاذه، والمكره على السفر، والأسير، والأعمى مع المتبرع بقوده، وإن كان أو ناوياً دونَ الثَّلاثةِ، وتُعتبر نيَّةُ الإقامة والسفرِ من الأصلِ، دون التَّبَعِ إِنْ عَلِمَ نية المتبوع، في الأصح.
And for the validity of the intention of travel, three things are required: independence in judgment, puberty, and that the duration of travel is not less than three days. So he does not shorten who has not crossed the built-up area of his residence, or if he has crossed but was a child, or a follower whose leader did not intend travel, like a woman with her husband, the slave with his master, and the soldier with his commander. (1) The correct view: And for the validity of the intention of travel, three things are required: independence in judgment, and the second: puberty, and the third: that the duration of travel is not less than three days. So he does not shorten who has not crossed the built-up area of his residence, or if he crossed the built-up area intending travel, but was a child, or a follower whose leader did not intend travel. And the follower is like a woman with her husband, and he has paid her prompt dowry; if he has not paid it, she is not a follower of him even if he has consummated the marriage, because she has the right to prevent him from intercourse and travel due to the dowry according to Abu Hanifa. And the slave (other than the mukatab, including mudabbar and umm walad) with his master, and the soldier with his commander if he draws provisions from the commander, and the hired worker with the employer, and the student with his teacher, and the one coerced to travel, and the captive, and the blind person with the one who volunteers to lead him, even if he intends less than three days. And the intention of residence and travel is considered from the leader, not the follower, if the follower knows the leader's intention, in the most sound view.
Source pages p. 441

Commentary
This is a ruling statement (ruling_statement) that enumerates the three conditions for a valid intention of travel that permits shortening prayer (qasr). The conditions are: (1) independence in judgment (al-istiqlal bi al-hukm), meaning the person is not dependent on another's permission for travel; (2) puberty (al-bulugh); and (3) the travel duration must be at least three days. The passage then explains who does not qualify: those who have not crossed the built-up area of their residence, minors, and followers (tabi') whose leader has not intended travel. Followers include a woman traveling with her husband (provided he has paid her prompt dowry; otherwise she is not obliged to follow), slaves with their masters (excluding mukatab but including mudabbar and umm walad), soldiers with their commander, and various others. The intention of the follower is derived from the leader, but only if the follower knows the leader's intention. This is the most sound view (al-ashah).

Key Terms
الاستقلال بالحكم (al-istiqlal bi al-hukm): Having independent authority to make decisions regarding travel, not requiring permission.
التابع (al-tabi'): A follower whose travel is dependent on the leader's intention, such as a wife, slave, or soldier.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a condition for valid intention of travel for qasr according to this passage?
A) Independent judgment (al-istiqlal bi al-hukm).
B) Puberty (al-bulugh).
C) Travel duration of at least three days.
D) Crossing more than one town boundary.

Key Takeaway
A valid intention of travel for qasr requires independence, puberty, and a journey of at least three days; followers must know the leader's intention.

Qasr as ʿAzīmah: Ruling on Completing Four Rakʿahs
Ruling with proof: qasr as ʿazīmah and its implications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that qasr is ʿazīmah and apply the conditions for validity when a traveler completes four rakʿahs.

Core Idea
Qasr is a binding resolution for the traveler, not a negotiable concession—completing four rakʿahs incurs dislike and may invalidate the prayer.

This passage establishes that qasr (shortening prayer) is the original ruling (ʿazīmah) for the traveler, not merely a concession. It then details the consequences if a traveler completes four rakʿahs: the prayer can be valid with dislike if the first sitting is performed, but invalid if the first sitting is omitted—unless the traveler intends residence. Understanding these nuances is essential for correct practice and for appreciating the Hanafi position in contrast to other schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled: qasr (shortening prayer) for a traveler. The text states it is ʿazīmah (resolution), meaning it is the prescribed ruling, not a concession.
This contrasts with other schools that view qasr as a rukhsah.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith of Yaʿlā ibn Umayyah where the Prophet (peace be upon him) calls qasr a 'charity' from Allah, implying it is to be accepted, not rejected.
The hadith is from Sahih Muslim.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The word 'ṣadaqah' (charity) indicates a favor to be welcomed, so qasr is the standard (ʿazīmah), not an exception. Thus, completing four rakʿahs is a departure from the norm.
The imperative 'faqbalū' (so accept) reinforces this.
4
Analyze the effects of completing four rakʿahs
If the traveler sits for tashahhud after two, prayer is valid but disliked (makrūh) due to delaying the obligatory salām. If no sitting, prayer is invalid unless he intends residence when standing for the third rakʿah.
The distinction between intentional and forgetful omission leads to sajdah al-sahw.
5
Understand the end of qasr
Travel established (mustaḥkam) after three days ends only by entering hometown or intending residence for half a month. Before three days, mere return ends it.
This determines when qasr no longer applies.

(والقصر عزيمة عندنا))، لما قدمناه (۳)، (فإذا أتم الرباعيَّة، و( الحال أنه (قعدَ القُعود الأوّل) قدر التشهد (صحت صلاته) لوجود الفرض في محله، وهو الجلوس على الركعتين، وتصير الأخريان نافلة لـه (مع الكراهة) لتأخير الواجب، وهو : السلام، عن محله إن كان متعمداً، وإن كان ساهياً يسجد للسهو، (وإلأ ) [ أي: وإن لم يكن قد جلس قدر التشهد على رأس الركعتين الأوليتين ) ( فلا تصح صلاته؛ لتركه فرض الجلوس في محله واختلاط الفرض بالنفل قبل كماله ) إلا إذا نوى الإقامة لما قام للثالثة) في محل تصح الإقامة فيه، لأنه صار مقيماً بالنية، فانقلب فرضه أربعاً، وترك القعدة في الأوليـيـن غـيـر مفسد في حقه، وعلى هذا لو ترك القراءة في إحدى الأوليين، ثم نوى الإقامة صح فرضه؛ لأنه أمكنه أن يقرأ في الأخريين)، كما في ( التبيين»، (ولا يزالُ) المسافر الذي استحكم سفره بمضي ثلاثة أيــام مسافراً (يقصر حتى يدخل مِصْرَه)، يعني: بلدة بها وطنه الأصلي (أو ينوي إقامته نصف شهر ببلد، أو قرية)، وأما إذا لم يسر ثلاثة أيام، فلا يشترط أن تكون إقامته في بلد أو قريــة؛ لعدم استحكام السفر، كما يتم بمجرد الرجوع إلى وطنه، وإن لم يدخله؛ لأنه نقض للسفر قبل الاستحكام، وهـو يحتمل النقض لأنه ترك، بخلاف السفر، فإنه لا يكون مسافراً بمجرد نيته؛ لأنه فعل ولابد من (1) لما روى يعلى بن أمية، قال: قلت لعمر بن الخطاب عَلَيْكُمْ جُنَاحٌ أنْ تَقْصُرُوا مِنَ الصَّلَاةِ إِنْ خِفْتُمْ أنْ يَفْتِنَكُمُ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا ) [ النساء: ۱۰۱ ] ، فقد أمر الناس فقال: عجبت مما عجبت منه. فسألت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن ذلك فقال: «صدقة تصدق الله بها عليكم فاقبلوا صدقته»، أخرجه مسلم في صلاة المسافرين، باب: صلاة المسافرين وقصرها (١٥٧١). (۳) ص (٤٣٦). (٤) صورة هذه المسألة: أن المسافر لو قرأ في ركعة واحدة في فرض ذات أربع فإن سلم على رأس الركعتين تفسد وإن لم يسلم وقام إلى الثالثة ونوى الإقامة قبل التقييد بسجدة لا تفسد. ش.
(And qasr is a resolution (ʿazīmah) according to us, as we have previously mentioned. So if he completes the four-rakʿah prayer, and he sat the first sitting to the extent of the tashahhud, his prayer is valid because the obligation (farḍ) occurred in its place, which is sitting after two rakʿahs, and the last two become voluntary (nafl) for him, but with dislike (karāhah) due to delaying the obligatory (wājib), which is the salām, from its place, if he did so intentionally; if he was forgetful, he performs prostration of forgetfulness (sajdah al-sahw). Otherwise, if he did not sit to the extent of the tashahhud at the end of the first two rakʿahs, his prayer is invalid due to abandoning the obligation of sitting in its place and mixing the obligatory with the voluntary before its completion, except if he intends residence when standing for the third rakʿah in a place where the intention of residence is valid, because he becomes a resident by intention, so his obligation becomes four, and leaving the sitting in the first two is not invalidating for him. And similarly, if he left the recitation in one of the first two, then intended residence, his obligation is valid because he can recite in the last two, as in al-Tabyīn. And the traveler whose travel is established by the passage of three days continues to shorten until he enters his hometown (miṣruhu), meaning the town of his original homeland, or intends residence for half a month in a city or village. If he has not traveled three days, it is not required that his residence be in a city or village due to the lack of establishment of travel, just as it is completed by mere return to his homeland even if he does not enter it, because he has nullified the travel before establishment, and it is susceptible to nullification because it is a leaving, unlike travel, for one does not become a traveler merely by intention, because it is an action and must (be actual). The hadith: Yaʿlā ibn Umayyah reported: I said to ʿUmar ibn al-Khaṭṭāb: 'There is no sin on you if you shorten the prayer if you fear that those who disbelieve may harm you' [Quran 4:101], and he commanded the people, and said: I wondered as you wondered, so I asked the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) about that, and he said: 'It is a charity that Allah has given to you, so accept His charity.' Reported by Muslim in the Book of the Traveler's Prayer (1571).
Source pages p. 442

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof (ruling_with_proof) that addresses several key points: (1) Qasr (shortening prayer) is a resolution (ʿazīmah) in the Hanafi school, meaning it is the original ruling for travel and not a concession (rukhṣah) that can be neglected. (2) If a traveler completes four rakʿahs and sits for the first tashahhud, his prayer is valid but disliked (makrūh) because he intentionally delayed the obligatory (wājib) of salām; if forgetful, he performs sajdah al-sahw. (3) If he did not sit for tashahhud in the first two rakʿahs, the prayer is invalid because the farḍ of sitting was omitted and the farḍ and nafl became mixed. However, if he intends residence (iqāmah) when standing for the third rakʿah, then his obligation becomes four rakʿahs, so the omission of sitting in the first two does not invalidate. (4) The traveler continues to shorten until he enters his hometown or intends to stay half a month in a place; if he has not traveled three days, returning to his homeland ends the travel concession even without entering the town, because the travel was not yet established (mustaḥkam). The proof for qasr being a resolution is the hadith of Yaʿlā ibn Umayyah in which the Prophet (peace be upon him) called it a charity from Allah, indicating that it is a favor to be accepted, not a concession that can be rejected.

Key Terms
العزيمة (al-ʿazīmah): The original, unrelaxed legal ruling; opposed to rukhsah (concession). Here, qasr is said to be ʿazīmah, meaning it is the prescribed prayer length for a traveler.
الكراهة (al-karāhah): Dislike, a legal category between permissible and forbidden; here, completing four rak'ahs intentionally while shortening is disliked.
الاستحكام (al-istiḥkām): Establishment; here, travel is 'established' after three days, meaning it cannot be easily nullified by return.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if a traveler completes four rak'ahs and does not sit for the first tashahhud?
A) The prayer is valid and complete.
B) The prayer is valid but disliked.
C) The prayer is invalid unless he intended residence when standing for the third rak'ah.
D) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated regardless.

Key Takeaway
Qasr is a binding resolution (ʿazīmah); completing four rakʿahs while traveling requires sitting after two for validity, and going beyond three days travel establishes the concession until a valid residence intention or return.
